Sects and Disagreements

5 min
Early Proofs of Abu Bakr's Merit
Baqillani lists the earliest proofs of Abu Bakr's merit.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first set of proofs that Imam al-Baqillani presents to establish Abu Bakr's qualification for the caliphate, including his precedence in faith, his role in the cave, and his defense of the Prophet.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr's caliphate is justified by divine favor and personal sacrifice, not politics.

Imam al-Baqillani begins by addressing an objection: what proof is there that Abu Bakr was truly fit for leadership? His answer is not a single argument but a cascade of evidence spanning the Prophet’s lifetime. In this first part, we examine the earliest and most personal proofs: his immediate faith, his spending, his companionship in the cave, and his fierce loyalty against the polytheists.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the opening question: someone asks for proof of Abu Bakr's suitability. This sets the stage for the answer that follows.
The objection is a common rhetorical device in kalam.
2
Read the first group of proofs
The author lists several proofs: precedence in faith, jihad, spending, the cave, bringing many converts through his invitation, building a mosque, and buying freed slaves.
Notice the variety: actions, words, and sacrifices.
3
Examine the Suhayl incident
Abu Bakr's harsh rebuke to Suhayl ibn 'Amr shows his unwavering defense of the Prophet.
This incident highlights Abu Bakr's courage.
4
Reflect on the pattern
Each proof demonstrates Abu Bakr's unique closeness to the Prophet and his extraordinary sacrifices for Islam.
This cumulative argument aims to silence doubters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال قائل : وما الدليل على أن أبا بكر كان بصفة ما ذكرتم من صلاحه لإمامة المسلمين واجتماع خلال الأئمة وآلتهم فيه؟ قيل له : الدليل على ذلك سبقه إلى الإيمان والجهاد في سبيل الله بماله ونفسه وإنفاقه على الرسول ماله وإيناسه له في الغار بنفسه وتعاظم انتفاع النبي صلّى الله عليه وسلم بدعوة من دعاة إلى الإيمان وإسلام من أسلم باستدعائه وبنائه مسجداً يدعو فيه إلى الإيمان وتصديق الرسول حتى قال الناس: من آمن بدعاء أبي بكر أكثر ممن آمن بالسيف؛ فمنهم عثمان وطلحة والزبير وغيرهم من علية الصحابة رضي الله عنهم، وإنما أرادوا أكثر قوة ومُنْةٌ لا أكثر عدداً ممن آمن بالسيف وشراؤه المعذبين في الله كبلال وعامر بن فهيرة (٢) ومناضلته المشركين وقوله لمثل سهيل بن عمرو (۳) لما جاء مصالحاً عن قريش حيث قال للنبي صلى الله وسلم ما أرى حولك إلا من لو عضه الحديد أو قربت الخيل لأسلمك ، فقال له : اسكت ; عضضت ببظر السلات ! أنحن نُسلمه ؟ ) ، وكونه مع النبي صلّى الله عليه وسلم يوم بدر في العريش وتخصصه له مع العلم بأنه لا يركن في مثل تلك الحال إلا إلى ذِي مُنْةٍ ورأي وبصيرة وغناء وقد دلّ على هذا بقوله للأعرابي حيث قال له: «إنك ضنين بصاحبك هذا، وقد استحر القتل في أصحابك»، فقال له : إن الله أمرني أن اتخذه خليلاً أو جليساً أو أنيساً) (۱) وما هذا معناه من اللفظ، هذا مع علمنا ضرورة بأنه كان معظماً في الجاهلية قبل الإسلام ومن أهل الثروة والجاه منهم وممن تجتمع إليه العرب وتسأله عن أيام الناس والأنساب والأخبار ففارق ذلك أجمع إلى الذلّ والصَّغَارِ والصبر على أذية أهل الكفر وعلمنا ضرورة بأن النبي صلّى الله عليه وسلم كان يعظمه ويشاوره ويخلي له مجلساً عن يمينه لا يجلس فيه غيره. ومما رُوي من الجهات المشهورة مما قاله عليه السلام فيه نحو قوله : «اقتدوا
If someone says: 'What is the proof that Abu Bakr was of the description you mentioned of his suitability for the imamah of the Muslims and the gathering of the qualities of the imams and their instruments in him?' It is said to him: The proof of that is his precedence in faith and jihad in the path of Allah with his wealth and himself, and his spending his wealth on the Messenger, and his giving him comfort in the cave with himself, and the great benefit the Prophet (peace be upon him) derived from his invitation to faith and the Islam of those who became Muslim through his summons, and his building a mosque in which he invited to faith and belief in the Messenger until people said: 'Those who believed through the invitation of Abu Bakr are more than those who believed by the sword'; among them were 'Uthman, Talha, al-Zubayr and others from the eminent Companions (may Allah be pleased with them), and they only meant more in strength and ability, not more in number than those who believed by the sword; and his buying the tortured ones for Allah like Bilal and 'Amir ibn Fuhayra; and his struggle against the polytheists and his saying to someone like Suhayl ibn 'Amr when he came to make peace from Quraysh, when he said to the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'I see around you none but if iron bit him or horses approached he would hand you over,' so he said to him: 'Be silent! You bit the clitoris of the palm-pith? Are we to hand him over?' And his being with the Prophet on the day of Badr in the shelter, and his distinction with him, with the knowledge that one does not rely in such a situation except upon one of ability, opinion, insight, and sufficiency; and the Prophet indicated this by his saying to the Bedouin when he said to him: 'You are stingy with your companion, and death has become widespread among your companions,' so he said: 'Allah has commanded me to take him as a friend (khalīl) or a companion or an intimate'; and this meaning of the wording; this with our necessary knowledge that he was honored in the Jahiliyya before Islam, among those of wealth and status, and those whom the Arabs would gather around and ask about the days of the people, genealogies, and reports, and he abandoned all that to humiliation, lowliness, and patience on the harm of the people of disbelief; and our necessary knowledge that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to honor him, consult him, and leave for him a seat on his right in which no one else sat; and from what has been narrated from famous authorities of what he (peace be upon him) said about him, such as his saying: 'Follow'.
Source pages p. 487

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer unit. The questioner asks for the proof that Abu Bakr was fit for the imamah as claimed. The answer provides an extensive list of proofs, each demonstrating his superiority. The author follows a cumulative argument: 
1. Precedence in faith and jihad with wealth and self.
2. Spending his wealth on the Messenger.
3. Accompanying the Prophet in the cave (al-ghār).
4. His invitation brought many to Islam, even more than those who converted by the sword – including eminent Companions like 'Uthman, Talha, al-Zubayr (referring to strength, not just numbers).
5. Buying and freeing slaves tortured for their faith, like Bilal and 'Amir ibn Fuhayra.
6. His verbal confrontation with Suhayl ibn 'Amr when Suhayl suggested the Prophet would be abandoned – Abu Bakr fiercely rebuked him.
7. He was with the Prophet in the shelter (al-‘arīsh) at Badr, showing the Prophet's special reliance on him.
8. The Prophet's reply to a Bedouin who accused Abu Bakr of being stingy with the Prophet: 'Allah commanded me to take him as a friend (khalīl) or companion or intimate' – indicating closeness.
9. Abu Bakr's high status in pre-Islamic times (Jahiliyya) – wealthy, consulted, knowledgeable – which he abandoned for the sake of Islam, enduring humiliation and harm from polytheists.
10. The Prophet's consistent honor, consultation, and giving him a special seat to his right.
11. The famous hadith 'Follow the two after me' (unfinished in this passage).
These proofs collectively establish Abu Bakr's qualifications for the imamah, answering the objection comprehensively.

Key Terms
إمامة
الغار
الجهاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that Abu Bakr's caliphate was based solely on political expediency or tribal allegiance.
Correction: Baqillani shows that Abu Bakr's merits were personal and spiritual, demonstrated by his sacrifices and closeness to the Prophet long before the caliphate.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT mentioned as a proof of Abu Bakr's merit in this part of the passage?
A) His precedence in faith
B) His building of a mosque for da'wah
C) His participation in the Battle of Badr
D) His buying of slaves like Bilal

Key Takeaway
Abu Bakr's early sacrifices and unwavering support for the Prophet establish his unique qualification for the caliphate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were in Abu Bakr's position in the cave, knowing the enemy was a step away, would you have been able to console the Prophet with calmness and trust? What would have been your first thought? Commit to strengthening your tawakkul so that you too can be a source of comfort for others in times of fear.
?
Abu Bakr spent his entire wealth on the cause of Islam and bought slaves to free them from torture. Look at your own bank account: what percentage of your wealth has gone to supporting the deen? What is one financial sacrifice you can make this week that will hurt—because real love of the Prophet demands it?
?
When Suhayl ibn 'Amr suggested the Prophet would be abandoned, Abu Bakr rebuked him harshly. Do you defend the honor of the Prophet and the Companions when they are attacked in discussions, or do you stay silent to avoid awkwardness? Write down the name of one person you will correct with firmness the next time you hear a disrespectful remark.

Later Proofs and the Prophet's Special Treatment
Baqillani presents further proofs from Badr, the Bedouin story, and the Prophet's honors.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the later proofs of Abu Bakr's merit, including his presence at Badr, the Prophet's reliance on him, his noble pre-Islamic background, and the Prophet's explicit honor toward him.

Core Idea
The Prophet's unique reliance on Abu Bakr confirms his superiority over all other Companions.

After listing the earlier proofs, Baqillani continues with further evidence from the Battle of Badr, the Prophet's intimate words about him, and his noble status before Islam. These proofs show that the Prophet honored Abu Bakr in ways he honored no one else, making the claim to the caliphate indisputable.

Guided Path
1
Read the later proofs carefully
This section covers Abu Bakr's presence at Badr in the shelter, the Prophet's reply to the Bedouin, his pre-Islamic status, and the Prophet's special treatment.
Each proof adds a different dimension: military reliance, personal closeness, and social standing.
2
Understand the Bedouin incident
When a Bedouin accused Abu Bakr of being stingy with the Prophet, the Prophet said Allah commanded him to take Abu Bakr as a friend or companion.
This shows an extraordinary divine directive.
3
Consider the pre-Islamic context
Abu Bakr was already a respected and wealthy figure in Jahiliyya, yet he humbled himself for Islam.
His sacrifice was greater because he had much to give up.
4
Note the Prophet's special honors
The Prophet would consult Abu Bakr, give him a seat on his right, and said 'Follow the two after me.'
These honors are unique to Abu Bakr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال قائل : وما الدليل على أن أبا بكر كان بصفة ما ذكرتم من صلاحه لإمامة المسلمين واجتماع خلال الأئمة وآلتهم فيه؟ قيل له : الدليل على ذلك سبقه إلى الإيمان والجهاد في سبيل الله بماله ونفسه وإنفاقه على الرسول ماله وإيناسه له في الغار بنفسه وتعاظم انتفاع النبي صلّى الله عليه وسلم بدعوة من دعاة إلى الإيمان وإسلام من أسلم باستدعائه وبنائه مسجداً يدعو فيه إلى الإيمان وتصديق الرسول حتى قال الناس: من آمن بدعاء أبي بكر أكثر ممن آمن بالسيف؛ فمنهم عثمان وطلحة والزبير وغيرهم من علية الصحابة رضي الله عنهم، وإنما أرادوا أكثر قوة ومُنْةٌ لا أكثر عدداً ممن آمن بالسيف وشراؤه المعذبين في الله كبلال وعامر بن فهيرة (٢) ومناضلته المشركين وقوله لمثل سهيل بن عمرو (۳) لما جاء مصالحاً عن قريش حيث قال للنبي صلى الله وسلم ما أرى حولك إلا من لو عضه الحديد أو قربت الخيل لأسلمك ، فقال له : اسكت ; عضضت ببظر السلات ! أنحن نُسلمه ؟ ) ، وكونه مع النبي صلّى الله عليه وسلم يوم بدر في العريش وتخصصه له مع العلم بأنه لا يركن في مثل تلك الحال إلا إلى ذِي مُنْةٍ ورأي وبصيرة وغناء وقد دلّ على هذا بقوله للأعرابي حيث قال له: «إنك ضنين بصاحبك هذا، وقد استحر القتل في أصحابك»، فقال له : إن الله أمرني أن اتخذه خليلاً أو جليساً أو أنيساً) (۱) وما هذا معناه من اللفظ، هذا مع علمنا ضرورة بأنه كان معظماً في الجاهلية قبل الإسلام ومن أهل الثروة والجاه منهم وممن تجتمع إليه العرب وتسأله عن أيام الناس والأنساب والأخبار ففارق ذلك أجمع إلى الذلّ والصَّغَارِ والصبر على أذية أهل الكفر وعلمنا ضرورة بأن النبي صلّى الله عليه وسلم كان يعظمه ويشاوره ويخلي له مجلساً عن يمينه لا يجلس فيه غيره. ومما رُوي من الجهات المشهورة مما قاله عليه السلام فيه نحو قوله : «اقتدوا
If someone says: 'What is the proof that Abu Bakr was of the description you mentioned of his suitability for the imamah of the Muslims and the gathering of the qualities of the imams and their instruments in him?' Checkpoint
What did the Prophet say to the Bedouin who accused Abu Bakr of being stingy?
A) 'You are wrong; Abu Bakr is generous.'
B) 'Allah has commanded me to take him as a friend or companion.'
C) 'Abu Bakr will be your leader after me.'
D) 'Do not speak ill of my Companions.'

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's unparalleled reliance on Abu Bakr, from the battlefield to personal intimacy, confirms his exclusive qualification for the caliphate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet defended Abu Bakr against a Bedouin's accusation. Is there someone you have misjudged without evidence? Will you seek to correct that and honor them as the Prophet honored Abu Bakr?
?
Abu Bakr left his wealth and status for Islam. What is one comfort or status you cling to that might hinder your devotion to Allah? What concrete step can you take this week to abandon it for His sake?
?
The Prophet gave Abu Bakr a seat to his right that no one else could occupy. Is there a person in your life whom you have not given their due respect or rightful place? What specific action will you take to rectify that today?

The Virtues of Abu Bakr and Umar Are Known by Necessity
The author cites evidence that the merits of Abu Bakr and Umar are necessarily known

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author claims that the virtues of Abu Bakr and Umar are known by necessity and the evidence he provides.

Core Idea
The virtues of the first two caliphs are so well-established they are known necessarily.

This passage defends the high status of Abu Bakr and Umar by citing prophetic statements and historical examples. The author argues that their virtues are so universally recognized that even their opponents acknowledged them. You'll see how he uses this to establish necessary knowledge that cannot be denied.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and then the translation to get the overall flow and arguments.
Notice the compressed style of the Arabic.
2
Identify key evidences
Find the prophetic hadith about Abu Bakr's wealth and the title al-Siddiq, the story of Abu Sufyan calling out their names, and the Prophet's practice of including them as witnesses in treaties.
3
Understand the conclusion
The author concludes that this knowledge is necessary (daruri) and cannot be repelled. Reflect on why he considers this conclusive.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالذين من بعدي أبي بكر وعمر، وإنهما من الدين بمنزلة الرأس من الجسد، و«ما نفعني مال ما نفعني مال أبي بكر»، و«إني بعثت إلى الناس كلهم فقالوا: كذبت وقال أبو بكر صدقت» فسمي لأجل ذلك صديقاً وغلب على اسمه وكنيته واسم أبيه، وإلى غير هذه الأخبار مما قد بسطنا طرفاً من ذكرها في غير هذا الكتاب. وقد كان أهل الكفر يعرفون هذا من أمره ويعرفون تقدمه في الجاهلية ثم في الإسلام وعند النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ولهذا صاح أبو سفيان بأعلى صوته عند تزاحف الصفوف: أين أبو بكر بن أبي قحافة؟ أين عمر بن الخطاب؟ يوم بيوم! في كلام طويل ولم يناد بغيرهما؛ ولهذا كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يقدمه في الشهادة عليه في عهوده وكتب صلحه ويكتب: شهد عبد الله بن أبي قحافة وعمر بن الخطاب وفلان وفلان؛ وهذا مما يعلم ضرورة ولا يمكن دفعه.
By those after me, Abu Bakr and Umar, and they are in the religion like the head from the body, and 'What benefited me wealth did not benefit me the wealth of Abu Bakr,' and 'I was sent to all people, so they said: You have lied, and Abu Bakr said: You have spoken the truth,' so he was named for that the Truthful and it dominated his name, his kunyah, and his father's name, and to other reports of which we have spread a portion in other than this book. And the people of disbelief used to know this about his affair and they knew his precedence in the pre-Islamic period, then in Islam, and with the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, and for this Abu Sufyan shouted at the top of his voice when the ranks moved forward: Where is Abu Bakr ibn Abi Quhafah? Where is Umar ibn al-Khattab? A day for a day! in a lengthy speech, and he did not call out to anyone else; and for this the Prophet used to advance him in testimony over him in his covenants and peace treaties and write: Testified Abdullah ibn Abi Quhafah and Umar ibn al-Khattab and so-and-so and so-and-so; and this is known necessarily and cannot be repelled.
Source pages p. 489

Commentary
This passage is a defense of the virtues of Abu Bakr and Umar. The author first lists several prophetic sayings and actions that indicate their high status: the Prophet's statement about them being like the head to the body, his claim that no wealth benefited him like Abu Bakr's, and his naming him al-Siddiq. The author then argues that these merits are so well known that even the disbelievers knew them, citing Abu Sufyan's call during the battle of Uhud where he specifically named Abu Bakr and Umar. Finally, he concludes that this knowledge is necessary (daruri) and cannot be denied, establishing the certainty of their virtue as a foundational point for the subsequent refutation of Shiite claims.

Key Terms
صديق
علم ضروري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think this is merely a collection of hadith without proof, and that the virtues of Abu Bakr and Umar are not definitively established.
Correction: The author uses these evidences not just as anecdotes but as proofs leading to necessary knowledge (daruri), meaning the virtues are so well-attested that they are undeniable.

Checkpoint
What is the author's main claim about the knowledge of Abu Bakr and Umar's virtues?
A) It is based on weak narrations.
B) It is known necessarily and cannot be denied.
C) It is only known by the Prophet.
D) It is disputed among scholars.

Key Takeaway
The passage establishes that the virtues of Abu Bakr and Umar are known by necessity through multiple lines of evidence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly hold the virtues of Abu Bakr and Umar as necessarily known in your heart, or do you allow doubts to linger despite the overwhelming evidence presented? Examine your conscience: is there any trace of hesitation or reservation, like that of the disbelievers who knew but refused to submit? Confront that hesitation now and ask Allah for certainty.
?
The Prophet placed Abu Bakr and Umar in the highest rank, even before himself in testimony. Do you honor those whom the Prophet honored, not just in words but in the way you speak of them and defend their legacy? When you hear criticisms or doubts about them, are you quick to defend, or do you remain silent? Commit to defending their honor as you would defend your own family.
?
Abu Sufyan, a bitter enemy of Islam, knew the status of Abu Bakr and Umar so well that he called them out by name in battle. What does that say about your own recognition of their status? If even their enemies acknowledged their greatness, how much more should you? Ask yourself: are there areas in your life where you fail to give them the respect they are due—perhaps in your heart, speech, or actions? Repent and resolve to rectify that today.

Refuting the Shiite Claim of Hypocrisy
Baqillani refutes the Shiite claim of Abu Bakr and Umar's hypocrisy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Prophet's actions and statements disprove the Shiite claim that Abu Bakr and Umar were hypocrites practicing dissimulation.

Core Idea
The Prophet's trust in Abu Bakr and Umar refutes any claim of their hypocrisy.

This lesson presents Imam al-Baqillani's refutation of a key Shiite accusation. The passage examines the Prophet's actions during his final illness and his explicit statements, concluding that the claim is logically and historically impossible. You will see how the author uses the Prophet's own words and deeds to dismantle the argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the Shiite claim
Begin by reading the opening lines where the author states the Shiite position. Notice the strong language used to dismiss it.
The phrase 'خرط القتاد' is an Arabic idiom for extreme difficulty.
2
Analyze the Prophet's actions
Identify the specific actions of the Prophet that the author cites: his insistence on Abu Bakr leading the prayer, his firm statement 'God and the Muslims refuse except Abu Bakr', and his warning to his wives.
These actions show the Prophet's confidence in Abu Bakr and Umar.
3
Examine the Prophet's general principles
Look at the general principles the author quotes: 'The best of you are the people' and 'Whoever advances someone while knowing a better person has betrayed God.' These principles contradict the Shiite narrative.
4
Understand the dismissal of counterclaims
Read the final lines where the author dismisses the idea that the Prophet removed Abu Bakr. The argument is that such an event would have been widely known and recorded.
This is a powerful historical argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غير أن الشيعة تزعم أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان ممتحناً به وبعمر على نفاق لهما وتقية منهما وهذه أماني دونها خرط القتاد وذهاب الأنفس حسرات ولولا علم النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بفضل سبقه وهجرته وعلمه لم يأتم به ولم يقدمه عليهم في مرضه ويعظم الأمر في بابه ويقول: يأبى الله ورسوله والمسلمون إلا أبا بكر وقوله لحفصة وعائشة: «إنكن صواحبات يوسف»؛ ولولا شدة تعلق هذا الأمر بأبي بكر وتخصصه بالفضل فيه وخشية الإثم في تقدم غيره لم يقل: إنكن صواحبات يوسف و «يأبى الله والمسلمون إلا أبا بكر». والأمر الذي التمس منه أمر سائغ ليس بإثم في الدين لأن فضل السن فقط وما جرى مجراه لا يوجب التحذير بهذا القول. هذا وهو عليه السلام يقول: «يوم الناس خيرهم» و «أئمتكم شفعاؤكم إلى الله، فانظروا بمن تستشفعون»، ويقول: من تقدم على قوم من المسلمين وهو يرى أن فيهم من هو أفضل منه، فقد خان الله ورسوله والمسلمين. وأما دعوى الشيعة أنه خرج فعزله ودفعه عن موضعه وأنكر تقديمه وأعظمه فمن جنس الترهات والأماني الكاذبة لأن مثل هذا لو كان لعلمناه
But the Shiites claim that the Messenger of God was tested by him (Abu Bakr) and Umar, on account of their hypocrisy and dissimulation from them, and these are wishes beyond which is the piercing of the al-Qatad thorns and the going of souls in regrets. And were it not for the Prophet's knowledge of the virtue of his precedence and his emigration and his knowledge, he would not have entrusted him nor placed him ahead of them in his illness, and he would have magnified the matter in his door and said: God, His Messenger, and the Muslims refuse except Abu Bakr; and his words to Hafsa and Aisha: 'You are the companions of Joseph'; and were it not for the severe attachment of this matter to Abu Bakr and his specialization in virtue and his fear of sin in advancing others, he would not have said: 'You are the companions of Joseph' and 'God and the Muslims refuse except Abu Bakr.' And the matter which he sought from him is a permissible matter, not a sin in the religion, because only the virtue of age and what runs its course does not necessitate warning with this statement. This, while he says: 'The people are the best of them' and 'Your leaders are your intercessors to God, so see whom you seek intercession with,' and he says: 'Whoever advances over a group of Muslims while he sees that among them there is one better than him, has betrayed God, His Messenger, and the Muslims.' And as for the Shiites' claim that he (the Prophet) went out, removed him, pushed him from his position, and denied his advancement and condemned it, it is of the kind of absurdities and false wishes, because if such had been, we would have known it.
Source pages p. 490

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Shiite claim that the Prophet was tested by Abu Bakr and Umar on account of their hypocrisy and dissimulation. The author argues that if the Prophet knew of their hypocrisy, he would not have entrusted them with leadership, especially during his final illness. Instead, he insisted on Abu Bakr despite opposition. The author further cites the Prophet's warning to his wives and his general principle that the best should lead. Finally, he dismisses the claim that the Prophet removed Abu Bakr from his position as absurd, because such an event would have been widely known.

Key Terms
تقية
نفاق
خرط القتاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that the Shiite claim of Abu Bakr and Umar's hypocrisy is plausible based on hidden motives.
Correction: The Prophet's consistent trust and public support for Abu Bakr and Umar, as demonstrated in his actions and statements, disproves any hidden hypocrisy. The claim contradicts established historical facts.

Checkpoint
What is the author's main argument against the Shiite claim of hypocrisy?
A) The Prophet did not have knowledge of the unseen.
B) If they were hypocrites, the Prophet would not have trusted them with leadership.
C) Abu Bakr and Umar repented publicly.
D) The Prophet never spoke about Abu Bakr's virtue.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's actions and statements consistently support Abu Bakr and Umar, refuting any notion of their hypocrisy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you discovered that someone you trusted deeply turned out to be a hypocrite, how would that affect your judgment of everyone they endorsed? Now, consider: the Prophet, the most truthful of all, fully trusted Abu Bakr and Umar. What does that demand of you when you hear accusations against them? Will you allow those whispers to erode your trust in the Prophet's judgment?
?
The Prophet's warning to his wives reveals that even those closest to him could be tested. Have you ever let personal loyalty to a group or leader lead you to spread or believe false accusations about those whom the Prophet honored? How will you actively guard your heart against such bias?
?
This passage makes a stark claim: advancing someone less worthy is a betrayal of God and His Messenger. Think of the people you look up to and follow. Have you ever promoted or defended a view of history that undermines the clear, established Sunnah of the Prophet? What will you do to align your loyalties with the Prophet's own choices, even if it costs you popularity or comfort?

Refutation of the Shia Claim of Testing Abu Bakr and Umar
Baqillani refutes the Shia claim of testing Abu Bakr and Umar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's arguments refuting the Shia claim that the Prophet was testing Abu Bakr and Umar for hypocrisy.

Core Idea
The Prophet's explicit actions and sayings disprove any claim of testing or hypocrisy.

Baqillani directly confronts a Shia claim that casts doubt on the integrity of Abu Bakr and Umar. He argues that the Prophet's own statements and actions during his final illness prove their eminent virtue, and that the idea of 'testing' is logically and theologically untenable. This passage presents a series of arguments drawn from the Prophet's conduct and teachings.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Baqillani begins by asserting the well-known testimony of companions and then dismisses the Shia claim as vain wishes.
Notice the emotional tone: 'wishes beyond which...'
2
Identify Baqillani's main arguments
Look for the distinct lines of reasoning: (1) known by necessity, (2) Prophet's knowledge prevents testing, (3) Prophet's explicit sayings like 'Allah refuses except Abu Bakr', (4) the warning about advancing over a better person.
These arguments build on each other.
3
Reflect on the Prophetic principles
Consider the general principles the Prophet is reported to have said: the best should lead, leaders are intercessors, and advancing oneself over a better person is betrayal. How do these support Baqillani's refutation?
4
Summarize the refutation
Write a brief summary of Baqillani's argument in your own words. Ensure you captured the key points: necessity, knowledge, sayings, and principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شهد عبد الله بن أبي قحافة وعمر بن الخطاب وفلان وفلان؛ وهذا مما يُعلمُ ضرورةً ولا يمكن دفعه . غير أن الشيعة تزعم أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان ممتحناً به وبعمر على نفاق لهما وتقيةٍ منهما وهذه أماني دونها خرط القتاد وذهاب الأنفس حسرات ولولا علم النبي صلّى الله عليه وسلم بفضل سبقه وهجرتـه وعلمه لم يأتم به ولم يقدمه عليهم في مرضه ويعظم الأمر في بابه ويقول : يأبى الله ورسوله والمسلمون إلا أبا بكر وقوله لحفصة وعائشة : «إنكن صواحبات يوسف»؛ ولولا شدة تعلق هذا الأمر بأبي بكر وتخصصه بالفضل فيه وخشية الإثم في تقدم غيره لم يقل: إنكن صواحبات يوسف و «يأبى الله والمسلمون إلا أبا بكر». والأمر الذي التمس منه أمر سائغ ليس بإثم في الدين لأن فضل السن فقط وما جرى مجراه لا يوجب التحذير بهذا القول. هذا وهو عليه السلام يقول: «يوم الناسَ خيرهم» و «أئمتكم شفعاؤكم إلى الله ، فانظروا بمن تستشفعون» ، ويقول : من تقدم على قوم من المسلمين وهو يرى أن فيهم من هو أفضل منه ، فقد خان الله ورسوله والمسلمين .
Abdullah ibn Abi Quhafa and Umar ibn al-Khattab and so-and-so and so-and-so testified; and this is a matter known by necessity and cannot be denied. However, the Shia claim that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, was testing him (Abu Bakr) and Umar because of hypocrisy on their part and dissimulation from them, and these are wishes beyond which the cutting of al-qatad and the departure of souls in regrets. And if it were not for the knowledge of the Prophet, peace be upon him, of the virtue of his precedence and his emigration and his knowledge, he would not have appointed him as imam and not have put him forward over them in his illness, and he magnifies the matter in its chapter and says: 'Allah, His Messenger, and the Muslims refuse except Abu Bakr,' and his saying to Hafsa and Aisha: 'You are the companions of Yusuf.' And if it were not for the intense attachment of this matter to Abu Bakr and his specialization in virtue in it and fear of sin in putting forward another, he would not have said: 'You are the companions of Yusuf' and 'Allah and the Muslims refuse except Abu Bakr.' And the matter for which he was asked is a permissible matter, not a sin in religion, because the virtue of age only and what runs in its course does not necessitate warning with this saying. This, while he, peace be upon him, says: 'The best of you in the day...' and 'Your leaders are your intercessors to Allah, so see whom you ask to intercede,' and he says: 'Whoever puts himself forward over a group of Muslims while he sees that among them is one better than him, has betrayed Allah, His Messenger, and the Muslims.'
Source pages p. 490

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Shia claim that the Prophet was testing Abu Bakr and Umar for hypocrisy. Baqillani first asserts that the testimony of witnesses (Abdullah ibn Abi Quhafa, Umar, etc.) makes the appointment of Abu Bakr as imam a matter known by necessity, not open to denial. He then dismisses the Shia claim as vain wishes. He argues that if the Prophet had known of any deficiency in Abu Bakr or Umar, he would not have appointed Abu Bakr to lead the prayer during his illness. The Prophet's saying 'Allah, His Messenger, and the Muslims refuse except Abu Bakr' and his addressing the wives as 'the companions of Yusuf' demonstrate the Prophet's deep attachment to Abu Bakr. If the reason for appointment had merely been age, the Prophet would not have used such strong language. Finally, the Prophet's general principles (the best should lead, leaders are intercessors, and advancing oneself when a better person exists is betrayal) all support Abu Bakr's superiority.

تقية
الصواحبات
يأبى الله ورسوله والمسلمون إلا أبا بكر
أئمتكم شفعاؤكم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet was testing Abu Bakr and Umar for hidden hypocrisy and dissimulation (taqiyya).
Correction: Baqillani argues that the Prophet's actions and sayings demonstrate his full knowledge of their virtue, making such a test impossible and contradictory to his conduct.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what would have prevented the Prophet from appointing Abu Bakr as imam if he had known any deficiency?
A) The Prophet would have tested him instead.
B) The Prophet would not have appointed him.
C) The Prophet would have appointed someone else.
D) The Prophet would have ignored it.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani refutes the Shia claim of testing by showing that the Prophet's actions and teachings affirm Abu Bakr's virtue and make any notion of hidden hypocrisy impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a claim that casts doubt on the Prophet's companions, do you immediately turn to the Prophet's own words and actions to verify, or do you let suspicion linger in your heart? What does that reveal about your trust in the Prophet's judgment?
?
The Prophet warned that advancing oneself over a better person is betrayal of Allah, His Messenger, and the Muslims. In your own life, are there situations where you have put yourself forward despite knowing someone else is more qualified or virtuous? How can you humble yourself and step back?
?
If you truly believe that the Prophet's explicit statement 'Allah and the Muslims refuse except Abu Bakr' settles the matter, then why do you sometimes entertain doubts about the choices of the early community? Are you willing to surrender your own reasoning to the Prophet's authority completely?

Refuting the Shia Claim about Abu Bakr Leading Prayer
Baqillani refutes the Shia claim about Abu Bakr's removal from prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's refutation of the Shia claim that the Prophet removed Abu Bakr from leading prayer, and why the dispute about one prayer does not affect Abu Bakr's leadership.

Core Idea
The Shia claim is based on nonsense; the only real dispute is a minor detail that does not change the known fact.

Imam Baqillani tackles a Shia argument that attempts to undermine Abu Bakr's role by claiming the Prophet removed him from leading prayer. In this passage, he explains why such a claim is impossible and clarifies the actual historical dispute. Let's follow his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Shia claim
Read the passage and locate the Shia claim that the Prophet removed Abu Bakr from leading prayer, replaced him, and disapproved of his advancement.
Notice how Baqillani characterizes this claim as 'nonsense and false wishes.'
2
Understand the argument from necessary knowledge
Baqillani argues that if such an event occurred, it would be known necessarily (like the fact that Abu Bakr led the prayer). Reflect on why this is a strong refutation.
Necessary knowledge in Islamic scholarship refers to facts that are universally known and cannot be denied.
3
Note the clarification of the dispute
Baqillani states that the only dispute among scholars is about one specific prayer: whether Abu Bakr led the Prophet or the Prophet led Abu Bakr. This does not change the overall fact that Abu Bakr led the prayers.
This is a key point—the Shia claim is about removal, not about a minor detail.
4
Review the hadith and Abu Bakr's statement
Read the hadith about every prophet being led in prayer by a man from his people, and Abu Bakr's own words showing he was put in charge while the Prophet was present.
These sources support Baqillani's refutation.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Baqillani ends by dismissing the Shia reports as rejected fabrications. Think about why he considers them invalid.
The claim is impossible because it contradicts necessary knowledge and reliable narrations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما دعوى الشيعة أنه خرج فعَزّله ودفعه عن موضعه وأنكر تقديمـه وأعظمه فمن جنس الترهات والأماني الكاذبة لأن مثل هذا لو كان لعلمناه ضرورةً كما علمنا أن أبا بكر تقدم ضرورة وإنما اختلف في أن أبا بكر صلّى بالنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أو صلّى به النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم صلاة واحدة ذُكر ذلك فيها وصلّى بهم بقية أيام مرض رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وروى النّبتُ الثقات أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «ما من نبي يموت حتى يؤمه رجل من قومه؛ وأن أبا بكر أم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وهذا هو الذي عناه أبو بكر بقوله : وليتكم ولست بخيركم؛ إني وليتكم الصلاة ورسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم حاضر؛ ولعمري إنه لا يجوز أن يكون خير قوم فيهم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فلا مُعْتَبر في هذا الأمر العظيم بتلفيق المخالفين وتمنيهم الأباطيل وتلقهِم بروايات ترد خاصة منهم ولهم لا يعلمها غيرهم .
As for the claim of the Shia that he (the Prophet) went out and removed him (Abu Bakr) and pushed him from his place and disapproved of his advancement and regarded it as great, it is of the kind of nonsense and false wishes, because if such a thing had happened, we would have known it necessarily, just as we know necessarily that Abu Bakr advanced. Rather, the dispute is only whether Abu Bakr led the Prophet in prayer or the Prophet led him in one prayer, mentioned therein, and he led them for the remaining days of the illness of the Messenger of Allah. And the trustworthy (narrators) reported that the Prophet said: 'There is no prophet who dies until a man from his people leads him in prayer,' and that Abu Bakr led the Messenger of Allah in prayer, and this is what Abu Bakr meant by his saying: 'I have been put in charge of you, and I am not the best of you; indeed I was put in charge of the prayer while the Messenger of Allah was present.' And by my life, it is not permissible that the best of a people be among them while the Messenger of Allah is present, so there is no consideration in this great matter for the fabrications of the opponents and their false wishes and their swallowing of reports that are rejected, especially from them and for them, which no one else knows.
Source pages p. 491

Commentary
This passage refutes the Shia claim that the Prophet actually removed Abu Bakr from leading the prayer. Baqillani says such an event would be known necessarily, just as the fact that Abu Bakr led the prayer is known necessarily. He then clarifies that the only dispute among scholars is about one specific prayer: whether Abu Bakr led the Prophet in that particular prayer or the Prophet led Abu Bakr. This does not affect the general fact that Abu Bakr led the prayers during the Prophet's illness. He cites a hadith that every prophet is led in prayer by a man from his people before dying, and that Abu Bakr led the Prophet. He also quotes Abu Bakr's own words, showing that he acknowledged he was not the best but was put in charge of prayer while the Prophet was present. Baqillani concludes that it is impossible for someone to be considered the best of his people while the Prophet is among them, so the Shia reports are rejected fabrications.

ما من نبي يموت حتى يؤمه رجل من قومه
وليتكم الصلاة ورسول الله حاضر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The dispute about who led whom in one prayer means the leadership of Abu Bakr is uncertain.
Correction: Baqillani shows the dispute is only about a single prayer and does not affect the established fact that Abu Bakr led the prayers during the Prophet's illness.

Checkpoint
What does Baqillani identify as the only dispute regarding the prayer incident?
A) Whether Abu Bakr led the Prophet in one specific prayer or the Prophet led him.
B) Whether the Prophet removed Abu Bakr permanently.
C) Whether Abu Bakr was qualified to lead.
D) Whether the Prophet prayed behind Abu Bakr at all.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani refutes the Shia claim by arguing that the only dispute about the prayer is a minor detail that does not affect the established leadership of Abu Bakr.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are there beliefs you hold about Islam that you have accepted simply because they are popular or come from a particular group, without checking them against the necessary knowledge of the Quran and Sunnah? How can you cultivate the courage to call such claims 'nonsense' if they conflict with established truths?
?
Baqillani dismisses the Shia claim as 'false wishes' (أماني كاذبة). What false wishes or desires have you entertained in your own faith—perhaps wanting a beloved practice to be correct despite clear evidence otherwise? Will you submit to the truth even when it contradicts your wishes?
?
The only dispute in the authentic narrations is a minor detail that does not shake the overall certainty of Abu Bakr's leadership. In your own life, do you allow small disagreements or uncertainties to undermine your confidence in the clear teachings of the Prophet? What step can you take today to anchor your faith firmly in the necessary knowledge of Islam?

Abu Bakr's Post-Prophet Virtues as Proof of Imamate
Baqillani argues that Abu Bakr's actions after the Prophet's death demonstrate his imamate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses Abu Bakr's actions after the Prophet's death as an independent proof for his imamate, even if prior virtues were unknown.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr's actions after the Prophet's death are sufficient proof of his imamate.

In this passage, Baqillani argues that even if we set aside all of Abu Bakr's earlier virtues, his conduct after the Prophet's death provides clear evidence of his leadership and worthiness for the caliphate. He emphasizes Abu Bakr's decisive actions, such as informing the people of the Prophet's death and restraining those who were in shock, as the first manifestation of his sound judgment.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without heavy analysis, then read the English translation to get the main argument.
Notice how Baqillani builds his case from general to specific.
2
Identify the key virtues after the Prophet's death
Look for the list of virtues Baqillani mentions: knowledge, virtue, severity, attaining what others missed, strengthening, repairing the breach, suppressing apostasy.
3
Focus on the first example
Baqillani gives the first example: Abu Bakr informing people of the Prophet's death and restraining Umar. Understand why this is significant.
This shows his leadership and calmness in crisis.
4
Reflect on the argument's role
Consider how this argument supports the imamate of Abu Bakr even without explicit textual proof.
It emphasizes practical leadership as evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا على أنه لو يعلم جميع من حاله، ولم يتقدم له شيء ء مما ذكرناه من فضائله ومناقبه لكان ما ظهر منه بعد موت النبي صلّى الله عليه وسلم من العلم والفضل والشدة في القول والفعل وتحصيل ما ذهب على غيــره دلالة على اجتماع خلال الفضل والإمامة فيه بل لو لم يدلّ على ذلك من أمره إلا ما ظهر منه من التثقيف والتقدم والتشدد وسد الخلل وقمع الرّدة وأهلها في أيام نظره لكان في ذلك مقنع لمن وُفِّقَ لرشده . فأول ما ظهر من فضله وتسديد رأيه إعلام الناس موت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وكفَّه عمر وغيره ممن تشتتت آراؤهم في موته وفجأتهم أمته
This, even if all of his situation were known, and nothing of what we mentioned of his virtues and merits had preceded him, what appeared from him after the death of the Prophet, peace be upon him, of knowledge, virtue, severity in word and deed, and attainment of what others missed, would be a proof of the gathering of the qualities of virtue and imamate in him. Rather, if nothing from his matter indicated that except what appeared from him of strengthening, advancement, rigor, repairing the breach, and suppressing apostasy and its people in the days of his rule, that would be sufficient for one who is guided to his rational sense. So the first thing that appeared from his virtue and sound opinion was informing the people of the death of the Messenger of Allah and his restraining Umar and others whose opinions were scattered about his death, and his nation was taken by surprise by it.
Source pages p. 491

Commentary
This passage argues that even if the earlier proofs of Abu Bakr's virtues (like precedence in Islam and emigration) were not known, his actions after the Prophet's death are sufficient evidence for his imamate. Baqillani lists his knowledge, virtue, severity in word and deed, and attainment of what others missed. He then specifies that even if only his actions of strengthening, advancement, rigor, repairing the breach, and suppressing apostasy during his caliphate were considered, they would be convincing for the rational person. He gives the first example: Abu Bakr's decisive act of informing the people of the Prophet's death and restraining Umar (who was in disbelief and denial) and others whose opinions were scattered. This shows his leadership and sound judgment.

تحصيل ما ذهب على غيره
سد الخلل
قمع الردة
تثقيف
تسديد رأيه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Abu Bakr's imamate relies solely on explicit textual evidence.
Correction: Baqillani shows his practical leadership after the Prophet's death is also an independent proof.

Checkpoint
What is the first example Baqillani gives of Abu Bakr's virtue after the Prophet's death?
A) His suppression of apostasy.
B) His informing people of the Prophet's death and restraining Umar.
C) His appointment of governors.
D) His compilation of the Quran.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani proves that Abu Bakr's decisive actions after the Prophet's death are a clear sign of his imamate, independent of earlier merits.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When was the last time you, like Umar, were overcome by confusion or shock in a critical moment, and who stepped in to guide you? How does Abu Bakr's decisive action challenge you to be that person for others, even when it costs you your comfort?
?
Abu Bakr's post-Prophet actions are described as 'strengthening, advancement, rigor, repairing the breach, and suppressing apostasy.' Examine your own role in your family or community. Which of these qualities are you lacking, and what concrete step will you take this week to embody it?
?
If the only evidence of your faith and leadership were your actions in the past year—with no mention of your past achievements—would those actions prove you worthy of trust? Why or why not? What needs to change?

Abu Bakr's Merits and His Right to the Imamate
Baqillani enumerates Abu Bakr's merits proving his worthiness for imamate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key merits of Abu Bakr that Baqillani presents to prove his worthiness for the imamate, and how these merits collectively establish his right to leadership.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr's unparalleled qualifications make him the rightful imam.

Imam Baqillani, in his defence of Abu Bakr's caliphate, presents a concise list of merits that demonstrate his suitability for leadership. This passage serves as a direct response to those who question Abu Bakr's right to the imamate, grounding his authority in concrete actions and qualities. As you read, notice how each merit builds a case for his unmatched excellence.

Guided Path
1
Read the rhetorical opening
The passage begins with a rhetorical question that sets the tone. Understand that Baqillani is presenting this as an obvious conclusion from the following merits.
The question 'So how can one with these qualities not be suitable?' implies that the merits are undeniable.
2
Identify the enumerated merits
List each merit mentioned: knowledge, compilation of Quran, consistency in rulings, succession to the Prophet, bequest to Umar, sound opinion, and alerting people to his insight.
Some merits are grouped; try to separate them clearly.
3
Connect merits to conclusion
Notice how the passage ends by stating that through these descriptions and traits, Abu Bakr becomes suitable and deserving of the imamate. This is the logical conclusion of the enumeration.
4
Reflect on the argumentative structure
Consider how Baqillani uses this list to counter any doubt about Abu Bakr's right to leadership. The argument is cumulative: each merit adds weight.
This is a typical kalam method of establishing a point through evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فكيف لا يصلح من هذه صفته لإمامة الأمة؟ هذا علمه مع ما ظهر من وانتدابه لجمع القرآن وأنه لم يتلعثم في حكم نزل في أيام نظره ولا رجع عنه وقد جلس مجلس النبي وخلفه في أمته وإن ذلك لأمر عظيم ثم ما كان من عهده إلى عمر عند موته وتسديده في رأيه وتنبيهه القوم على فضل رأيه ومكان نظره ما عمر بسبيله وما هو مخصوص به مما سنذكر طرفاً منه في باب إمامته. وببعض هذه الأوصاف والخلال وتسديد التدبير والرأي والمقال يصلح ويستحق الإمامة.
So how can one with these qualities not be suitable for the imamate of the nation? This is his knowledge along with what appeared from his appointing him to collect the Qur'an, and that he did not hesitate in a ruling that came down during his tenure nor recanted from it, and he sat in the seat of the Prophet and succeeded him over his community, and indeed that is a great matter. Then what came from his bequest to 'Umar at his death, and his soundness in his opinion, and his alerting the people to the merit of his opinion and the status of his insight, what 'Umar was able to do through him and what he was specifically distinguished by, a part of which we will mention in the chapter on his imamate. And through some of these descriptions, traits, soundness of management, opinion, and speech, he becomes suitable and deserving of the imamate.
Source pages p. 495

Commentary
This passage begins with a rhetorical question and then enumerates Abu Bakr's merits that qualify him for the imamate. The author lists: his knowledge, his role in compiling the Quran, his consistency in judgments, his succession to the Prophet, his appointment of Umar, and his sound judgment. The conclusion is that these qualities collectively make him suitable and deserving of the imamate. The passage follows the author's argumentative order, moving from the question to the evidence.

Correction: Baqillani shows that concrete actions and qualities—such as knowledge, judgment, and service to the community—are valid and strong grounds for the imamate.

Reply to the Objection on Abu Bakr's Admission of Fallibility
Baqillani answers the objection that Abu Bakr admitted lack of infallibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani defends the legitimacy of Abu Bakr's caliphate by refuting the objection that an imam must be infallible.

Core Idea
Infallibility is not required for an imam; Abu Bakr's humility proves his merit.

This passage tackles a critical objection against the first caliph's succession. Opponents argued that Abu Bakr's own words admitting fallibility disqualify him from leadership because imams should be infallible. Baqillani responds by redefining the requirements of leadership and turning the objection into evidence of virtue.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation. Pay attention to the structure: objection, then response.
Notice the author's use of 'قيل لهم' to signal the answer.
2
Identify the two parts of the response
The author gives two distinct arguments: (1) infallibility is not a necessary condition for the imam, (2) Abu Bakr's words actually demonstrate his merit.
The first argument is based on analogy with other officials.
3
Reflect on how the author uses Abu Bakr's words
Instead of denying the statement, the author reinterprets it as a sign of trustworthiness and fear of Allah, making it a virtue.
This is a key rhetorical move.
4
Connect to the broader Sunni position
Understand that Sunni theology holds that the imam is not considered infallible in the same sense as prophets; his role is administrative and judicial.
This distinction is important for the whole debate on successorship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا : وكيف يكون أبو بكر مستحقاً لهذا الأمر مع اعترافه بأنه ممن يميل ويضل ويزل وأنه غير معصوم، حيث يقول: ألا وإني أكثركم شغلاً وأثقلكم حملاً؛ فإن استقمت فاتبعوني، وإن ملت فقوموني أطيعوني ما أطعت الله فيكم وإذا عصيت الله فلا طاعة لي عليكم؛ ومن سبيل الإمام أن يكون معصوماً؟ قيل لهم: هذا غلط لما قد بيناه في صدر هذا الكتاب من أنه لا يجب أن يكون الإمام معصوماً كما لا يجب عصمة أمرائه وقضاته وعماله وأصحاب جيوشه ومسائله إذ كانوا يلون من ذلك ما يليه بنفسه وقد أوضحنا هذا بما نستغني عن رده. وهذا الكلام الذي قاله من أدل الأمور على فضله وأداء الأمانة فيما تحمل والخوف من التقصير فيه؛ وهو ادعى الأمور إلى الرضى به والاجتماع على طاعته.
If they say: How is Abu Bakr deserving of this authority while he admits that he is one who inclines, goes astray, and slips, and that he is not infallible, when he says: 'Indeed I am the busiest of you and the heaviest in burden; if I am upright, follow me, and if I deviate, correct me. Obey me as long as I obey Allah in you, and if I disobey Allah, there is no obedience to me upon you.' And the way of the imam is that he be infallible? Say to them: This is an error due to what we have explained in the beginning of this book: that it is not necessary for the imam to be infallible, just as it is not necessary for his governors, judges, officials, army commanders, and questioners to be infallible, since they undertake the same tasks that he undertakes himself, and we have clarified this sufficiently so that we need not repeat it. And this speech that he said is among the most indicative things of his merit, fulfillment of trust regarding what he undertook, and fear of falling short in it; and it is the most conducive thing to being satisfied with him and uniting upon his obedience.
Source pages p. 496

Commentary
This passage is an objection and its answer. The objectors argue that an imam must be infallible, citing Abu Bakr's own admission that he might err. The author replies that infallibility is not a requirement for the imam, as argued earlier in the book. He supports this by noting that other officials also are not infallible. Furthermore, Abu Bakr's admission itself demonstrates his merit, honesty, and sense of responsibility, which actually strengthens his claim to leadership.

Key Terms
عصمة
إمام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: An imam must be infallible to be legitimate.
Correction: Baqillani argues that infallibility is not a prerequisite; other officials also are not infallible, and the imam's role does not require it. Moreover, Abu Bakr's admission of fallibility actually enhances his credibility.

Checkpoint
How does the author respond to the objection that Abu Bakr admitted lack of infallibility?
A) He says Abu Bakr was actually infallible.
B) He says infallibility is not required for an imam.
C) He denies Abu Bakr said that.
D) He ignores the objection.

Key Takeaway
Abu Bakr's admission of fallibility does not disqualify him from leadership; it actually demonstrates his trustworthiness and merits obedience.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Baqillani says Abu Bakr's admission is ‘the most conducive thing to being satisfied with him’. How does your own honesty about your weaknesses—or lack of it—affect how others trust and follow you? What step will you take this week to be more transparent about your need for correction?

Baqillani records the beginning of an objection based on Abu Bakr's own words.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the sectarian objection that Abu Bakr's admission of having a devil undermined his qualification for leadership, and why this objection was taken seriously in theological debates.

Core Idea
Even admitting a devil could be used to challenge a caliph's authority.

The opponents of Abu Bakr's caliphate seized on a remark from his sermon where he acknowledged having a devil that occasionally afflicts him. They argued this imperfection disqualified him from leadership. In this passage, Baqillani presents their objection before refuting it.

Guided Path
1

The sentence is cut off; the full objection likely continued.
2

The objection uses Abu Bakr's own words against him: admission of a devil is taken as evidence of moral imperfection, which should disqualify him from being caliph.
3
Reflect on the context
Consider that this objection was part of broader debates about the qualifications of the early caliphs. Why would such an admission be considered damaging?
The answer from Baqillani is not included in this passage.

Refuting the Devil Objection Against Abu Bakr
Refutation of objection that Abu Bakr's devil shows unfitness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the objection based on Abu Bakr's mention of a devil is refuted by showing it refers to ordinary whispering, not possession.

Core Idea
Having a devil does not mean insanity; it means being human.

The objectors point to Abu Bakr's admission of a devil as proof of unfitness for leadership. In this passage, the author refutes this by explaining the metaphorical nature of the statement and citing the Prophet's own words to show that all humans have a devil. This lesson clarifies the distinction between demonic influence and normal whispering.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and refutation
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the objection is presented and then immediately countered.
The refutation uses both rational and scriptural arguments.
2
Analyze the rational argument
Identify the author's claim that no rational person would consider Abu Bakr mad, and that the Companions would not have accepted him if he were.
This is a logical argument based on consensus (ijma).
3
Understand the prophetic analogy
Examine the hadith about everyone having a devil, including the Prophet. Notice how it supports the metaphorical interpretation.
The Prophet's devil submitted through divine help, not removal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا : فكيف يستحق أبو بكر هذا الأمر وهو يعترف بأن له شيطاناً يعتريه حيث يقول في هذه الخطبة: ألا وإنَّ لي شيطاناً يعتريني فإذا رأيتم ذلك فلا تقربوني لا أُوَشِّرُ في أشعاركم وأَبْشَارِكم» (۱)؛ وأقل أحوال الإمام أن يكون عاقلاً سليماً من عوارض الشيطان؟ يقال لهم : ليس على وجه ذو عقل يرى أن أبا بكر كان مجنوناً ومعترفاً في هذا القول بالصرع والغلبة ولو كان على هذه الحال لما خفي أمره على الصحابة ولا تركوا بأسرهم دفعه هذا الأمر والاحتجاج بأنه مجنون محتاج إلى العلاج دون الإمامة والمناظرة فيها وإقامة الحِجَاج وهذا جهل ممن بلغ إليه كفينا مؤونة كلامه وإنما قال ذلك أبو بكر مُخبِراً بأن الشيطان يوسوس له ويلقي إليه كما يوسوس في صدور جميع الخلق وأنه ليس بمباين لهم في هذا الباب ليتقوا وقت غضبه ووسوسته. وهذا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول: «ما من أحد إلا وله شيطان»، قالوا : ولا أنت يا رسول الله؟ قال: ولا أنا؛ إلا أن الله قد أعانني عليـه فاسْلَمَ) (۲) ، أفتَرى أن رسول الله صلّى الله عليه وسلم أخبر في هذا القول عن جنونه حاشاه من ذلك وجنون سائر الصحابة؟ إن هذا لجهل عظيم واقتحام طريف .
If they say: How does Abu Bakr deserve this matter while he admits that he has a devil that afflicts him, where he says in this sermon: 'Indeed I have a devil that afflicts me, so if you see that, do not approach me; I will not harm your hair and skin' (1); and the least condition of the Imam is that he be rational, free from the effects of the devil? It is said to them: There is no rational person who would think that Abu Bakr was mad and admitting in this statement to epilepsy and overpowering. Had he been in that state, his case would not have been hidden from the Companions, nor would they have all refrained from removing him from this matter and arguing that he was insane and in need of treatment rather than the imamate and debate about it and establishing proofs. This is ignorance from whoever has reached that [opinion]; we are spared the trouble of his speech. Rather, Abu Bakr said that informing that the devil whispers to him and casts to him as he whispers to all creation, and that he is not different from them in this matter, so that they would beware of his anger and his whispering. And the Messenger of Allah (s) said: 'There is no one except that he has a devil.' They said: Not even you, O Messenger of Allah? He said: Not even I; but Allah has helped me against him so he submitted. Do you think that the Messenger of Allah (s) informed in this statement of his madness? Far be it from that! And the madness of the rest of the Companions? This is great ignorance and a strange audacity.
Source pages p. 497

Commentary
This passage presents the second objection and its refutation. The objectors claim Abu Bakr's admission of a devil proves he is not rational. The author argues that no rational person would consider this madness, and the Companions would not have accepted him if he were. Abu Bakr meant the devil's whispering, like all humans, and the Prophet's own words show that having a devil is not madness. Thus, the objection is based on ignorance.

Key Terms
شيطان
وسوسة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A person who speaks of having a devil must be insane or possessed.
Correction: The term 'devil' can refer to the ordinary whispering (waswasa) that all humans experience, as clarified by the Prophet's own statement.

Checkpoint
How does the author refute the claim that Abu Bakr's mention of a devil makes him unfit?
A) By denying the devil exists.
B) By showing the Prophet also had a devil, and it means whispering not possession.
C) By saying Abu Bakr was joking.
D) By saying the objection is from hypocrites.

Key Takeaway
Abu Bakr's mention of a devil is not a sign of madness but an acknowledgment of human whispering, as even the Prophet had a devil under divine control.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you feel a sudden whisper of doubt or anger, do you immediately blame external forces, or do you recognize it as your own shaytan that Allah has allowed as a test? How does this lesson change your reaction to those moments?
?
Abu Bakr openly warned others about his own devil's whispering, yet the Companions still trusted him with leadership. ?
The Prophet ﷺ said every human has a devil, including himself, but Allah helped him overcome it. This lesson shows that even the best of creation had to rely on Allah against whispers. In what area of your life have you stopped asking Allah for this help, assuming you could handle it alone? Will you commit today to a daily du'a for protection against waswasa?

Answering the Objection on Abu Bakr's Statement
Objection and two answers regarding Abu Bakr's statement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Baqillani defends Abu Bakr's statement 'I am not the best of you' from the objection that it implies injustice.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr's 'not the best' was said in specific contexts, not a confession of unworthiness.

The opposition argues that Abu Bakr's own words contradict his caliphate. Imam al-Baqillani presents multiple ways to interpret the statement, showing it was never an admission of general inferiority. Let's examine the objection and the initial answers provided in the text.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Objection
Read the objection carefully: the opponents claim that Abu Bakr's admission of not being the best implies he is unjust for taking leadership.
2
First Answer: Context of the Prophet's Presence
Notice how al-Baqillani explains that Abu Bakr meant he was not the best because the Prophet was present, and that he led prayer during the Prophet's lifetime.
This answer shows humility, not incompetence.
3
Second Answer: Meaning of Tribe
The second possible interpretation is that Abu Bakr referred to not being the best in lineage, not in overall merit.
This addresses potential tribal concerns.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا : فكيف يكون أبو بكر مستحقاً لهذا الأمر وهو يقول في هذه الخطبة: «وَلِيتُكم ولستُ بخيركم»؛ فألا علم بذلك أن الأمر لمن هو خير منه وأنه ظالم في استبداده به؟ قيل لهم في هذا أجوبة كثيرة : فأولها أنه قال ذلك محتجاً على الأنصار وعلى من ظن أنه يتأخر عنه لأنه قد وليهم الصَّلاةَ ورسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم حاضر ولعمري إنه لا يجوز أن يكون خَيْرَ قوم فيهم رسول الله صلّى الله عليه وسلم فكأنه قال: كيف لا أليكم بعد النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وقد وليتكم مع وجوده ولست بخيركم إذ ذلك؟ ومنها أنه يمكن أن يكون أراد بقوله : وليتكم ولست بخيركم أني لست بخيركم قبيلة
If they say: How can Abu Bakr be deserving of this matter while he says in this sermon: 'I have been put in charge of you while I am not the best of you.' Does it not indicate that the matter belongs to someone better than him and that he is unjust in taking it for himself? It is said to them regarding this many answers: The first of them is that he said that arguing against the Ansar and against whoever thought that he would fall behind because he had led them in prayer while the Messenger of Allah was present. By my life, it is not permissible that he be the best of a people in whom the Messenger of Allah is present. So it is as if he said: How can I not be in charge of you after the Prophet while I was in charge of you in his presence and I am not the best of you at that time? And among them is that it is possible that he intended by his saying 'I have been put in charge of you and I am not the best of you' that I am not the best of you in tribe.
Source pages p. 497

Commentary
This passage presents the third objection and the beginning of the answer. The objectors claim that Abu Bakr's statement 'I am not the best of you' suggests he is unjust. The author gives multiple responses. The first: he said this to the Ansar who thought he might be inferior; he meant he was not the best because the Prophet was present. The second: he may have meant he was not the best in lineage. The answer continues beyond the page.

Key Terms
أنصار
قبيلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Abu Bakr's statement 'I am not the best of you' shows he believed he was unfit for leadership.
Correction: The statement is contextualized: either he meant he was not the best due to the Prophet's presence, or he referred to tribal lineage, not overall merit. It does not imply injustice or unfitness.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what was one meaning of Abu Bakr's saying 'I am not the best of you'?
A) He was admitting he was a sinner.
B) He meant he was not the best due to the Prophet's presence.
C) He was lying about his abilities.
D) He wanted to abdicate.

Key Takeaway
Abu Bakr's statement was misinterpreted; he was asserting his suitability for leadership despite not being the best in specific, limited senses.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear someone's words that seem to contradict their actions, how quickly do you jump to a negative judgment? Can you think of a time when understanding the full context changed your view of a person? What commitment can you make to seek context before judging?
?
Abu Bakr's statement 'I am not the best of you' was used against him. In your own life, are there words you have spoken that could be misunderstood? How can you ensure your intentions are clear, and how can you respond if someone misinterprets you, trusting in Allah's knowledge of your heart?

Defending Abu Bakr's Humility: Five Answers
Baqillani refutes the objection that Abu Bakr's humility negates his imamate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the five rational interpretations Baqillani offers for Abu Bakr's statement 'I am not the best of you' and how they defend his imamate against objection.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr's humility was a rhetorical tool, not a confession of unfitness.

When Abu Bakr said 'I am not the best of you,' critics saw it as an admission of unfitness. But Baqillani shows this statement was a masterful argument against tribal pride, the idea of infallible leaders, and more. In this passage, he unpacks five distinct meanings that actually strengthen Abu Bakr's claim to leadership.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the initial objection: if Abu Bakr admits he's not the best, why should he be caliph? This sets up the need for answers.
The objectors assume that 'best' means most virtuous overall.
2
Examine the first answer
Baqillani's first answer: Abu Bakr was arguing against the Ansar who thought he would step back because he led prayer in the Prophet's presence. He was not claiming he was better than the Prophet.
3
Study the lineage answer
The second answer: Abu Bakr meant he is not the best in lineage, to show that leadership is not by high birth but by the Prophet's designation.
This refutes those who say only Banu Hashim can lead.
4
Analyze the infallibility answer
The third answer: by admitting human error, Abu Bakr refutes the claim that only an infallible person can be imam.
This targets a specific Shi'a claim.
5
Review the remaining answers and conclusion
The fourth and fifth answers address divine favor and practical necessity. Baqillani ends by noting that the objectors have no rebuttal.
Note how each answer serves a specific refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا : فكيف يكون أبو بكر مستحقاً لهذا الأمر وهو يقول في هذه الخطبة: «وَلِيتُكم ولستُ بخيركم»؛ فألا علم بذلك أن الأمر لمن هو خير منه وأنه ظالم في استبداده به؟ قيل لهم في هذا أجوبة كثيرة : فأولها أنه قال ذلك محتجاً على الأنصار وعلى من ظن أنه يتأخر عنه لأنه قد وليهم الصَّلاةَ ورسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم حاضر ولعمري إنه لا يجوز أن يكون خَيْرَ قوم فيهم رسول الله صلّى الله عليه وسلم فكأنه قال: كيف لا أليكم بعد النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وقد وليتكم مع وجوده ولست بخيركم إذ ذلك؟ ومنها أنه يمكن أن يكون أراد بقوله : وليتكم ولست بخيركم أني لست بخيركم قبيلة وعشيرة ولأن بني هاشم أعلى منه في ذِرْوَةِ النسب لكي يدلهم بذلك على أن هذا الأمر العظيم ليس يُستحق بعلو النسب، وأنه ليس بمقصور على بني هاشم دون غيرهم من قريش بظاهر قوله عليه السلام : «الأئمة من قريش». ويمكن أن يكون أراد بقوله : وليتكم ولست بخيركم» أي إنه يجوز علي من السهو والغلط ووساوس الصدور وخواطر النفوس ما يجوز من السهو عليكم لكي يدلّهم بذلك على فساد قول من زعم أن هذا الأمر لا يستحقه إلا الوافر المعصوم. ويمكن أن يكون أراد بقوله: «وليتكم ولست بخيركم لولا أن الله فضلني عليكم بحق الولاية فأوجب عليكم من طاعتي أن صرت إماماً وأسقط عني فرض طاعتكم ويمكن أيضاً أن يكون قد اعتقد أن في الأمة أفضل منه إلا أن الكلمة عليه أجمعُ والأمةَ بنظره أصلحُ لكي يدلهم على جواز إمامة المفضول عند عارض يمنع من نصب الفاضل ولهذا ما قال للأنصار وغيرهم : قد رضيت لكم أحد هذين الرجلين فبايعوا أحدهما عمر بن الخطاب وأبا عبيدة بن الجراح وهو يعلم أن أبا عبيدة دونه ودون عثمان وعلي في الفضل غير أنه قد رأى أن الكلمة تجتمع عليه وتنحَسِمُ الفتنة بنظره وهذا أيضاً مما لا جواب لهم عنه .
If they say: 'How can Abu Bakr be worthy of this matter while he says in this sermon: “I have been put in charge of you while I am not the best of you”; does he not know thereby that the matter belongs to one who is better than him and that he is unjust in his exclusive assumption of it?' It is said to them: There are many answers to this. The first is that he said that as an argument against the Ansar and against those who thought that he would step back because he had led them in prayer while the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) was present, and by my life, it is not possible that he be the best of a people among whom is the Messenger of God (peace be upon him). It is as if he said: 'How can I not be in charge of you after the Prophet (peace be upon him) while I was put in charge of you in his presence and I am not the best of you at that time?' And among them (the answers) is that it is possible that he meant by his saying 'I have been put in charge of you while I am not the best of you' that I am not the best of you in tribe and clan, and because Banu Hashim are higher than him in the peak of lineage, in order to indicate to them that this great matter is not deserved by high lineage, and that it is not confined to Banu Hashim to the exclusion of other Quraysh, by the apparent meaning of his statement (peace be upon him): 'The leaders are from Quraysh.' And it is possible that he meant by his saying 'I have been put in charge of you while I am not the best of you' that forgetfulness, error, whisperings of the heart, and thoughts of the soul befall me just as they befall you, in order to indicate to them the invalidity of the claim of those who assert that this matter is not deserved except by the infallible and preserved. And it is possible that he meant by his saying 'I have been put in charge of you and I am not the best of you, were it not that God has favored me over you by the right of authority, making obedience to me obligatory upon you so that I became an imam and removed from me the obligation of obedience to you.' And it is also possible that he believed that there is someone better than him in the community, but the word (consensus) is more united upon him and the community is more suitable in his view, in order to indicate to them the permissibility of the imamate of the less meritorious when there is an obstacle preventing the appointment of the more meritorious. For this reason, he said to the Ansar and others: 'I am pleased for you with one of these two men, so pledge allegiance to one of them: Umar ibn al-Khattab and Abu Ubayda ibn al-Jarrah.' And he knew that Abu Ubayda was inferior to him and to Uthman and Ali in virtue, but he saw that the word (unity) would gather around him and that sedition would be ended by his view. And this too is something they have no answer for.
Source pages p. 497

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer unit. The objectors argue: if Abu Bakr admits he is not the best, then the caliphate should go to someone better, and his assumption of it is unjust. Baqillani responds by listing multiple answers, following the author's own order. First answer: Abu Bakr was addressing the Ansar who thought he would step back because he had led prayer in the Prophet's presence. But leading prayer in the Prophet's presence does not make him better than the Prophet, so his statement means: 'How can I not lead you after the Prophet, when I led you in his presence even though I am not better than him at that time?' Second answer: He meant he is not the best in lineage, because Banu Hashim are nobler, to show that leadership is not by lineage (since the Prophet said leaders are from Quraysh generally). Third answer: He meant he is prone to human error and whisperings, to refute the claim that only an infallible person deserves leadership. Fourth answer: He meant that were it not for God's favor in making him imam, he would be obliged to obey others; this highlights authority as a divine grant. Fifth answer: He believes there might be someone better, but due to practical considerations (unity, prevention of fitna), the less virtuous can be imam when obstacles prevent the virtuous from being appointed. This is supported by his suggestion of Umar and Abu Ubayda, both less virtuous than him, Uthman, and Ali, but chosen for unity. Baqillani concludes that these answers leave the objectors with no rebuttal.

Key Terms
وليتكم ولست بخيركم
إمامة المفضول
النص
الأئمة من قريش
المعصوم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Abu Bakr's statement 'I am not the best of you' proves he was unworthy of the caliphate and that Ali should have been caliph.
Correction: Baqillani shows the statement had multiple rhetorical meanings, including refuting the idea that only an infallible or high-born person can lead, and emphasizing practical unity.

Checkpoint

A) To admit that he is unfit for the caliphate
B) To show that high lineage is the basis for leadership
C) To refute the claim that only an infallible person can be imam
D) To praise the Ansar

Key Takeaway
Abu Bakr's humility was not a weakness but a strategic defense of his imamate, rebutting multiple objections.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you used humility as a shield to avoid taking responsibility? Abu Bakr's humility was strategic, not evasive. Is your humility driving you toward duty or away from it?
?
If you were chosen to lead despite feeling less capable than others, would you accept or defer? Baqillani argues that practical unity can outweigh personal merit. Where in your life is God calling you to step up, even if you feel unworthy?
