باب الكلام في إمامة عثمان رضي الله عنه وصحة فعل عمر في الشورى. إن سأل سائل فقال : ما الدليل على إثبات إمامة عثمان رضي الله عنه ؟ قيل له : الدليل على ذلك أن عبد الرحمن بن عوف عقدها له بمحضر من أهل الشورى سوى طلحة وأن طلحة بايعه لما قدم وعلم ضرورة من حاله رضاه بإمامته وأن عثمان في فضله وسابقته وقرابته وجهاده بنفسه وماله وما هو بسبيله من الإحاطة بحفظ القرآن ومعرفة الأحكام والحلال والحرام . وقد كملت له الخلال التي يصلح معها التقدم لإمامة المسلمين؛ هذا مع ما قد عُرِفَ من كثرة مناقبه وفضل جهاده وإنعامه، وأنه مُجهز جيش العسرة ومشتري بئر رومة وموسع مسجد النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم من ماله.
Chapter on the discussion of the imamate of Uthman, may God be pleased with him, and the correctness of Umar's action in the shura. If a questioner asks: 'What is the evidence for establishing the imamate of Uthman, may God be pleased with him?' It is said to him: The evidence for that is that Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf contracted it for him in the presence of the people of the shura except Talha, and that Talha gave him the oath of allegiance when he arrived and knew necessarily from his state his approval of his imamate, and that Uthman, in his virtue, precedence, kinship, jihad with his self and wealth, and his encompassing memorization of the Quran and knowledge of rulings and the lawful and unlawful. And he has completed the qualities that qualify him for leadership of the Muslims; this along with what is known of his many merits, the virtue of his jihad and his beneficence, and that he equipped the Army of Hardship, bought the Well of Rumah, and expanded the Prophet's mosque, peace be upon him, from his own wealth.
Source pages p. 509

Commentary
This passage presents the evidence for Uthman's imamate. It is a proof by citing historical events: Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf conducted the shura and appointed Uthman in the presence of the other shura members except Talha, who later gave bay'ah, indicating consent. Then it lists Uthman's personal qualities: his early Islam, kinship to the Prophet, jihad, wealth, knowledge of Quran and rulings, and specific deeds like equipping the army of 'Usra, buying the Well of Rumah, and expanding the mosque. These demonstrate his qualification for the imamate.

?

Evidence for Uthman's Imamate: His Virtues and Deeds
Uthman's virtues and deeds as evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Uthman's personal qualities, virtues, and specific deeds qualify him for the imamate.

Core Idea
Uthman's excellence in faith, knowledge, and generosity proves his worthiness for leadership.

After presenting the procedural evidence of the shura, al-Baqillani reinforces the case by listing Uthman's personal merits. These include his early conversion, kinship to the Prophet, jihad, wealth, knowledge of the Quran and rulings, and benevolent acts such as equipping the army, buying a well, and expanding the mosque. These virtues show that Uthman was eminently qualified for the imamate.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on virtues
Read the Arabic and translation that lists Uthman's qualities and specific deeds. Notice the sequence: virtue, precedence, kinship, jihad, knowledge, then specific acts.
2
Categorize the qualities
Group the qualities into personal attributes (virtue, precedence, kinship, jihad, knowledge) and concrete actions (equipping army, buying well, expanding mosque). Reflect on how each supports his qualification.
3
Understand the argumentative purpose
This list serves to demonstrate that Uthman possessed all the necessary qualities (khalal) for leadership. Al-Baqillani is refuting any claim that Uthman was not fit by showing his comprehensive excellence.

Suspicion Does Not Invalidate the Covenant for Umar's Caliphate
Baqillani concludes the argument for Umar's caliphate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's argument that the Muslims' suspicion towards Umar does not invalidate the covenant of his caliphate, and why this argument relies on the consistency of general legal principles.

Core Idea
Suspicion is a sin, not a reason to cancel a covenant.

Baqillani concludes his defense of Umar's caliphate by addressing the objection that some Muslims harbored suspicion towards him. He argues that suspicion, even if sinful, does not nullify the legal validity of the covenant made by Abu Bakr. This passage demonstrates a key principle in Islamic political theology: the distinction between personal sin and institutional legitimacy.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice that Baqillani is building a logical argument with an analogy.
The Arabic text has some OCR uncertainties, but the meaning is clear from context.
2
Identify key terms
Pay attention to the terms 'عهد' (covenant) and 'تهمة' (suspicion). Understand how they are used in the argument.
3
Follow the analogy
Baqillani argues that if suspicion could invalidate the covenant, then it would also have to invalidate any contract made by someone who might be influenced by personal inclination. Since we do not invalidate such contracts, the covenant remains valid.
4
Understand the conclusion
The imama of Umar is established because the covenant is sound, and Abu Bakr was a just imam who rightfully made it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عليهم أو جاهل بأمورهم أولى وفي هذا ما يوجب أن يكون ظن المسلمين بإمامهم الذي لم يعرفوه إلا بالصلاح والاستقامة والتهمة له ذنباً التوبة والاستغفار منه منهم تجب ولا يجوز أن يبطل العهد منه إلى من عهد إليه، وإن كان ممن يصلح أن يبتدىء العقد على غيره لأجل هذه التهمة وعلى أن هذا المعنى قائم في العاقد كوجوده في العاهد فيجب أيضاً أن يبطل عقد العاقد لغيره، لأنه قد يجوز أن يعقل لمن يميل إلى نظره ويؤثر ولايته ويرجو الاعتداد والانتفاع به مع العلم بأنه غير مقصر في هذا الشأن فلما لم يجز إبطال العقد بهذه التهمة لم يجز إبطال العهد. فصحت بهذه الجملة إمامة عمر رضي الله عنه وأنه بصفة من يصلح العهد إليه وابتداء العقد له وكان العاقد له إماماً عدلاً رضى بصفة من له أن يعهد إلى غيره.
upon them or ignorant of their affairs is more appropriate, and in this is what necessitates that the suspicion of the Muslims towards their imam whom they only know as righteous and upright, and the accusation against him is a sin; repentance and seeking forgiveness for it from them is obligatory. And it is not permissible to invalidate the covenant from him to the one to whom he covenanted, even if that one is among those who are fit to initiate the contract for another because of this suspicion. And because this meaning exists in the one who makes the contract just as it exists in the one who bequeaths, it would also be necessary to invalidate the contract of the one who makes the contract for another, because it may be that he acts rationally for one who inclines to his view, prefers his guardianship, and hopes for esteem and benefit from him while knowing that he is not negligent in this matter. So when it is not permissible to invalidate the contract due to this suspicion, it is not permissible to invalidate the covenant. Thus, by this summary, the imama of Umar, may God be pleased with him, is established, and that he is of the description of one fit for the covenant to be made to him and for the initiation of the contract for him, and the one who made the contract for him was a just imam, satisfied with the description of one who has the right to bequeath to another.
Source pages p. 509

Commentary
This is the concluding passage of an argument for the legitimacy of Umar's caliphate. Baqillani argues that even if some Muslims harbored suspicion towards Umar (because they did not know him except as righteous), that suspicion does not invalidate the covenant (عهد) made by Abu Bakr appointing Umar as successor. The logic is: if suspicion were to invalidate the covenant, then it would also have to invalidate any contract made by someone who might be influenced by personal inclination. But since we do not invalidate contracts on such grounds, we likewise do not invalidate the covenant of leadership. Therefore, Umar's imama is valid, and Abu Bakr was a just imam who rightfully made the covenant.

Key Terms
عهد
تهمة
إمامة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that any suspicion towards a leader automatically invalidates his appointment.
Correction: Baqillani clarifies that suspicion is a personal sin, not a legal ground to nullify a covenant of leadership.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what is the effect of the Muslims' suspicion towards Umar on his imama?
A) It invalidates his imama
B) It requires repentance but does not invalidate the covenant
C) It makes his imama questionable
D) It is a sin that cancels the covenant

Key Takeaway
Baqillani establishes Umar's caliphate by showing that suspicion does not break the covenant of leadership, preserving legal consistency.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Think of a person you have been suspicious of recently—perhaps a family member, friend, or leader. Does your suspicion rest on solid evidence or on vague feelings? In light of this lesson, are you willing to seek forgiveness for unjust suspicion and act with trust until proven otherwise? Commit to a specific change.
?
Baqillani says that the Muslims 'only know' the imam as righteous and upright. Look at your own assumptions about those who lead you. Do you truly know them as righteous, or do you allow whispers of doubt to cloud your judgment? What would it cost you to assume the best and repent when you fail?

Shura and Personal Virtues in Uthman's Imama
Baqillani gives proof through shura and personal virtues.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses the shura process and Uthman's personal qualities to establish his caliphate.

Core Idea
The shura contract and Uthman's personal virtues form a strong foundational proof for his imama.

Baqillani begins by addressing a hypothetical questioner seeking proof for Uthman's caliphate. He first points to the procedural legitimacy of the shura conducted by Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf, followed by Uthman's personal merits that qualify him for leadership. This passage combines political and religious arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Note how Baqillani structures his answer.
The passage is a direct response to a question.
2
Identify the two parts
First, the shura process; second, Uthman's personal virtues. See how they connect.
3
Consider the shura details
Notice that the shura was conducted by Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf in the presence of the shura members except Talha, who later pledged allegiance.
This shows the contract was known and accepted.
4
Examine the personal virtues
List Uthman's qualities: precedence, kinship, jihad, knowledge of Quran and rulings.
These are standard criteria for imama.

باب الكلام في إمامة عثمان رضي الله عنه وصحة فعل عمر في الشورى إن سأل سائل فقال: ما الدليل على إثبات إمامة عثمان رضي الله عنه؟ قيل له: الدليل على ذلك أن عبد الرحمن بن عوف عقدها له بمحضر من أهل الشورى سوى طلحة وأن طلحة بايعه لما قدم وعلم ضرورة من حاله رضاه بإمامته وأن عثمان في فضله وسابقته وقرابته وجهاده بنفسه وماله وما هو بسبيله من الإحاطة بحفظ القرآن ومعرفة الأحكام والحلال والحرام. وقد كملت له الخلال التي يصلح معها التقدم لإمامة المسلمين؛ هذا مع ما قد عُرِفَ من كثرة مناقبه وفضل جهاده وإنعامه، وأنه مُجهز جيش العسرة ومشتري بئر رومة وموسع مسجد النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم من ماله، وكونه من المهاجرين الأولين وتزويج النبي لابنتيه منه، وقوله: «لو كانت لنا ثالثة لزوجناك» وقوله في خبر آخر: «لو أمدنا الله بالبنات، لأمددناك بالأزواج»، وقوله: «عثمان أخي ورفيقي في الجنة»، وقوله لما ستر ركبتيه عند دخول عثمان عليه: «ألا أستحي ممن تستحي منه الملائكة؟»، وقوله فيه وفي عليّ لما أتياه في شيء حُمِلَ إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بعد أن طرح علي جبة شعر: «هكذا تدخلان الجنة ولا يحبكما إلا مؤمن ولا يبغضكما إلا منافق» وحكمه له بأنه يقتل شهيداً وأمره إياه بألا يخلع ثوباً كساه الله إياه في أخبار كثيرة يطول تعدادها تسبيح الحصى في يده وقوله: «اسكن حِرَاء! فما عليك إلا نبي وصديق وشهيد»، وفي بعض الأخبار «شهيدان»؛ فوجب بذلك أجمع أن يكون مع
Chapter on discourse concerning the imama of Uthman, may God be pleased with him, and the correctness of Umar's action in the shura. If a questioner asks: 'What is the proof for establishing the imama of Uthman, may God be pleased with him?' It is said to him: The proof for that is that Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf contracted it for him in the presence of the people of the shura except Talha, and that Talha gave him the pledge of allegiance when he arrived and knew necessarily from his state his satisfaction with his imama, and that Uthman, in his virtue, precedence, kinship, struggling with his self and wealth, and his encompassing knowledge of memorizing the Quran, understanding rulings, the permissible and the forbidden. And the traits through which one is fit to advance to the leadership of the Muslims are complete in him; this is in addition to what is known of the abundance of his merits, the virtue of his struggle, and his beneficence, and that he equipped the army of hardship (jaysh al-‘usra) and bought the well of Rumah and expanded the mosque of the Prophet (peace be upon him) from his wealth, and that he was among the first emigrants, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) marrying two of his daughters to him, and his saying: 'If we had a third, we would have married her to you,' and his saying in another report: 'If God had provided us with daughters, we would have provided you with spouses,' and his saying: 'Uthman is my brother and my companion in Paradise,' and his saying when he covered his knees during Uthman's entry: 'Should I not feel shy of the one whom the angels feel shy of?' and his saying concerning him and Ali when they came to him regarding something that was brought to the Prophet (peace be upon him) after Ali had put on a garment of wool: 'Thus you both enter Paradise; none loves you but a believer, and none hates you but a hypocrite,' and his judgment that he would be killed as a martyr, and his command to him not to take off a garment with which God had clothed him, in many reports whose enumeration would be lengthy, the pebbles glorifying in his hand, and his saying: 'Be still, Hira! For upon you there is only a prophet, a truthful one, and a martyr,' and in some reports: 'two martyrs'; thus, by all of that, it is necessary that he be with
Source pages p. 509

Commentary
This is a systematic proof for the caliphate of Uthman. Baqillani presents it in response to a hypothetical questioner. The first part of the proof is the shura (consultation) conducted by Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf, who appointed Uthman in the presence of all the members of the shura except Talha (who later gave his pledge). The second part is the enumeration of Uthman's personal qualities: his virtue, precedence in Islam, kinship to the Prophet, jihad, knowledge of the Quran and rulings. Then Baqillani lists specific historical merits: equipping the army of hardship (Tabuk expedition), buying the well of Rumah for public use, expanding the Prophet's mosque, being among the first emigrants, and marrying two of the Prophet's daughters. He then cites several Prophetic hadiths that explicitly honor Uthman: the promise of marriage to a third daughter, the statement that Uthman is his brother and companion in Paradise, the angels' shyness, the joint entry with Ali into Paradise with the test of faith, the prophecy of his martyrdom, the command not to remove the garment, and the miracle of pebbles glorifying in his hand, and the testimony of Hira. After this comprehensive list, Baqillani concludes that all of this necessitates Uthman's high rank and thus the validity of his imama.

Key Terms
شورى
عقد البيعة
مناقب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Baqillani establishes Uthman's imama through the procedural legitimacy of shura and his personal virtues.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of Uthman's virtues—his precedence, sacrifice, and knowledge—do you see those same qualities developing in your own character? What specific virtue do you lack most, and what will you do today to begin cultivating it?
?
The shura process required the involvement of the most qualified companions to reach a decision. Who are the people you consult before making major life decisions? Are you seeking counsel from those with wisdom, or are you relying solely on your own judgment?
?
Uthman's imama was validated by both proper procedure and inner virtue. In your own life, do you focus more on outward correctness (following steps) or on inward righteousness? Which one needs more attention from you right now, and what is one concrete change you can make this week?

Specific Merits and Prophetic Testimonies for Uthman
Baqillani lists merits and prophetic hadiths for Uthman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses Uthman's concrete historical merits and numerous prophetic hadiths to reinforce his caliphate's validity.

Core Idea
The miracle of pebbles and the Prophet's own words confirm Uthman's high rank and martyrdom.

Baqillani continues the proof by listing Uthman's specific contributions, such as equipping the army of hardship and buying the well of Rumah, and then cites several hadiths that directly honor Uthman. These include the Prophet's statements about Uthman being his brother in Paradise, the angels' shyness, and the testimony of Mount Hira. This passage strengthens the case with supernatural elements and divine attestation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the long list of merits and hadiths.
This is a cumulative argument.
2
Identify the merits
Find the actions like equipping the army, buying the well, expanding the mosque, and being among the first emigrants.
These are historical facts.
3
Find the prophetic sayings
Look for each hadith: from marriage promise to the Hira narration. Understand how they elevate Uthman.
4
Consider the miracle
Note the mention of pebbles glorifying in his hand—a miracle indicating saintly status.

باب الكلام في إمامة عثمان رضي الله عنه وصحة فعل عمر في الشورى إن سأل سائل فقال: ما الدليل على إثبات إمامة عثمان رضي الله عنه؟ قيل له: الدليل على ذلك أن عبد الرحمن بن عوف عقدها له بمحضر من أهل الشورى سوى طلحة وأن طلحة بايعه لما قدم وعلم ضرورة من حاله رضاه بإمامته وأن عثمان في فضله وسابقته وقرابته وجهاده بنفسه وماله وما هو بسبيله من الإحاطة بحفظ القرآن ومعرفة الأحكام والحلال والحرام. وقد كملت له الخلال التي يصلح معها التقدم لإمامة المسلمين؛ هذا مع ما قد عُرِفَ من كثرة مناقبه وفضل جهاده وإنعامه، وأنه مُجهز جيش العسرة ومشتري بئر رومة وموسع مسجد النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم من ماله، وكونه من المهاجرين الأولين وتزويج النبي لابنتيه منه، وقوله: «لو كانت لنا ثالثة لزوجناك» وقوله في خبر آخر: «لو أمدنا الله بالبنات، لأمددناك بالأزواج»، وقوله: «عثمان أخي ورفيقي في الجنة»، وقوله لما ستر ركبتيه عند دخول عثمان عليه: «ألا أستحي ممن تستحي منه الملائكة؟»، وقوله فيه وفي عليّ لما أتياه في شيء حُمِلَ إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بعد أن طرح علي جبة شعر: «هكذا تدخلان الجنة ولا يحبكما إلا مؤمن ولا يبغضكما إلا منافق» وحكمه له بأنه يقتل شهيداً وأمره إياه بألا يخلع ثوباً كساه الله إياه في أخبار كثيرة يطول تعدادها تسبيح الحصى في يده وقوله: «اسكن حِرَاء! فما عليك إلا نبي وصديق وشهيد»، وفي بعض الأخبار «شهيدان»؛ فوجب بذلك أجمع أن يكون مع
Chapter on discourse concerning the imama of Uthman, may God be pleased with him, and the correctness of Umar's action in the shura. If a questioner asks: 'What is the proof for establishing the imama of Uthman, may God be pleased with him?' It is said to him: The proof for that is that Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf contracted it for him in the presence of the people of the shura except Talha, and that Talha gave him the pledge of allegiance when he arrived and knew necessarily from his state his satisfaction with his imama, and that Uthman, in his virtue, precedence, kinship, struggling with his self and wealth, and his encompassing knowledge of memorizing the Quran, understanding rulings, the permissible and the forbidden. And the traits through which one is fit to advance to the leadership of the Muslims are complete in him; this is in addition to what is known of the abundance of his merits, the virtue of his struggle, and his beneficence, and that he equipped the army of hardship (jaysh al-‘usra) and bought the well of Rumah and expanded the mosque of the Prophet (peace be upon him) from his wealth, and that he was among the first emigrants, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) marrying two of his daughters to him, and his saying: 'If we had a third, we would have married her to you,' and his saying in another report: 'If God had provided us with daughters, we would have provided you with spouses,' and his saying: 'Uthman is my brother and my companion in Paradise,' and his saying when he covered his knees during Uthman's entry: 'Should I not feel shy of the one whom the angels feel shy of?' and his saying concerning him and Ali when they came to him regarding something that was brought to the Prophet (peace be upon him) after Ali had put on a garment of wool: 'Thus you both enter Paradise; none loves you but a believer, and none hates you but a hypocrite,' and his judgment that he would be killed as a martyr, and his command to him not to take off a garment with which God had clothed him, in many reports whose enumeration would be lengthy, the pebbles glorifying in his hand, and his saying: 'Be still, Hira! For upon you there is only a prophet, a truthful one, and a martyr,' and in some reports: 'two martyrs'; thus, by all of that, it is necessary that he be with
Source pages p. 509

Commentary
This is a systematic proof for the caliphate of Uthman. Baqillani presents it in response to a hypothetical questioner. The first part of the proof is the shura (consultation) conducted by Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf, who appointed Uthman in the presence of all the members of the shura except Talha (who later gave his pledge). The second part is the enumeration of Uthman's personal qualities: his virtue, precedence in Islam, kinship to the Prophet, jihad, knowledge of the Quran and rulings. Then Baqillani lists specific historical merits: equipping the army of hardship (Tabuk expedition), buying the well of Rumah for public use, expanding the Prophet's mosque, being among the first emigrants, and marrying two of the Prophet's daughters. He then cites several Prophetic hadiths that explicitly honor Uthman: the promise of marriage to a third daughter, the statement that Uthman is his brother and companion in Paradise, the angels' shyness, the joint entry with Ali into Paradise with the test of faith, the prophecy of his martyrdom, the command not to remove the garment, and the miracle of pebbles glorifying in his hand, and the testimony of Hira. After this comprehensive list, Baqillani concludes that all of this necessitates Uthman's high rank and thus the validity of his imama.

Key Terms
مناقب
تسبيح الحصى
جيش العسرة
بئر رومة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the proof for Uthman's imama relies only on political appointment without spiritual support.
Correction: Baqillani shows that numerous hadiths and a miracle indicate divine approval.

Checkpoint
Which miracle is attributed to Uthman in this passage?
A) Splitting the moon
B) Water flowing from his fingers
C) Pebbles glorifying in his hand
D) The sun returning for him

Key Takeaway
Baqillani reinforces Uthman's imama with concrete merits and prophetic testimonies, including a miracle.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet foretold Uthman's martyrdom and commanded him not to remove the 'garment' of caliphate. If you knew that a certain trial would lead to martyrdom, would you have the courage to stay in that position as Uthman did? Are you ready to accept whatever Allah has written for you, even if it involves hardship?
?
Uthman spent his wealth freely for the sake of Allah—equipping an army, buying a well, expanding the mosque. What is your relationship with your wealth? Are you using it in ways that will bring you closer to Allah, or are you holding back out of fear of poverty?
?
The Prophet said that only a believer loves Uthman and only a hypocrite hates him. Examine your own heart: do you feel love or indifference toward the Companions? What does that say about your own faith, and what steps can you take to increase your love for them?

Uthman's Early Emigration and Marriages to the Prophet's Daughters
Baqillani opens with Uthman's early emigration and marriages.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses Uthman's status as an early emigrant and his marriage to the Prophet's daughters as evidence for his fitness for the caliphate.

Core Idea
Uthman's early emigration and unique marriages establish his close connection to the Prophet.

Baqillani begins his argument for Uthman's merit by highlighting two foundational virtues: Uthman's place among the first emigrants and the unprecedented honor of marrying two of the Prophet's daughters. These are not mere accolades but serve as proofs that Uthman held a special status that justifies his later leadership.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Let the flow of arguments come through.
Notice that this is a list of merits, each introduced with 'و' (and).
2
Identify the two main virtues
Find the mention of being among the first emigrants and the marriage to two daughters. These are the core facts.
The additional sayings about a third daughter reinforce the second virtue.
3
Understand the conditional sayings
Examine the Prophet's statements 'If we had a third...' and 'If God provided us with daughters...'. They indicate that Uthman would have been married to more daughters if available.
These are not actual events but emphasize the Prophet's high regard for Uthman.
4
Reflect on the argumentative method
Baqillani is building a cumulative case. Each point adds to Uthman's qualification. Think about how this method strengthens the overall argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكونه من المهاجرين الأولين وتزويج النبي لابنتيه منه، وقوله : «لو كانت لنا ثالثة لزوجناك» وقوله في خبر آخر: «لو أمدنا الله بالبنات، لأمددناك بالأزواج»، وقوله: «عثمان أخي ورفيقي في الجنة»، وقوله لما ستر ركبتيه عند دخول عثمان عليه : ألا أستحي ممن تستحي منه الملائكة؟» وقوله فيه وفي عليّ لما أتياه في شيء حُمِلَ إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بعد أن طرح علي جبة شعر : «هكذا تدخلان الجنة ولا يحبكما إلا مؤمن ولا يبغضكما إلا منافق» وحكمه له بأنه يقتل شهيداً وأمره إياه بألا يخلع ثوباً كساه الله إياه في أخبار كثيرة يطول تعدادها تسبيح الحصى في يده وقوله : اسكن حِرَاءُ! فما عليك إلا نبي وصديق وشهيد» وفي بعض الأخبار «شهيدان» ; فوجب بذلك أجمع أن يكون بصفة من يصلح لهذا الشأن.
And his being among the first emigrants, and the Prophet's marriage of his two daughters to him, and his saying: 'If we had a third, we would have married you to her,' and his saying in another report: 'If God provided us with daughters, we would provide you with wives,' and his saying: 'Uthman is my brother and companion in Paradise,' and his saying when Uthman entered and the Prophet covered his knees: 'Should I not be shy of one from whom the angels are shy?' and his saying concerning him and Ali when they came to him in a matter that was brought to the Prophet after Ali had thrown off a woolen cloak: 'Thus you will enter Paradise; none loves you but a believer and none hates you but a hypocrite,' and his ruling that he would be killed as a martyr, and his commanding him not to remove a garment with which God had clothed him – in many reports whose enumeration would be lengthy – and the glorification of pebbles in his hand, and his saying: 'Be still, Hira! For upon you is only a prophet, a siddiq, and a martyr,' and in some reports 'two martyrs.' So by all that it is necessary that he be of the description of one who is fit for this matter.
Source pages p. 510

Commentary
This passage is an argument by accumulation, presenting multiple hadiths that collectively establish Uthman's merit for the caliphate. The author lists these virtues: Uthman was among the first emigrants (muhājirūn), the Prophet married two of his daughters to him, and the Prophet stated that if there were a third daughter he would marry him. Other hadiths say that Uthman is the Prophet's brother and companion in Paradise, that the angels are shy of him, that he and Ali are loved only by believers and hated only by hypocrites, that he would die a martyr, and that he should not remove a garment God had given him. Additionally, the stones glorified God in his hand, and the Prophet told Mount Hira to be still because only a prophet, a siddīq, and a martyr (or two martyrs) were upon it. The author concludes that all these proofs together necessitate that Uthman is qualified for this position (the caliphate). The method is to marshal a body of evidence to demonstrate that Uthman was the most deserving of the caliphate after the previous caliphs, countering any doubts about his fitness.

Key Terms
المهاجرين الأولين
تزويج ابنتيه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These honors are purely personal and do not relate to political leadership.
Correction: Baqillani treats them as evidence of moral and spiritual excellence required for the caliphate.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is mentioned as a virtue of Uthman in this passage?
A) He was a companion of the Prophet.
B) He was among the first emigrants.
C) He participated in all battles.
D) He was a relative of the Prophet.

Key Takeaway
Uthman's early emigration and unique marriages establish a foundational closeness to the Prophet that qualifies him for leadership.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Uthman was among the 'first emigrants' who left everything for Allah. What have you left behind for Allah? What attachment still holds you back from being among the 'first' in your commitment?
?
The Prophet said he would have married Uthman to a third daughter if he had one — that shows deep trust and love. Is there any relationship in your life that reflects such trust with the Prophet? How can you build your connection to him today?

Uthman as Brother in Paradise and the Angels' Shyness
Two hadiths about Uthman's brotherhood in Paradise and angels' shyness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadiths about Uthman being the Prophet's brother in Paradise and the angels being shy of him serve as proofs of his high station.

Core Idea
Prophetic statements elevate Uthman to a unique spiritual rank.

Baqillani continues to accumulate evidence by citing two powerful hadiths. The first declares Uthman the Prophet's brother and companion in Paradise, while the second reports that the Prophet covered his knees in modesty when Uthman entered, saying the angels themselves are shy of Uthman. These elevate Uthman's status beyond ordinary merits.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the two separate hadiths.
2
Examine the first hadith
The Prophet says Uthman is his brother and companion in Paradise. This indicates a special eternal bond.
This is a direct statement of Uthman's high rank in the afterlife.
3
Examine the second hadith
When Uthman entered, the Prophet covered his knees and said he should be shy of one whom the angels are shy of.
The covering of knees is a gesture of modesty, and the mention of angels underscores Uthman's purity.
4
Connect to the argument
Both hadiths portray Uthman as possessing a degree of sanctity that even the angels recognize. This bolsters his qualification for leadership.

Love, Hate, Martyrdom, and the Garment
Three virtues: love/hate test, martyrdom prophecy, and garment command.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith about love for Uthman and Ali, the prophecy of Uthman's martyrdom, and the command not to remove the garment prove his special status.

Core Idea
Uthman's unique position is affirmed by the test of love and hate, his predestined martyrdom, and a divine garment.

Baqillani presents three more pieces of evidence: a hadith stating that only believers love Uthman and Ali while only hypocrites hate them, a prophecy that Uthman would be killed as a martyr, and a command that he should not remove a garment given by God. These together point to Uthman's distinguished role and fate.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the three distinct points.
2
Analyze the love/hate hadith
This hadith includes Ali as well, but it explicitly states that love for them is a sign of faith, and hate is a sign of hypocrisy.
This establishes Uthman's correct position as a beloved figure of the believers.
3
Examine the martyrdom prophecy
The Prophet ruled that Uthman would be killed as a martyr, which is a high honor.
This indicates that Uthman's death would be noble.
4
Consider the command about the garment
The Prophet commanded Uthman not to remove a garment that God had clothed him with, often interpreted as the caliphate.
This has direct relevance to his leadership.

?

?

Miraculous Signs and Final Verdict
Final two miracles and the conclusion that Uthman is fit for leadership.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the miracles of stones glorifying and the hadith about Mount Hira – together with the conclusion – prove Uthman's fitness for the caliphate.

Core Idea
Miraculous signs confirm Uthman's exceptional status, leading to the verdict that he is fit for leadership.

Baqillani presents two miraculous signs: the glorification of pebbles in Uthman's hand and the Prophet's statement on Mount Hira that only a prophet, a siddiq, and a martyr (or two martyrs) are on it. He then concludes that all these proofs collectively establish Uthman's fitness for the caliphate.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Observe the two signs and the conclusion.
2
Examine the pebble glorification
Pebbles glorified God in Uthman's hand – a miracle indicating his blessedness.
This is a direct miracle (karāmah) associated with Uthman.
3
Examine the Hira hadith
The Prophet told Mount Hira to be still because upon it were only a prophet, a siddiq, and a martyr (or two).
Uthman is identified as the martyr (one of the two), placing him among the highest ranks.
4
Understand the conclusion
Baqillani states that by all this accumulated evidence, Uthman is necessarily of the description of one fit for this matter (the caliphate).
This is the final verdict of the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكونه من المهاجرين الأولين وتزويج النبي لابنتيه منه، وقوله : «لو كانت لنا ثالثة لزوجناك» وقوله في خبر آخر: «لو أمدنا الله بالبنات، لأمددناك بالأزواج»، وقوله: «عثمان أخي ورفيقي في الجنة»، وقوله لما ستر ركبتيه عند دخول عثمان عليه : ألا أستحي ممن تستحي منه الملائكة؟» وقوله فيه وفي عليّ لما أتياه في شيء حُمِلَ إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بعد أن طرح علي جبة شعر : «هكذا تدخلان الجنة ولا يحبكما إلا مؤمن ولا يبغضكما إلا منافق» وحكمه له بأنه يقتل شهيداً وأمره إياه بألا يخلع ثوباً كساه الله إياه في أخبار كثيرة يطول تعدادها تسبيح الحصى في يده وقوله : اسكن حِرَاءُ! فما عليك إلا نبي وصديق وشهيد» وفي بعض الأخبار «شهيدان» ; فوجب بذلك أجمع أن يكون بصفة من يصلح لهذا الشأن.
And his being among the first emigrants, and the Prophet's marriage of his two daughters to him, and his saying: 'If we had a third, we would have married you to her,' and his saying in another report: 'If God provided us with daughters, we would provide you with wives,' and his saying: 'Uthman is my brother and companion in Paradise,' and his saying when Uthman entered and the Prophet covered his knees: 'Should I not be shy of one from whom the angels are shy?' and his saying concerning him and Ali when they came to him in a matter that was brought to the Prophet after Ali had thrown off a woolen cloak: 'Thus you will enter Paradise; none loves you but a believer and none hates you but a hypocrite,' and his ruling that he would be killed as a martyr, and his commanding him not to remove a garment with which God had clothed him – in many reports whose enumeration would be lengthy – and the glorification of pebbles in his hand, and his saying: 'Be still, Hira! For upon you is only a prophet, a siddiq, and a martyr,' and in some reports 'two martyrs.' So by all that it is necessary that he be of the description of one who is fit for this matter.
Source pages p. 510

Commentary
This passage is an argument by accumulation, presenting multiple hadiths that collectively establish Uthman's merit for the caliphate. The author lists these virtues: Uthman was among the first emigrants (muhājirūn), the Prophet married two of his daughters to him, and the Prophet stated that if there were a third daughter he would marry him. Other hadiths say that Uthman is the Prophet's brother and companion in Paradise, that the angels are shy of him, that he and Ali are loved only by believers and hated only by hypocrites, that he would die a martyr, and that he should not remove a garment God had given him. Additionally, the stones glorified God in his hand, and the Prophet told Mount Hira to be still because only a prophet, a siddīq, and a martyr (or two martyrs) were upon it. The author concludes that all these proofs together necessitate that Uthman is qualified for this position (the caliphate). The method is to marshal a body of evidence to demonstrate that Uthman was the most deserving of the caliphate after the previous caliphs, countering any doubts about his fitness.

تسبيح الحصى
شهيد

Misconception: These miracles alone are not enough to prove leadership.
Correction: Baqillani argues that the cumulative weight of all proofs, including these miracles, makes the conclusion necessary.

Key Takeaway
The miracles confirm Uthman's exceptional status, and the accumulated evidence leads to the necessary conclusion that he is fit for leadership.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The lesson argues that miracles necessitate a conclusion about Uthman's fitness. When have you dismissed extraordinary evidence because it didn't fit your preconceptions? How can you be more open to accepting divine signs in matters of faith?
?
The Prophet's words 'Be still, Hira' imply that true worth is known by God. Examine your own judgments of people: do you prioritize spiritual rank over worldly status? What step will you take today to correct your vision?
?
Baqillani uses the word 'wajaba' (it is necessary). Is your faith built on a foundation of logical necessity or on comfortable traditions? Are you willing to follow the evidence wherever it leads, even to uncomfortable conclusions about leadership?

Defending Umar's Shura and Uthman's Caliphate
Baqillani defends Umar's decision to appoint a consultative council for the caliphate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani defends Umar's decision to appoint a shura and argues that even if it were mistaken, the pledge to Uthman remains valid.

Core Idea
Umar's shura was wise and not required for Uthman's legitimacy.

This passage presents a key objection from opponents of the Sunni position on the caliphate. They question Umar's authority to appoint a limited council. Baqillani responds with a two-pronged argument: first, the council's decision was independently valid; second, Umar's action was itself correct and prudent. As you read, see how he prioritizes the qualifications of the six and Umar's caution.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and initial response
Notice how Baqillani first sidesteps the need to validate the shura by emphasizing the qualifications of the six.
The six were the best of the community and most deserving.
2
Examine the hypothetical scenario
If the six had convened on their own, the pledge would be binding. This shows their independent authority.
3
Follow Baqillani's positive defense
Umar had the right to appoint one, but chose consultation due to ambiguity and fear of corruption.
Umar's caution for the umma is highlighted.
4
Consider the historical details
Umar's sermon and the dream of the rooster add backing to his decision.
The dream indicates imminent death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا فما الدليل على أن لعمر أن يجعلها شورى في نفر من المسلمين؟ قيل لهم : ليس الكلام في تصحيح الشورى مما يُحتاج إليه في إثبات إمامة عثمان لأن الستة الذين هم أهلها كانوا أفضل الأمة وأحق الناس بهذا الأمر وبالنظر فيه فلو أنهم اجتمعوا بأنفسهم ونظروا في أمر إمامتهم، وعقد عبد الرحمن أو غيره لواحد منهم لتمت بيعته ولزم الإنقياد له. فلو اعترفنا بغلط عُمَر في جعله شورى فيهم لم يضر ذلك بصحة عقد عبد الرحمن بن عوف لعثمان رضي الله عنهما، غير أن البراهين الواضحة قد أوجبت سلامة عمر بن الخطاب رضي الله عنه هذا الفعل، ودلت على صوابه وتسديد رأيه وشدة احتياطه للأمة، لأنه كان له أن يعهد إلى واحد منهم فلما ترجح الأمر في نفسه وأشكل عليه ولم يرد صلاح الأمة على أيهم يكون أكثر ، وخاف هَرْجاً وفساداً بعهده وعلم أنهم أفاضل الأمة وبلغه أن قوماً يخوضون في أمر الإمامة يريدون إخراجها عن جميع الستة وأخبره بذلك عبد الرحمن وغيره فقام في الناس خطيباً بفضلهم وأخبرهم أن الأمر لا يعدوهم وأنه فيهم فقال لهم في خطبته المشهورة: «ألا وأني رأيت كأن ديكاً نقرني نقرةً أو نقرتين وما أظن ذلك إلا اقتراب أجلي ألا وإني جعلت الأمر شورى في هؤلاء الستة الرهط الذين توفّي رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وهو عنهم راض وقد بلغني أن قوماً يقولون : لئن مات عمر لنولين فلاناً أولئك أعداء الله الضَّلال الجهال، والله لقد جالدتهم هذه على الإسلام بيدي
If they say: What is the evidence that Umar had the right to make it a consultative council among a group of Muslims? It is said to them: The discussion is not that the validation of the shura is needed for establishing the imamate of Uthman, because the six who were its people were the best of the community and most deserving of this matter and of considering it. For if they had gathered by themselves and considered the matter of their imamate, and Abd al-Rahman or someone else had concluded the pledge for one of them, his allegiance would have been completed and submission to him would have been obligatory. So if we acknowledged that Umar was mistaken in making it a shura among them, that would not harm the validity of Abd al-Rahman's pledge to Uthman. However, clear proofs have obligated the soundness of Umar's action, and indicated its correctness, the rightness of his opinion, and the intensity of his caution for the community. Because he had the right to appoint one of them, but when the matter was ambiguous to him and he did not know who would be best for the community, and he feared turmoil and corruption if he appointed someone, and he knew that they were the elite of the community, and it reached him that some people were immersing themselves in the matter of the imamate, wanting to remove it from all the six – and Abd al-Rahman and others informed him of that – so he stood among the people as a preacher, praising their virtue, and informed them that the matter would not go beyond them, and that it was among them. He said to them in his famous sermon: 'Lo, I saw as if a rooster pecked me once or twice, and I do not think that is anything but the approach of my death. Lo, I have made the matter a consultation among these six men with whom the Messenger of God was pleased when he died. And it has reached me that some people say: If Umar dies, we will appoint so-and-so. Those are the enemies of God, the misguided ignoramuses. By God, I have fought them over this [caliphate] in Islam with my own hand.'
Source pages p. 511

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objectors ask: what proof is there that Umar had the right to make the caliphate a shura among a few Muslims? The answer first argues that the validity of the shura is not necessary for establishing Uthman's imamate, because the six members were the best of the community and most entitled to decide. Even if they had convened on their own and Abd al-Rahman had pledged allegiance to one of them, it would be binding. Thus, even if we concede that Umar erred in making it a shura, that does not harm the validity of Abd al-Rahman's pledge to Uthman. However, the author adds that clear proofs show Umar's action was correct and prudent. Umar had the right to appoint one person, but when the matter was unclear and he feared corruption if he appointed a specific person, he chose consultation. He knew the six were the elite, and he learned that some people were trying to remove the caliphate from all of them. So he gave a sermon praising them and declaring that the caliphate would remain among them. The sermon includes Umar's dream of being pecked by a rooster (a sign of imminent death) and his warning against those who would try to appoint someone else. The argument demonstrates that Umar's action was both valid and wise, and the subsequent pledge to Uthman was sound.

Key Terms
شورى
عقد عبد الرحمن بن عوف
سلامة عمر بن الخطاب
أفضل الأمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Umar's shura was a mistake that would invalidate Uthman's caliphate.
Correction: Baqillani argues that even if it were a mistake, the pledge of Abd al-Rahman to Uthman is independently valid because the six were qualified. Moreover, Umar's action was actually correct and wise.

Checkpoint
What does Baqillani argue would be the case even if Umar had been mistaken in making the shura?
A) The caliphate of Uthman would be invalid.
B) The pledge of Abd al-Rahman to Uthman would still be valid.
C) The umma would have to hold a new election.
D) Ali would have been the rightful caliph.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani defends the Sunni view by showing that the shura was both valid and wise, and that Uthman's caliphate is secure regardless.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are faced with a decision that affects others, do you seek counsel like Umar, or do you rely solely on your own judgment? What would it take for you to admit uncertainty and ask for guidance, especially when the stakes are high?
?
Umar feared turmoil (harj) if he acted alone. In your life, have you ever caused harm by making a decision without consulting those it would affect? How can you build the habit of seeking input before acting?
?
The six were described as 'the best of the community' (afḍal al-ummah). Do you recognize and defer to those with greater knowledge and virtue in your own circles, or does pride prevent you from acknowledging their worth? What is one step you can take today to humble yourself before those who are more qualified?

The Validity of Uthman's Caliphate Does Not Depend on Umar's Shura
Baqillani responds to an objection by arguing that the validity of Uthman's caliphate does not depend on Umar's shura.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the validity of Uthman's caliphate is not contingent on the correctness of Umar's shura, as the six companions had the authority to appoint him independently.

Core Idea
Uthman's caliphate is valid even if Umar had erred in the shura.

Baqillani begins by addressing a potential objection: What evidence is there that Umar had the right to make the caliphate a shura among six people? He responds by clarifying that the shura's validity is not necessary to prove Uthman's imamate. Instead, the six themselves were the most qualified to decide, and their choice would be binding regardless of Umar's method. This argument shifts the focus from the process to the capability of the electors.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the objection
Baqillani first presents an imagined objection: 'What is the evidence that Umar made it a shura among a group?' Read the opening lines carefully.
2
Understand Baqillani's strategic response
Notice that Baqillani does not directly defend Umar's action. Instead, he argues that even if Umar had erred, the contract of Abd al-Rahman for Uthman would still be valid.
This is a key defensive move.
3
Reflect on the implications
Ask yourself: Why would Baqillani make this argument? It shows that the legitimacy of a caliph does not rest on a single procedural step if the choice is made by qualified individuals.
This strengthens the case for Uthman.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بصفة من يصلح لهذا الشأن. فإن قالوا فما الدليل على أن لعمر أن يجعلها شورى في نفر من المسلمين؟ . قيل لهم : ليس الكلام في تصحيح الشورى مما يُحتاج إليه في إثبات إمامة عثمان لأن الستة الذين هم أهلها كانوا أفضل الأمة وأحق الناس بهذا الأمر وبالنظر فيه فلو أنهم اجتمعوا بأنفسهم ونظروا في أمر إمامتهم، وعقد عبد الرحمن أو غيره لواحد منهم لتمت بيعته ولزم الإنقياد له. فلو اعترفنا بغلط عُمَر في جعله شورى فيهم لم يضر ذلك بصحة عقد عبد الرحمن بن عوف لعثمان رضي الله عنهما، غير أن البراهين الواضحة قد أوجبت سلامة عمر بن الخطاب رضي الله عنه هذا الفعل، ودلت على صوابه وتسديد رأيه وشدة احتياطه للأمة، لأنه في كان له أن يعهد إلى واحد منهم فلما ترجح الأمر في نفسه وأشكل عليه ولم يرد صلاح الأمة على أيهم يكون أكثر ، وخاف هَرْجاً وفساداً بعهده وعلم أنهم أفاضل الأمة وبلغه أن قوماً يخوضون في أمر الإمامة يريدون إخراجها عن جميع الستة وأخبره بذلك عبد الرحمن وغيره فقام في الناس خطيباً بفضلهم وأخبرهم أن الأمر لا يعدوهم وأنه فيهم فقال لهم في خطبته المشهورة: «ألا وأني رأيت كأن ديكاً نقرني نقرةً أو نقرتين وما أظن ذلك إلا اقتراب أجلي ألا وإني جعلت الأمر شورى في هؤلاء الستة الرهط الذين توفّي رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وهو عنهم راض وقد بلغني أن قوماً يقولون : لئن مات عمر لنولين فلاناً أولئك أعداء الله الضَّلال الجهال، والله لقد جالدتهم هذه على الإسلام بيدي وهذا غاية ما يكون من الإحتياط للأمة وحسم مادة الفتنة وإطماع من طمع في هذا الأمر من غير أهله وتنبيهه للمسلمين على فضل فاضلهم والتوقيف على مراشدهم ومصالحهم وقد كانوا قالوا لعمر تعهد ؟ فقال: «إن أعْهَد ، فقد عهد من هو خير مني» يعني أبا بكر «وإن أترك ، فقد ترك من هو خير مني» يعني رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وذكر له عبد الله ابنه لأجل فضله وعلمه ونسكه وكثرة الرضا بمثله، فقال: «لم أكن بالذي أتحملها حياً وميتاً» وقال : «يكفي آل الخطاب أن يسأل منهم رجل واحد» وقال: «أما إنه لو حضرني سالم مولى أبي حذيفة لرأيت أني قد أصبت الرأي، وما تداخلني فيه الشكوك، وفي خبر آخر «أبو عبيدة بن الجراح أو سالم»، يريد مشاورة سالم وأخذ رأيه دون العقد له لأنه أحد.
As for the quality of one who is suitable for this matter. If they say: what is the evidence that Umar made it a shura among a group of Muslims? It is said to them: The discussion about the validity of the shura is not needed for establishing the imamate of Uthman, because the six who were its people were the best of the community and the most rightful of people for this matter and for deliberation in it. If they had gathered by themselves and looked into the matter of their imamate, and Abd al-Rahman or others had contracted for one of them, his pledge of allegiance would have been completed and submission to him would have been obligatory. So if we were to acknowledge an error on the part of Umar in making it a shura among them, that would not harm the validity of the contract of Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf for Uthman (may Allah be pleased with them both). However, clear proofs have necessitated the soundness of this action of Umar ibn al-Khattab (may Allah be pleased with him), and indicated its correctness, the rightness of his opinion, and his extreme caution for the community, because he had the right to entrust it to one of them. When the matter became unclear to him and ambiguous, and he did not know whose appointment would be more beneficial for the community, and he feared turmoil and corruption from his appointment, and he knew that they were the virtuous of the community, and it reached him that a group of people were speculating about the matter of the imamate, wanting to take it away from all six, and Abd al-Rahman and others informed him of that, so he stood among the people as a sermonizer about their merits and informed them that the matter does not go beyond them and that it is among them. He said to them in his famous sermon: 'Behold, I saw as if a rooster pecked me once or twice, and I do not think that but the approach of my death. Behold, I have made the matter a shura among these six men with whom the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) passed away while he was pleased with them. And it has reached me that some people say: If Umar dies, we will appoint so-and-so. They are the enemies of Allah, the misled ignorant. By Allah, I have fought them with this (hand) for Islam.' This is the utmost caution for the community, and cutting off the source of discord, and cutting off the hopes of those who coveted this matter from other than its people, and alerting the Muslims to the virtue of their virtuous one, and directing them to their guidance and interests. And they had said to Umar: 'Will you appoint a successor?' So he said: 'If I appoint, then one better than me has appointed' meaning Abu Bakr, 'and if I leave, then one better than me has left' meaning the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). And he was mentioned Abdullah his son because of his merit, knowledge, piety, and the abundance of satisfaction with his like, so he said: 'I am not one to bear it alive and dead.' And he said: 'It is enough for the family of al-Khattab that one man is asked from among them.' And he said: 'As if Salim, the freed slave of Abu Hudhayfa, were present, I would think that I have hit the opinion, and no doubts would enter me about it.' And in another report: 'Abu Ubayda ibn al-Jarrah or Salim' – meaning consulting Salim and taking his opinion, not contracting for him, because he was one.
Source pages p. 511

Commentary
This passage is a defense of Umar's decision to make the caliphate a shura among six companions, and an argument for the validity of Uthman's appointment. It begins by addressing an objection: 'What is the evidence that Umar had the right to make it a shura among a group?' The author responds that the validity of the shura is not necessary to prove Uthman's imamate, because the six were the best of the community and most entitled to decide. Even if they had gathered on their own and chosen one of them, the pledge would be binding. So even if Umar had erred in restricting it to six, the contract of Abd al-Rahman for Uthman would still be valid. However, the author then insists that clear proofs show Umar's action was correct and cautious. He explains that Umar could have appointed one directly, but the matter was unclear, and he feared factionalism. He learned that some sought to exclude all six, so he delivered a famous sermon declaring the shura and warning against those who would 'appoint so-and-so' after him. The sermon shows his caution: he dreamed of a rooster pecking him, indicating his death, and he fought for Islam with his own hand. The author then adds further evidence: when asked to appoint a successor, Umar said it was better to leave it as the Prophet and Abu Bakr did. He even mentioned his son Abdullah but declined, saying he would not bear it alive or dead. He also mentioned Salim, a freed slave, as someone whose opinion he would follow, but not as a candidate. This demonstrates his impartiality and concern for the community's welfare.

Correction: Baqillani argues that even if Umar erred, the contract made by Abd al-Rahman for Uthman would still be valid because the six had the inherent authority to choose.

C) The six would have to choose a different process.

Key Takeaway
Uthman's caliphate is valid because the six electors were qualified to choose, regardless of any potential flaw in Umar's procedural setup.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

In light of this lesson's principle, could the decision still be valid if those who made it were qualified? What does this require from your heart concerning trust in the choices of righteous people?
?
The six electors were the best of the community. In your own life, do you seek out the best qualified people to make decisions that affect your community, or do you insist on perfect procedures first? How does this lesson challenge your attitude?
?
Baqillani did not defend Umar's action directly but rooted legitimacy in the authority of the electors. This teaches us to focus on the qualifications of decision-makers rather than procedural perfection. Is there a situation in your own life where you have focused too much on the process and not enough on the integrity of the people involved? What would it look like to shift that focus?

Umar's Caution and Wisdom in the Shura
Baqillani defends Umar's shura as correct and demonstrates his caution through his sermons and statements.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will appreciate the strong evidence that Umar's decision to form a shura among the six was correct, cautious, and in the best interest of the community.

Core Idea
Umar's shura was a model of caution, not a mistake.

After establishing that the shura's validity is not essential, Baqillani proceeds to defend Umar's action itself. He marshals evidence that Umar acted with extreme caution, fearing discord and ensuring that the caliphate remained among the most qualified. He describes Umar's famous sermon and his responses to suggestions of appointing a successor, showing his impartiality and wisdom.

Guided Path
1
Read the defense of Umar's action
Baqillani now provides clear proofs that Umar's action was correct. Notice the phrase 'غير أن البراهين الواضحة' as a transition.
2
Understand Umar's reasons for the shura
Baqillani explains that Umar could have appointed one directly but chose a shura because the matter was unclear, he feared corruption, and he wanted to involve the best.
This shows his caution.
3
Analyze Umar's sermon and his sayings
Read the sermon about the rooster pecking and his warning against those who sought to exclude the six. Then consider his refusal to appoint his son or Salim. What do these tell you about his character?
They demonstrate his reluctance to favor relatives and his openness to merit.

بصفة من يصلح لهذا الشأن. فإن قالوا فما الدليل على أن لعمر أن يجعلها شورى في نفر من المسلمين؟ . قيل لهم : ليس الكلام في تصحيح الشورى مما يُحتاج إليه في إثبات إمامة عثمان لأن الستة الذين هم أهلها كانوا أفضل الأمة وأحق الناس بهذا الأمر وبالنظر فيه فلو أنهم اجتمعوا بأنفسهم ونظروا في أمر إمامتهم، وعقد عبد الرحمن أو غيره لواحد منهم لتمت بيعته ولزم الإنقياد له. فلو اعترفنا بغلط عُمَر في جعله شورى فيهم لم يضر ذلك بصحة عقد عبد الرحمن بن عوف لعثمان رضي الله عنهما، غير أن البراهين الواضحة قد أوجبت سلامة عمر بن الخطاب رضي الله عنه هذا الفعل، ودلت على صوابه وتسديد رأيه وشدة احتياطه للأمة، لأنه في كان له أن يعهد إلى واحد منهم فلما ترجح الأمر في نفسه وأشكل عليه ولم يرد صلاح الأمة على أيهم يكون أكثر ، وخاف هَرْجاً وفساداً بعهده وعلم أنهم أفاضل الأمة وبلغه أن قوماً يخوضون في أمر الإمامة يريدون إخراجها عن جميع الستة وأخبره بذلك عبد الرحمن وغيره فقام في الناس خطيباً بفضلهم وأخبرهم أن الأمر لا يعدوهم وأنه فيهم فقال لهم في خطبته المشهورة: «ألا وأني رأيت كأن ديكاً نقرني نقرةً أو نقرتين وما أظن ذلك إلا اقتراب أجلي ألا وإني جعلت الأمر شورى في هؤلاء الستة الرهط الذين توفّي رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وهو عنهم راض وقد بلغني أن قوماً يقولون : لئن مات عمر لنولين فلاناً أولئك أعداء الله الضَّلال الجهال، والله لقد جالدتهم هذه على الإسلام بيدي وهذا غاية ما يكون من الإحتياط للأمة وحسم مادة الفتنة وإطماع من طمع في هذا الأمر من غير أهله وتنبيهه للمسلمين على فضل فاضلهم والتوقيف على مراشدهم ومصالحهم وقد كانوا قالوا لعمر تعهد ؟ فقال: «إن أعْهَد ، فقد عهد من هو خير مني» يعني أبا بكر «وإن أترك ، فقد ترك من هو خير مني» يعني رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وذكر له عبد الله ابنه لأجل فضله وعلمه ونسكه وكثرة الرضا بمثله، فقال: «لم أكن بالذي أتحملها حياً وميتاً» وقال : «يكفي آل الخطاب أن يسأل منهم رجل واحد» وقال: «أما إنه لو حضرني سالم مولى أبي حذيفة لرأيت أني قد أصبت الرأي، وما تداخلني فيه الشكوك، وفي خبر آخر «أبو عبيدة بن الجراح أو سالم»، يريد مشاورة سالم وأخذ رأيه دون العقد له لأنه أحد.
As for the quality of one who is suitable for this matter. If they say: what is the evidence that Umar made it a shura among a group of Muslims? It is said to them: The discussion about the validity of the shura is not needed for establishing the imamate of Uthman, because the six who were its people were the best of the community and the most rightful of people for this matter and for deliberation in it. If they had gathered by themselves and looked into the matter of their imamate, and Abd al-Rahman or others had contracted for one of them, his pledge of allegiance would have been completed and submission to him would have been obligatory. So if we were to acknowledge an error on the part of Umar in making it a shura among them, that would not harm the validity of the contract of Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf for Uthman (may Allah be pleased with them both). However, clear proofs have necessitated the soundness of this action of Umar ibn al-Khattab (may Allah be pleased with him), and indicated its correctness, the rightness of his opinion, and his extreme caution for the community, because he had the right to entrust it to one of them. When the matter became unclear to him and ambiguous, and he did not know whose appointment would be more beneficial for the community, and he feared turmoil and corruption from his appointment, and he knew that they were the virtuous of the community, and it reached him that a group of people were speculating about the matter of the imamate, wanting to take it away from all six, and Abd al-Rahman and others informed him of that, so he stood among the people as a sermonizer about their merits and informed them that the matter does not go beyond them and that it is among them. He said to them in his famous sermon: 'Behold, I saw as if a rooster pecked me once or twice, and I do not think that but the approach of my death. Behold, I have made the matter a shura among these six men with whom the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) passed away while he was pleased with them. And it has reached me that some people say: If Umar dies, we will appoint so-and-so. They are the enemies of Allah, the misled ignorant. By Allah, I have fought them with this (hand) for Islam.' This is the utmost caution for the community, and cutting off the source of discord, and cutting off the hopes of those who coveted this matter from other than its people, and alerting the Muslims to the virtue of their virtuous one, and directing them to their guidance and interests. And they had said to Umar: 'Will you appoint a successor?' So he said: 'If I appoint, then one better than me has appointed' meaning Abu Bakr, 'and if I leave, then one better than me has left' meaning the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). And he was mentioned Abdullah his son because of his merit, knowledge, piety, and the abundance of satisfaction with his like, so he said: 'I am not one to bear it alive and dead.' And he said: 'It is enough for the family of al-Khattab that one man is asked from among them.' And he said: 'As if Salim, the freed slave of Abu Hudhayfa, were present, I would think that I have hit the opinion, and no doubts would enter me about it.' And in another report: 'Abu Ubayda ibn al-Jarrah or Salim' – meaning consulting Salim and taking his opinion, not contracting for him, because he was one.
Source pages p. 511

Commentary
This passage is a defense of Umar's decision to make the caliphate a shura among six companions, and an argument for the validity of Uthman's appointment. It begins by addressing an objection: 'What is the evidence that Umar had the right to make it a shura among a group?' The author responds that the validity of the shura is not necessary to prove Uthman's imamate, because the six were the best of the community and most entitled to decide. Even if they had gathered on their own and chosen one of them, the pledge would be binding. So even if Umar had erred in restricting it to six, the contract of Abd al-Rahman for Uthman would still be valid. However, the author then insists that clear proofs show Umar's action was correct and cautious. He explains that Umar could have appointed one directly, but the matter was unclear, and he feared factionalism. He learned that some sought to exclude all six, so he delivered a famous sermon declaring the shura and warning against those who would 'appoint so-and-so' after him. The sermon shows his caution: he dreamed of a rooster pecking him, indicating his death, and he fought for Islam with his own hand. The author then adds further evidence: when asked to appoint a successor, Umar said it was better to leave it as the Prophet and Abu Bakr did. He even mentioned his son Abdullah but declined, saying he would not bear it alive or dead. He also mentioned Salim, a freed slave, as someone whose opinion he would follow, but not as a candidate. This demonstrates his impartiality and concern for the community's welfare.

احتياط
سالم مولى أبي حذيفة
أبو عبيدة بن الجراح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Umar's shura was a sign of indecisiveness or weakness.
Correction: Baqillani shows it was a deliberate and cautious act to prevent discord and ensure the best outcome for the community.

Checkpoint
Why did Umar make the shura among the six instead of appointing one directly, according to Baqillani?
A) He was unsure who was best and feared corruption.
B) He was forced by the people.
C) He wanted to follow the Prophet's example.
D) He was too weak to decide.

Key Takeaway
Umar's shura was a wise and cautious decision to preserve unity and ensure the caliphate remained among the most qualified.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a major decision where the right path is unclear, do you rush to decide or pause to seek counsel from those with wisdom and piety? How does Umar's example of shura challenge your own habit of relying solely on your own judgment?
?
Umar refused to appoint his own son despite his qualifications, prioritizing justice over family loyalty. Is there someone in your life whom you have favored unfairly due to relationship or affection? What would it cost you to choose merit over preference as Umar did?
?
Umar was willing to share authority with a council to preserve unity. In what area of your life—work, family, or community—do you hold onto power or control that could be shared for the greater good? What is holding you back from letting go?

Umar's Precautions in Forming the Shura
Baqillani narrates Umar's measures to prevent fitna in succession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Umar's actions in forming the shura exemplify the principle of ihtiyat (precaution) to prevent fitna and preserve the unity of the Muslim community.

Core Idea
Umar's precautions show that preserving community unity outweighs personal preference or explicit appointment.

Imam Baqillani presents the actions of Umar ibn al-Khattab as a model of the utmost precaution for the Muslim community. In this passage, we see how Umar carefully avoided any step that might lead to discord or misinterpretation, from refusing to appoint a successor to preventing any of the candidates from leading the prayer. This lesson explores the reasoning behind each precaution and its relevance to the broader discussion of imamate and succession.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about Umar's shura
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation. Pay attention to Umar's various statements and actions.
The passage is a historical narrative, so focus on the sequence of precautions.
2
Identify the key precautions Umar took
List the specific measures Umar implemented: not appointing a successor, considering Salim, making it a shura, preventing prayer leadership, and instructions to the council.
3
Understand the reasoning behind each precaution
For each precaution, note the reason Umar gave. For example, he refused to appoint because the Prophet did not appoint, and he feared fitna from prayer leadership.
Consider how each action aligns with ihtiyat.
4
Connect to the principle of ihtiyat
Reflect on how these precautions collectively aim to cut off sources of discord and preserve unity. Baqillani explicitly calls this 'the utmost precaution.'
This connects to broader themes in Islamic theology about leadership and community welfare.

And this is the utmost precaution for the community, cutting off the source of discord and the aspirations of those who covet this matter without being its people, and alerting the Muslims to the merit of their virtuous, and guiding them to their right paths and interests. Then he prevented them from having one among them lead the prayer, for fear that it might be thought or considered as an appointment, and that his opinion would be seen as such, and that it would become an argument for those who believed in his self-exaltation and that he was more entitled to the matter than them, or so that no one would dislike him or be repelled at his advance, stirring discord leading to division of word, dispersal of opinion, and removal of the matter from its proper place. And he put forward for them one in whose trustworthiness and righteousness they had no doubt, namely Suhayb, so he led them in prayer during the days of their consultation, until their poet said: 'Suhayb prayed three times, then sent it forth / as a kingdom to Ibn Affan, not forced.' Source pages p. 512

Commentary
This passage is a historical narrative by Baqillani describing the actions of Umar ibn al-Khattab (may God be pleased with him) regarding the succession after him. The author presents this as an example of utmost precaution (ihtiyat) for the Muslim community. The passage explains that Umar did not directly appoint a successor, citing the examples of Abu Bakr (who appointed him) and the Prophet (who left without appointing). He rejected the suggestion to appoint his son Abdullah due to his virtue, saying he would not bear that responsibility. He considered Salim, a freed slave, for consultation but not for the pledge, because Salim was among those who used the hadith 'The leaders are from Quraysh' against the Ansar. Umar then decided to make the selection a shura (consultative council) among six specified individuals, informing the Muslims that the best of the community were included and that the imamate does not go beyond them. He feared that someone unqualified might covet the position, so he prevented any of them from leading the prayer to avoid the appearance of a designation (nass). He appointed Suhayb, a trustworthy and righteous man, to lead the prayer during the consultation. The poet's verse indicates that Suhayb's prayer was a sign of the eventual selection of Uthman. Umar also gave instructions regarding Talha's tardiness and advised that if the council splits, they should side with Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf. The narrative emphasizes Umar's careful measures to preserve unity and avoid discord.

شورى
إمامة
احتياط
فتنة
نص
قريش
صهيب
عبد الرحمن بن عوف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Umar's refusal to appoint a successor showed indecision or lack of planning.
Correction: Umar's actions were deliberate precautions (ihtiyat) to avoid fitna and follow the best examples, not indecision.

Checkpoint
Why did Umar prevent any of the six candidates from leading the prayer during the shura?
A) He did not trust them
B) To avoid the appearance that leading prayer was a designation (nass) for the caliphate
C) He wanted Suhayb to be caliph
D) He did not want prayer to be interrupted

Key Takeaway
Umar's careful measures in the shura demonstrate that protecting community unity and avoiding fitna are paramount in matters of succession.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Umar took extreme care to avoid even the appearance of favoritism, going so far as to prevent the shura members from leading prayer. In your own life, where might you be insensitive to how your actions appear to others, potentially causing division? What step will you take this week to neutralise a perceived bias?
?
Umar refused to appoint his own son despite his merit, saying, 'I would not take it upon myself alive or dead.' Is there a position or privilege you hold that you could release for the greater good of unity? What fear keeps you from letting go?
?
Umar's primary concern was 'cutting off the source of discord' for the entire ummah. When you make decisions affecting your family, workplace, or community, do you prioritise unity and long-term harmony over personal preference or immediate gain? What is one decision you need to revisit with this lesson's standard?

Umar's Shura as a Virtue
Author argues Umar's shura was a virtue based on his leadership.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Baqillani considers Umar ibn al-Khattab's appointment of a shura to choose the next caliph as a virtue and sign of his careful leadership.

Core Idea
Umar's shura was a deliberate virtue, not indecision.

This passage presents a defense of Umar's decision to set up a shura (consultation council) to choose his successor. Some may see this as a deviation from earlier practice, but Imam Baqillani argues that it was a reflection of Umar's caution and concern for the ummah's unity. Let's read his argument and see how he turns a potential criticism into a praise.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the rhetorical opening: 'Would that I knew...'
2
Identify Umar's precautions
The passage lists several actions Umar took to avoid fitna and ensure a smooth transition. List them: informing the ummah, preventing prayer leadership, appointing Suhayb, setting time limits, advising to follow Abd al-Rahman.
3
Understand the conclusion
The author concludes that because Umar was a just imam and acted with caution, his making the shura must be counted as a virtue. Relate this to the overall argument defending Umar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويا ليت شعري ما الذي حضّر على عمر جعلها شورى وإخبار المسلمين أنهم أفضل الأمة وأن الإمامة لا تعدوهم وقد أجمع المسلمون على ما ذكر هذا مع خوفه مما أنهي إليه من طمع من ليس من أهل هذا الأمر ثم منعهم من أن يصلي بالناس واحد منهم خوفاً من أن يُظَنَّ أو يُقَدَّرَ أنه كالنص عليه وأن رأيه فيه وأن يصير ذلك حجة لمن اعتقد منهم تعظيم نفسه وأنه أولى بالأمر منهم أو لأن لا يكرهه كاره أو ينفر عند تقدمه نافر فتهيج فتنة تعود بتفريق الكلمة وشتات الرأي وخروج الأمر عن نصابه وقدم لهم من لا يشكون في أمانته وصلاحه وهو صهيب فصلى بهم أيام مشورتهم حتى قال شاعرهم: صلى صهيب ثلاثاً ثم أرسلها على ابن عفان ملكاً غير مقسور وقال: «لا تنتظروا طلحة أكثر من ثلاثة أيام؛ فإن قدم، وإلا فأنفذوا أمركم»، وقال لهم: «فإن انقسم القوم شطرين، فكونوا في حيز عبد الرحمن بن عوف»، لعلمه بأمانته وثقته وأنه مرضي عند الكافة وأزهدهم في هذا الأمر؛ على أن هذه الرواية شاذة غير معلومة؛ ولم يكن يبعد إذا اعتقد هذا أجمع في عبد الرحمن أن ينص عليه أو يعهد إليه، وظاهر الفعل المتفق عليه يدل على اعتدالهم في نفسه وتقاربهم في المنزلة وما يُحتاج إليه من صلاح الأمة. وإذا كان ذلك كذلك وكان عمر بما قدمناه إماماً عدلاً مرضيّاً وقد خالف من الأمر ما وصفه وعُلِمَ احتياطه وجب أن يكون جعله لها شورى إحدى فضائله ومناقبه، ومضافاً إلى ما سلف من إنعام نظره للمسلمين ونصحه إياهم.
Would that I knew what prompted Umar to make it a consultation and to inform the Muslims that they are the best of the community and that the imamate does not go beyond them, while the Muslims were in agreement on what he mentioned, along with his fear of what had reached him of the greed of those not of this matter, then he prevented any one of them from leading the people in prayer for fear that it might be thought or supposed that it was a designation and his opinion of him, and that this would become a proof for those among them who thought highly of themselves and that he was more entitled to the matter than them, or lest a disliker dislike him or an aversive turn away at his advancement, causing a sedition that would lead to disunity of word, scattering of opinion, and the matter departing from its proper place; and he put forward for them one in whose honesty and righteousness they had no doubt, namely Suhayb, who led them in prayer during the days of their consultation until their poet said: 'Suhayb prayed three times then sent it upon Ibn Affan as a king without force.' And he said: 'Do not wait for Talha more than three days; if he comes, otherwise carry out your affair.' And he said to them: 'If the people split into two parties, be in the party of Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf,' because of his knowledge of his trustworthiness and confidence in him, and that he was acceptable to the whole and the most abstinent among them in this matter; although this report is anomalous and not known; and it would not be far, if he believed all this about Abd al-Rahman, that he would designate him or entrust him; and the apparent agreed-upon action indicates their equality in his eyes and their proximity in rank and what is needed for the welfare of the community. And if this is so, and Umar, as we have presented, was a just, acceptable imam, and he acted contrary to what was described, and his caution was known, then it must be that his making it a consultation was one of his virtues and merits, in addition to what preceded of his beneficent care for the Muslims and his sincere advice to them.
Source pages p. 513

Commentary
This passage is an argument defending Umar ibn al-Khattab's decision to establish a consultation (shura) to choose the next caliph after him. The author begins by expressing wonder at what motivated Umar to set up the shura and informs the Muslims that they are the best community and that the imamate does not go beyond them, while the Muslims agreed on that. Umar feared that someone not fit might aspire to the caliphate. He prevented any one of the candidates from leading the prayer to avoid creating the impression that this was a designation (nass) or that his opinion favored that person, which could become a proof for those who thought highly of themselves. He feared that a disliked candidate would cause division. He appointed Suhayb, who was unquestionably trustworthy, to lead prayer during the consultation. The author then quotes a poet and Umar's instructions: not to wait for Talha more than three days, and to side with Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf if there is a split, because Umar knew of his trustworthiness and that he was acceptable to all. However, the author notes that this report is anomalous (shādhdha) and not well known, so it may not be reliable. The author then argues that if Umar believed all this about Abd al-Rahman, it would not be far that he would designate him, but the apparent agreed-upon action shows the candidates were equal in Umar's view. The conclusion: since Umar was a just and acceptable imam and acted with caution, his making the succession a shura must be counted as one of his virtues and merits, adding to his previous beneficial care and sincere advice to the Muslims.

Misconception: Some think Umar's shura was a sign of indecision or weakness.
Correction: Imam Baqillani argues that Umar's actions show careful planning and concern for unity, making the shura a virtue, not a flaw.

Checkpoint

A) It was a sign of Umar's indecisiveness.
B) It was a deviation from the proper method.
