Umar's establishment of the shura was a praiseworthy act of caution and foresight, ensuring the ummah's continuity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Umar's careful planning of the shura shows his concern for the ummah's unity. Look at your own leadership or influence—when have you made decisions that prioritized the long-term unity of your community or family over your own immediate desires? What would it cost you to imitate Umar's caution in your own life?
?
The author says Umar feared that a disliked candidate might cause division. In your relationships, have you ever pushed forward your own preference without considering how it might cause discord among those who disagree? How can you emulate Umar's wisdom in consulting others before making a decision that affects the group?
?
Umar's shura was a virtue because it demonstrated his sincere advice and care. Think of a recent decision you made that affected others. Was it driven by your own self-interest or by genuine care for their welfare? Are you willing to let go of your own preferences for the sake of harmony, even if it means you don't get what you want?

Objection: Umar's Criticism of the Shura Members
Author presents objection about Umar's criticism of shura members.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection raised against Umar's claim of seeking the ummah's welfare, based on the reported harsh criticisms he directed at the shura members.

Core Idea
Umar's harsh words to the shura members seem to contradict his claim of seeking the community's welfare.

This passage presents a key objection to the argument that Umar acted in the best interest of the Muslim community. The objectors point to reports of Umar severely criticizing the very members of the shura council he later appointed. Understanding this objection is crucial before examining the response of the author, which unfortunately is not fully preserved in this excerpt.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection statement
Begin by reading the opening objection question. It asks how Umar's harsh criticism of the shura members can be reconciled with his claim of seeking the ummah's welfare.
Notice that the objection is not a denial of the reports, but a challenge to the compatibility with Umar's intention.
2
Examine Umar's words to Talha
Read the section where Umar addresses Talha. He rebukes him for pride and reminds him of an incident where the Prophet died angry with Talha until the verse of hijab was revealed.
This is a strong accusation; note the gravity of the claim.
3
Examine Umar's words to Zubayr
Read Umar's address to Zubayr. He describes him as inconsistent: a believer when satisfied, a disbeliever when angry, sometimes a devil, sometimes a human.
This implies Zubayr is unstable, questioning his suitability for leadership.
4
Examine Umar's words to Uthman and Ali
Read Umar's prediction for Uthman (will favor his relatives, be killed) and his words to Ali (would lead well but prevented by a playful trait).
The passage ends mid-sentence on Ali; the full response is not available.
5
Reflect on the objection's force
Consider how these reports, if authentic, seem to undermine Umar's stated intention. This is the strength of the objection that the author must answer.
Without the refutation, we only have one side of the argument here.

فإن قالوا: كيف يجوز أنه يكون قاصداً للمصلحة وحسن النظر للأمة بهذا القول مع ما روي عنه من ذمه لجميع أهل الشورى ووصفه لهم بأنهم لا يقومون بالإمامة ولا يصلحون لها نحو ما رُوِيَ عنه أنه أمر بهم يوماً وهم مجتمعون، فأقبل عليهم وقال لهم: «أكلكم يطمع في هذا الأمر؟» أما قول وأن طلحة قال له: إن رأيت أن تكف عنا القول فافعل؛ فإنك لا تقول خيراً»، وأن الزبير قال له: «قل، وما عساك أن تقول؟»، فقال لطلحة: أما أنت فما أعرفك منذ أن شلت يمينك مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من البأوِ والكبر الذي أحدثته، ولقد مات رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وهو عليك غضبان لما قلت ما قلت حتى نزلت آية الحجاب»؛ ثم قال للزبير: وأما أنت فإنك مؤمن الرضا كافر الغضب يوماً شيطان ويوماً إنسان؛ فمن للمسلمين يوم تكون شيطاناً؟»؛ وأقبل على عثمان فقال له: «أما أنت، فوالله لئن وليت هذا الأمر، لتحملن بني أبي معيط على رقاب الناس وليأكلن مال الله، ولتسيرن العرب إليك ولتقتلنك؛ والله لئن فعلت ليفعلن»؟ ثم أخذ لحيته فهزها ثم قال: اذكرني إذا كان ذلك يا ابن عفان!»؛ ثم أقبل على علي فقال له: (وأما أنت يا علي، فلئن وليتهم، لتحملتهم على المحجة البيضاء والطريق المستقيم وما يقعدك عن هذا إلا دعابة فيك وأنك
For if they say: How can it be that he intended the welfare and good consideration for the community by this statement, given what has been narrated from him of his criticism of all the members of the shura and his description of them as not capable of the imamate and not fit for it, similar to what has been narrated from him that he summoned them one day while they were gathered, and he faced them and said to them: 'Do all of you covet this matter?' As for the statement that Talha said to him: 'If you see fit to stop speaking to us, do so, for you do not say good,' and that al-Zubayr said to him: 'Speak, what could you say?' Then he said to Talha: 'As for you, I do not recognize you since your right hand was paralyzed with the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, because of the pride and arrogance you have acquired. The Messenger of God died while he was angry with you because of what you said until the verse of the hijab was revealed.' Then he said to al-Zubayr: 'As for you, you are a believer in satisfaction and a disbeliever in anger; one day a devil, one day a human; so who will be for the Muslims on the day you are a devil?' And he turned to Uthman and said to him: 'As for you, by God, if you take charge of this matter, you will surely place the sons of Abu Mu'ayt upon the necks of the people, and they will surely devour the wealth of God, and the Arabs will surely march to you and kill you. By God, if you do it, they will certainly do it.' Then he took his beard and shook it and said: 'Remember me when that happens, O Ibn Affan.' Then he turned to Ali and said to him: 'As for you, O Ali, if you take charge of them, you will surely lead them on the white path and the straight road, and nothing prevents you from this except a playful disposition in you and that you...'
Source pages p. 513

Commentary
This passage presents an objection to the author's previous argument. The objectors question how Umar could have been seeking the welfare of the ummah when he is reported to have harshly criticized all the members of the shura, describing them as incapable of the imamate. The objection is followed by a detailed narration of Umar's words to Talha, Zubayr, Uthman, and Ali. To Talha, Umar rebukes him for pride and reminds him that the Prophet died angry with him due to an incident until the verse of hijab was revealed. To Zubayr, Umar describes him as inconsistent: a believer when satisfied, a disbeliever when angry, sometimes a devil, sometimes a human, asking who will lead the Muslims on the day he is a devil. To Uthman, Umar predicts that if he becomes caliph, he will favor his Banu Umayya relatives, devour public wealth, and be killed. Then he shakes his beard and tells him to remember that warning. To Ali, Umar says that Ali would lead on the right path, but is held back by a playful (dāʿiba) trait. The narration ends abruptly mid-sentence with 'and that you...' (wa-annaka...). The author does not provide his own response to this objection within this window; the passage only presents the evidence for the objection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The shura members each reacted differently to Umar's criticism: Talha was defensive, Zubayr was dismissive, Uthman remained silent, and Ali listened patiently. Which response most closely mirrors your own when you are criticized? What does that reveal about your character, and what would it take for you to receive correction with humility?
?
Umar's words, though harsh, were intended to expose weaknesses for the good of the community. Think of a time when someone spoke a hard truth to you for your own benefit. Did you receive it as a gift or as an attack? What concrete step will you take next time to welcome such criticism rather than resist it?
?
The objection in this lesson quotes Umar to challenge his integrity. Consider your own life: Are there past words or actions of yours that could be misused to cast doubt on your intentions? Baqillani's Principle: Interpreting Umar's Statements as Warnings
Baqillani establishes that Umar's statements cannot be literal criticisms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's foundational argument that Umar's statements about the Companions, even if seemingly critical, must be interpreted as warnings and not as contradictions or accusations.

Core Idea
Umar's words are warnings, not accusations.

Baqillani opens his refutation by challenging the assumption that Umar could have contradicted his own deep knowledge and practice. He argues that any report critical of the Companions must be understood in the context of Umar's consistent praise and guidance. This lesson sets the hermeneutic principle for the entire discussion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage where Baqillani questions how Umar could be accused of contradiction
Notice how Baqillani appeals to Umar's known virtue and knowledge.
2
Understand the principle
If Umar's statements were literal criticisms, they would contradict his known actions of leading the community.
3
Recognize the conclusion
Baqillani uses this to demand that such reports be discarded or reinterpreted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فوجب دفعها واطراحُها . المناقصات وكيف يجوز أن يُظنَّ بعُمَرَ في فضله وتيقظه وصرامته وثاقب رأيه وعلمه بمواقع الخطاب وأحوال الكلام وموارد الأمور ومصادرها أن يناقض بمثل هذه في كلامه وهو من أعلمهم بضبط الصحابة وتحصيلهم واستدراكهم للدقيق اللطيف فضلاً المناقضة الظاهرة وإن كان قاصداً بهذا الكلام القدح عن في فضلهم؟ وكيف لم يعرف أن القوم يعلمون بأن الكثير البطالة والدعابة لا يحمل الناس على المحجة البيضاء والطريق المستقيم وأن حملهم على هذا المنهاج ضد البطالة والدعابة ونقيضها؟ فلو لم نعلم ضرورة بالروايات المعارضة لهذه الأخبار الواردة عنه في تقريظهم وتعظيمهم، لوجب أن يُنفى مثل هذه المناقضات فكيف والأمر بخلاف ذلك؟ وكيف يجوز أن يقبل مثل هذا في طلحة ما روي عن النبي صلّى الله عليه وسلم من تفضيله مع له وقوله : «هذا كله الطلحة» ولولا أنه قال حس، لطار الملائكة، وقوله للصحابة وقد أحدقوا به لأخذ دِرْعِه وحط السلاح عنه : عليكم بطلحة، في أمثال لهذه الأخبار معلومة ثابتة؟ ويكون قاصداً بقوله للزبير ما قاله للتحذير له من التشدد والمضايقة ولم يصفه بالبخل في نفسه؛ لأن الإنسان قد يكون أسخى من الريح الهَبُوبِ مع تشدده ومضايقته في المعاملة. وعلى أنه لم يَقُلْ فيه إنه قد فعل ذلك أو يفعله، وإنما قال: «لألفي فاعلا على مذهب التحذير. وعلى ذلك تأويل قوله إنه «ضرس شرس». وأما قوله : «يوماً شيطان ويوماً إنسان»، وإنه «مؤمنُ الرّضا كافر الغضب»، فإنه أيضاً يصف فيه لين أخلاقه تارة وحسن رضاً أو شدة غضبه تارة وتعسُّفه والتحذير له من ذلك إن ولى الأمر. وكذلك قوله في سعد إنه صاحب قنص وقوس وسهام» وإنه «صاحب مقنب من مقانبهم، وليس بصاحب الجسيم من أمرهم إنه خرج مخرج التحذير له من أن يكون بهذه الصفة إن ولى الأمر والدعاء له إلى ترك الاشتغال بذلك أحياناً والانتصاب إلى النظر في مصالح الأمة وكيف يكون هذا الخبر صحيحاً وهو يستكفيه ويُؤَمِّرُه على الأقاليم ويقول عند موته: «أوصي الخليفة من بعدي أن يُوَلِّي سعداً ؛ فإني لم أصرفه عن خيانة ولا موجدةٍ». وكذلك قوله في عليّ وأنه لكثير البطالة والدعابة، لو صحت هذه الرواية أيضاً، إنما المراد به النهي والتحذير والدعاء إلى ترك المزح في بعض الأوقات وهذا كله لا يوجبُ الفجور وإسقاط العدالة وإخراج من له هذه الأوصاف أو شيء منها عن استحقاق الإمامة . وأما قوله في عبد الرحمن: وما زُهرةُ وهذا الأمر!» إنما هو على مذهب التحذير من العجز إن صح ولقد ظهر من صرامة عبد الرحمن وشدته وجمع القوم للنظر في هذا الأمر معه شاكاً سلاحه ما يدل على نفي العجز عنه وبُعدُهُ منه وهذا مع اجتماع القوم على الرضا به والاعتماد على رأيه ومع ما عُلم من زهده فيه وإخراجه نفسه عنه مع صلاحه له وتمكنه من القيام به. فمن ظن أن عمر أراد غير ما ذكرناه إن صح الحديث فقد ظن بعيداً قدر أنا نترك الظاهر المعلوم من إعظام عمر لهم وحُسنِ ثنائه عليهم إلى هذه الروايات فقد ظن عجزاً وتفريطاً عظيماً واعتقد شططاً .
It is necessary to reject and discard them. The contradictions: How can it be supposed of Umar, with his virtue, alertness, firmness, piercing insight, knowledge of the places of address, conditions of speech, and the sources and origins of matters, that he would contradict himself with such things in his speech, while he is among the most knowledgeable of them in the precision of the Companions, their acquisition (of knowledge), and their grasping of subtle and fine points, let alone an apparent contradiction? Even if he intended by this speech to disparage their virtue? And how did he not know that the people know that one who is much given to frivolity and jesting does not lead people on the white path and the straight way, and that leading them on this path is the opposite of frivolity and jesting? If we did not know necessarily the narrations that oppose these reports reported from him in praise and exaltation of them, it would be necessary to deny such contradictions – how then when the matter is contrary to that? And how can such (reports) be accepted regarding Talha, given what has been narrated from the Prophet, peace be upon him, regarding his preference for him and his saying: 'This is all Talha,' and 'If it were not for what he said, the angels would have flown,' and his saying to the Companions when they surrounded him to take his armor and remove his weapons: 'Upon you is Talha,' among similar well-known and established reports? And his saying regarding al-Zubair what he said was for the purpose of warning him against severity and tightness, and he did not describe him as miserly in himself, because a man may be more generous than the blowing wind with his severity and tightness in transactions. Moreover, he did not say about him that he had done that or would do it; rather he said: 'I will find a doer' in the manner of warning. And on that is the interpretation of his saying that he is 'a rough rock'. As for his saying: 'One day a devil, one day a human,' and that he is 'a believer in satisfaction, disbeliever in anger,' he is also describing in him the softness of his character sometimes and good satisfaction, or the severity of his anger sometimes and his harshness, and warning him against that if he were to assume authority. Similarly, his saying regarding Sa'd that he is 'a master of hunting, bow, and arrows' and that he is 'a master of a squadron among their squadrons, and not a master of the great matter of their affair' was issued as a warning to him against being of this description if he were to assume authority, and a call to him to abandon preoccupation with that sometimes and to devote himself to considering the interests of the nation. And how can this report be authentic while he (Umar) deemed him sufficient and appointed him over regions and said at his death: 'I advise the Caliph after me to appoint Sa'd; for I did not dismiss him due to betrayal or resentment'? Similarly, his saying regarding Ali, that he is much given to frivolity and jesting, even if this narration were authentic, its meaning is prohibition, warning, and a call to abandon jesting at some times. And all of this does not require wickedness, dropping of uprightness, or removing one who has these descriptions or some of them from deserving the imamate. As for his saying regarding Abd al-Rahman: 'What is Zuhra and this matter!' it is in the manner of warning against incapability, if it is authentic. And indeed the firmness of Abd al-Rahman, his severity, and the people gathering to consider this matter with him while armed has appeared, indicating the negation of incapability from him and his distance from it. And this, with the people's agreement to be satisfied with him and reliance on his opinion, and with what is known of his asceticism regarding it and his removing himself from it despite his suitability for it and his ability to undertake it. Whoever thinks that Umar intended other than what we have mentioned, if the report is authentic, has thought far off. If we leave the apparent known from Umar's veneration of them and his good praise of them for these reports, he would have thought incapability and great negligence and believed an extreme thing.
Source pages p. 516

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of accusations against Umar and other Companions. Baqillani begins by stating that such accusations must be rejected. He asks how it is possible to suppose that Umar, given his intelligence and knowledge, would contradict himself in his speech. He then argues that if Umar had truly intended to disparage the Companions, it would conflict with his own actions in leading them on the right path. Baqillani invokes the well-known praise that Umar expressed for them, which contradicts any negative reports. He then addresses specific charges against Talha, Zubair, Sa'd, Ali, and Abd al-Rahman individually. For Talha, he cites the Prophet's praise to establish his high status, implying that Umar's statements could not be negative. For Zubair, he explains that Umar's remark about finding him 'a doer' was a warning against severity, not a description of miserliness. He further interprets Umar's description of Zubair as 'a rough rock' and his statements about him being 'one day a devil, one day a human' as references to his character fluctuations, but still as warnings. For Sa'd, Baqillani notes that Umar's description of him as a hunter was a warning against neglecting duties, and points out that Umar himself appointed Sa'd and recommended him as caliph. For Ali, he argues that even if the report of his frivolity is authentic, it was a call to avoid jesting at times, not a negation of his uprightness. Finally, for Abd al-Rahman, Baqillani interprets Umar's question 'What is Zuhra and this matter?' as a warning against incapability, but notes that Abd al-Rahman's actual firmness and the people's agreement with him disprove any inability. The passage concludes by dismissing those who would interpret Umar's words as anything other than warnings, calling such interpretations far-fetched and negligent.

Key Terms
مناقصة
بطالة
دعابة
تحذير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Umar's critical statements about the Companions were literal accusations of deficiency.
Correction: Baqillani argues that such an interpretation contradicts Umar's known virtue and the evidence of his praise for the Companions. Therefore, these statements must be understood as warnings and advice.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, why should reports critical of Umar's view of the Companions be rejected?
A) Because they contradict Umar's known praise of them
B) Because they are from unreliable narrators
C) Because Umar never said them
D) Because the Companions were infallible

Key Takeaway
Umar's statements about the Companions must be interpreted as warnings, not accusations, because literal interpretation contradicts his known virtue and praise.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When someone criticizes you, do you immediately assume they are attacking, or do you consider their character and intentions? Umar's statements were reinterpreted as warnings. How often do you give others the benefit of the doubt in light of their known virtues? How can you apply this principle to your own judgments of people starting today?
?
Baqillani argues that Umar's actions of leading on the straight path contradict any intent to disparage. Are there actions in your life that contradict your words? Are you consistent? What specific step can you take this week to align your speech with your deeds?
?
The Companions were praised by Umar despite reports of criticism. Do you seek out the positive reports about others or dwell on the negative? What does your default assumption say about your heart? Will you commit to actively looking for the good in someone you currently judge harshly?

Defending Talha and Zubair from Umar's Alleged Criticisms
Baqillani defends Talha and Zubair against specific criticisms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani defends Talha and Zubair by citing the Prophet's praise for Talha and interpreting Umar's statements about Zubair as warnings against severity.

Core Idea
Prophetic praise protects Talha; Umar's words about Zubair are warnings.

Baqillani addresses specific reports about Talha and Zubair. For Talha, he invokes the Prophet's explicit commendation to show his high status, implying that Umar could not have criticized him. For Zubair, he explains that Umar's description of him as a 'rough rock' and fluctuating character were warnings against extreme behavior, not condemnations.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about Talha
Notice how Baqillani uses the Prophet's sayings to establish Talha's virtue.
2
Read the passage about Zubair
Understand Baqillani's interpretation of Umar's statements as warnings.
He emphasizes that Umar did not say Zubair had done anything wrong.
3
Compare the two defenses
Both rely on the principle that Umar's words are not literal accusations.
For Talha, direct prophetic praise; for Zubair, reinterpretation as warning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فوجب دفعها واطراحُها . المناقصات وكيف يجوز أن يُظنَّ بعُمَرَ في فضله وتيقظه وصرامته وثاقب رأيه وعلمه بمواقع الخطاب وأحوال الكلام وموارد الأمور ومصادرها أن يناقض بمثل هذه في كلامه وهو من أعلمهم بضبط الصحابة وتحصيلهم واستدراكهم للدقيق اللطيف فضلاً المناقضة الظاهرة وإن كان قاصداً بهذا الكلام القدح عن في فضلهم؟ وكيف لم يعرف أن القوم يعلمون بأن الكثير البطالة والدعابة لا يحمل الناس على المحجة البيضاء والطريق المستقيم وأن حملهم على هذا المنهاج ضد البطالة والدعابة ونقيضها؟ فلو لم نعلم ضرورة بالروايات المعارضة لهذه الأخبار الواردة عنه في تقريظهم وتعظيمهم، لوجب أن يُنفى مثل هذه المناقضات فكيف والأمر بخلاف ذلك؟ وكيف يجوز أن يقبل مثل هذا في طلحة ما روي عن النبي صلّى الله عليه وسلم من تفضيله مع له وقوله : «هذا كله الطلحة» ولولا أنه قال حس، لطار الملائكة، وقوله للصحابة وقد أحدقوا به لأخذ دِرْعِه وحط السلاح عنه : عليكم بطلحة، في أمثال لهذه الأخبار معلومة ثابتة؟ ويكون قاصداً بقوله للزبير ما قاله للتحذير له من التشدد والمضايقة ولم يصفه بالبخل في نفسه؛ لأن الإنسان قد يكون أسخى من الريح الهَبُوبِ مع تشدده ومضايقته في المعاملة. وعلى أنه لم يَقُلْ فيه إنه قد فعل ذلك أو يفعله، وإنما قال: «لألفي فاعلا على مذهب التحذير. وعلى ذلك تأويل قوله إنه «ضرس شرس». وأما قوله : «يوماً شيطان ويوماً إنسان»، وإنه «مؤمنُ الرّضا كافر الغضب»، فإنه أيضاً يصف فيه لين أخلاقه تارة وحسن رضاً أو شدة غضبه تارة وتعسُّفه والتحذير له من ذلك إن ولى الأمر. وكذلك قوله في سعد إنه صاحب قنص وقوس وسهام» وإنه «صاحب مقنب من مقانبهم، وليس بصاحب الجسيم من أمرهم إنه خرج مخرج التحذير له من أن يكون بهذه الصفة إن ولى الأمر والدعاء له إلى ترك الاشتغال بذلك أحياناً والانتصاب إلى النظر في مصالح الأمة وكيف يكون هذا الخبر صحيحاً وهو يستكفيه ويُؤَمِّرُه على الأقاليم ويقول عند موته: «أوصي الخليفة من بعدي أن يُوَلِّي سعداً ؛ فإني لم أصرفه عن خيانة ولا موجدةٍ». وكذلك قوله في عليّ وأنه لكثير البطالة والدعابة، لو صحت هذه الرواية أيضاً، إنما المراد به النهي والتحذير والدعاء إلى ترك المزح في بعض الأوقات وهذا كله لا يوجبُ الفجور وإسقاط العدالة وإخراج من له هذه الأوصاف أو شيء منها عن استحقاق الإمامة . وأما قوله في عبد الرحمن: وما زُهرةُ وهذا الأمر!» إنما هو على مذهب التحذير من العجز إن صح ولقد ظهر من صرامة عبد الرحمن وشدته وجمع القوم للنظر في هذا الأمر معه شاكاً سلاحه ما يدل على نفي العجز عنه وبُعدُهُ منه وهذا مع اجتماع القوم على الرضا به والاعتماد على رأيه ومع ما عُلم من زهده فيه وإخراجه نفسه عنه مع صلاحه له وتمكنه من القيام به. فمن ظن أن عمر أراد غير ما ذكرناه إن صح الحديث فقد ظن بعيداً قدر أنا نترك الظاهر المعلوم من إعظام عمر لهم وحُسنِ ثنائه عليهم إلى هذه الروايات فقد ظن عجزاً وتفريطاً عظيماً واعتقد شططاً .
It is necessary to reject and discard them. The contradictions: How can it be supposed of Umar, with his virtue, alertness, firmness, piercing insight, knowledge of the places of address, conditions of speech, and the sources and origins of matters, that he would contradict himself with such things in his speech, while he is among the most knowledgeable of them in the precision of the Companions, their acquisition (of knowledge), and their grasping of subtle and fine points, let alone an apparent contradiction? Even if he intended by this speech to disparage their virtue? And how did he not know that the people know that one who is much given to frivolity and jesting does not lead people on the white path and the straight way, and that leading them on this path is the opposite of frivolity and jesting? If we did not know necessarily the narrations that oppose these reports reported from him in praise and exaltation of them, it would be necessary to deny such contradictions – how then when the matter is contrary to that? And how can such (reports) be accepted regarding Talha, given what has been narrated from the Prophet, peace be upon him, regarding his preference for him and his saying: 'This is all Talha,' and 'If it were not for what he said, the angels would have flown,' and his saying to the Companions when they surrounded him to take his armor and remove his weapons: 'Upon you is Talha,' among similar well-known and established reports? And his saying regarding al-Zubair what he said was for the purpose of warning him against severity and tightness, and he did not describe him as miserly in himself, because a man may be more generous than the blowing wind with his severity and tightness in transactions. Moreover, he did not say about him that he had done that or would do it; rather he said: 'I will find a doer' in the manner of warning. And on that is the interpretation of his saying that he is 'a rough rock'. As for his saying: 'One day a devil, one day a human,' and that he is 'a believer in satisfaction, disbeliever in anger,' he is also describing in him the softness of his character sometimes and good satisfaction, or the severity of his anger sometimes and his harshness, and warning him against that if he were to assume authority. Similarly, his saying regarding Sa'd that he is 'a master of hunting, bow, and arrows' and that he is 'a master of a squadron among their squadrons, and not a master of the great matter of their affair' was issued as a warning to him against being of this description if he were to assume authority, and a call to him to abandon preoccupation with that sometimes and to devote himself to considering the interests of the nation. And how can this report be authentic while he (Umar) deemed him sufficient and appointed him over regions and said at his death: 'I advise the Caliph after me to appoint Sa'd; for I did not dismiss him due to betrayal or resentment'? Similarly, his saying regarding Ali, that he is much given to frivolity and jesting, even if this narration were authentic, its meaning is prohibition, warning, and a call to abandon jesting at some times. And all of this does not require wickedness, dropping of uprightness, or removing one who has these descriptions or some of them from deserving the imamate. As for his saying regarding Abd al-Rahman: 'What is Zuhra and this matter!' it is in the manner of warning against incapability, if it is authentic. And indeed the firmness of Abd al-Rahman, his severity, and the people gathering to consider this matter with him while armed has appeared, indicating the negation of incapability from him and his distance from it. And this, with the people's agreement to be satisfied with him and reliance on his opinion, and with what is known of his asceticism regarding it and his removing himself from it despite his suitability for it and his ability to undertake it. Whoever thinks that Umar intended other than what we have mentioned, if the report is authentic, has thought far off. If we leave the apparent known from Umar's veneration of them and his good praise of them for these reports, he would have thought incapability and great negligence and believed an extreme thing.
Source pages p. 516

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of accusations against Umar and other Companions. Baqillani begins by stating that such accusations must be rejected. He asks how it is possible to suppose that Umar, given his intelligence and knowledge, would contradict himself in his speech. He then argues that if Umar had truly intended to disparage the Companions, it would conflict with his own actions in leading them on the right path. Baqillani invokes the well-known praise that Umar expressed for them, which contradicts any negative reports. He then addresses specific charges against Talha, Zubair, Sa'd, Ali, and Abd al-Rahman individually. For Talha, he cites the Prophet's praise to establish his high status, implying that Umar's statements could not be negative. For Zubair, he explains that Umar's remark about finding him 'a doer' was a warning against severity, not a description of miserliness. He further interprets Umar's description of Zubair as 'a rough rock' and his statements about him being 'one day a devil, one day a human' as references to his character fluctuations, but still as warnings. For Sa'd, Baqillani notes that Umar's description of him as a hunter was a warning against neglecting duties, and points out that Umar himself appointed Sa'd and recommended him as caliph. For Ali, he argues that even if the report of his frivolity is authentic, it was a call to avoid jesting at times, not a negation of his uprightness. Finally, for Abd al-Rahman, Baqillani interprets Umar's question 'What is Zuhra and this matter?' as a warning against incapability, but notes that Abd al-Rahman's actual firmness and the people's agreement with him disprove any inability. The passage concludes by dismissing those who would interpret Umar's words as anything other than warnings, calling such interpretations far-fetched and negligent.

Key Terms
تحذير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Umar criticized Zubair for miserliness or harshness.
Correction: Baqillani shows that Umar's words were warnings against potential excessive strictness, not judgments of his character.

Checkpoint
How does Baqillani defend Talha against negative reports?
A) By denying the reports existed
B) By citing the Prophet's praise of Talha
C) By saying Umar never spoke about Talha
D) By claiming Talha was infallible

Key Takeaway
Prophetic praise safeguards Talha's reputation, and Umar's remarks about Zubair are reinterpreted as constructive warnings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a report about a respected person from the past, do you rush to assume the worst, or do you, like Baqillani, seek a charitable interpretation? What prevents you from giving the benefit of the doubt?
?
Umar's words to Zubair were warnings, not condemnations. In your own relationships, are you quick to label someone's flaws as permanent traits, or do you see them as warnings to be addressed with care? Which approach would please Allah?
?
Prophetic praise of Talha forces us to reject any criticism against him. How does your heart react when someone you love in Allah is criticized? Do you defend them with evidence, or remain silent? What would you change after today?

Sa'd and Ali: Warnings, Not Criticisms
Baqillani defends Sa'd and Ali by reinterpreting Umar's statements as warnings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani defends Sa'd and Ali by interpreting Umar's statements as warnings against neglecting duties and as calls to abandon frivolity.

Core Idea
Umar's words about Sa'd and Ali are warnings about potential neglect, not character flaws.

Baqillani addresses reports that Umar described Sa'd as a hunter and Ali as frivolous. He argues these were not negative assessments but warnings: urging Sa'd to attend to leadership duties and Ali to reduce jesting. He also cites Umar's own appointment of Sa'd and his testimony as proof of his trust in them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about Sa'd
Notice how Baqillani interprets Umar's description as a warning against neglecting duties, and points to Umar's appointment of Sa'd.
2
Read the passage about Ali
Understand that even if the report is authentic, it is a call to avoid excessive jesting, not a condemnation.
Baqillani emphasizes this does not affect uprightness or eligibility for imamate.
3
Compare the defenses
Both rely on reinterpretation as warnings and on external evidence of Umar's trust.

Source Text

على الرضا به والاعتماد على رأيه ومع ما عُلم من زهده فيه وإخراجه نفسه عنه مع صلاحه له وتمكنه من القيام به. فمن ظن أن عمر أراد غير ما ذكرناه إن صح الحديث فقد ظن بعيداً قدر أنا نترك الظاهر المعلوم من It is necessary to reject and discard them. The contradictions: How can it be supposed of Umar, with his virtue, alertness, firmness, piercing insight, knowledge of the places of address, conditions of speech, and the sources and origins of matters, that he would contradict himself with such things in his speech, while he is among the most knowledgeable of them in the precision of the Companions, their acquisition (of knowledge), and their grasping of subtle and fine points, let alone an apparent contradiction? If we did not know necessarily the narrations that oppose these reports reported from him in praise and exaltation of them, it would be necessary to deny such contradictions – how then when the matter is contrary to that? And how can such (reports) be accepted regarding Talha, given what has been narrated from the Prophet, peace be upon him, regarding his preference for him and his saying: 'This is all Talha,' and 'If it were not for what he said, the angels would have flown,' and his saying to the Companions when they surrounded him to take his armor and remove his weapons: 'Upon you is Talha,' among similar well-known and established reports? Moreover, he did not say about him that he had done that or would do it; rather he said: 'I will find a doer' in the manner of warning. Commentary
This passage is a refutation of accusations against Umar and other Companions. Baqillani begins by stating that such accusations must be rejected. He asks how it is possible to suppose that Umar, given his intelligence and knowledge, would contradict himself in his speech. He then argues that if Umar had truly intended to disparage the Companions, it would conflict with his own actions in leading them on the right path. Baqillani invokes the well-known praise that Umar expressed for them, which contradicts any negative reports. He then addresses specific charges against Talha, Zubair, Sa'd, Ali, and Abd al-Rahman individually. For Talha, he cites the Prophet's praise to establish his high status, implying that Umar's statements could not be negative. For Zubair, he explains that Umar's remark about finding him 'a doer' was a warning against severity, not a description of miserliness. He further interprets Umar's description of Zubair as 'a rough rock' and his statements about him being 'one day a devil, one day a human' as references to his character fluctuations, but still as warnings. For Sa'd, Baqillani notes that Umar's description of him as a hunter was a warning against neglecting duties, and points out that Umar himself appointed Sa'd and recommended him as caliph. For Ali, he argues that even if the report of his frivolity is authentic, it was a call to avoid jesting at times, not a negation of his uprightness. Finally, for Abd al-Rahman, Baqillani interprets Umar's question 'What is Zuhra and this matter?' as a warning against incapability, but notes that Abd al-Rahman's actual firmness and the people's agreement with him disprove any inability. The passage concludes by dismissing those who would interpret Umar's words as anything other than warnings, calling such interpretations far-fetched and negligent.

Misconception & Correction

Checkpoint
How does Baqillani defend Sa'd against the report that Umar called him a hunter?
A) By denying the report
B) By saying Sa'd was not a hunter
C) By interpreting it as a warning and citing Umar's appointment of Sa'd
D) By claiming the report is weak

Key Takeaway
Umar's descriptions of Sa'd and Ali are warnings against potential neglect, not condemnations, and Umar's actions affirm their competence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a criticism of someone you respect, do you instinctively assume the worst or do you seek a charitable interpretation? How can you apply Baqillani's method of reinterpreting apparent criticism as a warning in your own relationships?
?
Consider a time when you were warned about something you enjoy. Did you take it as a personal attack or as guidance to prioritize? What does this passage teach you about the difference between character assassination and loving guidance?
?
If someone's actions contradict their words, as Umar's appointments contradict a surface reading of his statements, how should you weigh them? Are you quick to dismiss someone based on a single statement, or do you look at the full picture of their deeds? Commit to judging others as Baqillani judged Umar.

Abd al-Rahman's Defense and Final Conclusion
Baqillani defends Abd al-Rahman and concludes his refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani interprets Umar's remark about Abd al-Rahman as a warning against incapability and concludes that those who take Umar's words literally are mistaken.

Core Idea
Umar's words about Abd al-Rahman are warnings; literal interpretation is a grave error.

Baqillani addresses the report that Umar questioned Abd al-Rahman's lineage (Zuhra) relative to leadership. He argues it is a warning against incapability, and that Abd al-Rahman's firmness and the people's agreement disprove any deficiency. He concludes by condemning those who misinterpret Umar's words as negligence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about Abd al-Rahman
Notice how Baqillani interprets Umar's question as a warning, and highlights Abd al-Rahman's actual firmness.
2
Read the concluding remarks
Understand Baqillani's final condemnation of those who misinterpret Umar's words.
He calls such interpretation 'far-fetched' and 'negligent'.
3
Reflect on the overall pattern
Notice that all defenses follow the same method: reinterpret as warning, cite evidence of Umar's trust.

فوجب دفعها واطراحُها . المناقصات وكيف يجوز أن يُظنَّ بعُمَرَ في فضله وتيقظه وصرامته وثاقب رأيه وعلمه بمواقع الخطاب وأحوال الكلام وموارد الأمور ومصادرها أن يناقض بمثل هذه في كلامه وهو من أعلمهم بضبط الصحابة وتحصيلهم واستدراكهم للدقيق اللطيف فضلاً المناقضة الظاهرة وإن كان قاصداً بهذا الكلام القدح عن في فضلهم؟ وكيف لم يعرف أن القوم يعلمون بأن الكثير البطالة والدعابة لا يحمل الناس على المحجة البيضاء والطريق المستقيم وأن حملهم على هذا المنهاج ضد البطالة والدعابة ونقيضها؟ فلو لم نعلم ضرورة بالروايات المعارضة لهذه الأخبار الواردة عنه في تقريظهم وتعظيمهم، لوجب أن يُنفى مثل هذه المناقضات فكيف والأمر بخلاف ذلك؟ وكيف يجوز أن يقبل مثل هذا في طلحة ما روي عن النبي صلّى الله عليه وسلم من تفضيله مع له وقوله : «هذا كله الطلحة» ولولا أنه قال حس، لطار الملائكة، وقوله للصحابة وقد أحدقوا به لأخذ دِرْعِه وحط السلاح عنه : عليكم بطلحة، في أمثال لهذه الأخبار معلومة ثابتة؟ ويكون قاصداً بقوله للزبير ما قاله للتحذير له من التشدد والمضايقة ولم يصفه بالبخل في نفسه؛ لأن الإنسان قد يكون أسخى من الريح الهَبُوبِ مع تشدده ومضايقته في المعاملة. وعلى أنه لم يَقُلْ فيه إنه قد فعل ذلك أو يفعله، وإنما قال: «لألفي فاعلا على مذهب التحذير. وعلى ذلك تأويل قوله إنه «ضرس شرس». وأما قوله : «يوماً شيطان ويوماً إنسان»، وإنه «مؤمنُ الرّضا كافر الغضب»، فإنه أيضاً يصف فيه لين أخلاقه تارة وحسن رضاً أو شدة غضبه تارة وتعسُّفه والتحذير له من ذلك إن ولى الأمر. وكذلك قوله في سعد إنه صاحب قنص وقوس وسهام» وإنه «صاحب مقنب من مقانبهم، وليس بصاحب الجسيم من أمرهم إنه خرج مخرج التحذير له من أن يكون بهذه الصفة إن ولى الأمر والدعاء له إلى ترك الاشتغال بذلك أحياناً والانتصاب إلى النظر في مصالح الأمة وكيف يكون هذا الخبر صحيحاً وهو يستكفيه ويُؤَمِّرُه على الأقاليم ويقول عند موته: «أوصي الخليفة من بعدي أن يُوَلِّي سعداً ؛ فإني لم أصرفه عن خيانة ولا موجدةٍ». وكذلك قوله في عليّ وأنه لكثير البطالة والدعابة، لو صحت هذه الرواية أيضاً، إنما المراد به النهي والتحذير والدعاء إلى ترك المزح في بعض الأوقات وهذا كله لا يوجبُ الفجور وإسقاط العدالة وإخراج من له هذه الأوصاف أو شيء منها عن استحقاق الإمامة . وأما قوله في عبد الرحمن: وما زُهرةُ وهذا الأمر!» إنما هو على مذهب التحذير من العجز إن صح ولقد ظهر من صرامة عبد الرحمن وشدته وجمع القوم للنظر في هذا الأمر معه شاكاً سلاحه ما يدل على نفي العجز عنه وبُعدُهُ منه وهذا مع اجتماع القوم على الرضا به والاعتماد على رأيه ومع ما عُلم من زهده فيه وإخراجه نفسه عنه مع صلاحه له وتمكنه من القيام به. فمن ظن أن عمر أراد غير ما ذكرناه إن صح الحديث فقد ظن بعيداً قدر أنا نترك الظاهر المعلوم من إعظام عمر لهم وحُسنِ ثنائه عليهم إلى هذه الروايات فقد ظن عجزاً وتفريطاً عظيماً واعتقد شططاً .
It is necessary to reject and discard them. The contradictions: How can it be supposed of Umar, with his virtue, alertness, firmness, piercing insight, knowledge of the places of address, conditions of speech, and the sources and origins of matters, that he would contradict himself with such things in his speech, while he is among the most knowledgeable of them in the precision of the Companions, their acquisition (of knowledge), and their grasping of subtle and fine points, let alone an apparent contradiction? Even if he intended by this speech to disparage their virtue? And how did he not know that the people know that one who is much given to frivolity and jesting does not lead people on the white path and the straight way, and that leading them on this path is the opposite of frivolity and jesting? If we did not know necessarily the narrations that oppose these reports reported from him in praise and exaltation of them, it would be necessary to deny such contradictions – how then when the matter is contrary to that? And how can such (reports) be accepted regarding Talha, given what has been narrated from the Prophet, peace be upon him, regarding his preference for him and his saying: 'This is all Talha,' and 'If it were not for what he said, the angels would have flown,' and his saying to the Companions when they surrounded him to take his armor and remove his weapons: 'Upon you is Talha,' among similar well-known and established reports? And his saying regarding al-Zubair what he said was for the purpose of warning him against severity and tightness, and he did not describe him as miserly in himself, because a man may be more generous than the blowing wind with his severity and tightness in transactions. Moreover, he did not say about him that he had done that or would do it; rather he said: 'I will find a doer' in the manner of warning. And on that is the interpretation of his saying that he is 'a rough rock'. As for his saying: 'One day a devil, one day a human,' and that he is 'a believer in satisfaction, disbeliever in anger,' he is also describing in him the softness of his character sometimes and good satisfaction, or the severity of his anger sometimes and his harshness, and warning him against that if he were to assume authority. Similarly, his saying regarding Sa'd that he is 'a master of hunting, bow, and arrows' and that he is 'a master of a squadron among their squadrons, and not a master of the great matter of their affair' was issued as a warning to him against being of this description if he were to assume authority, and a call to him to abandon preoccupation with that sometimes and to devote himself to considering the interests of the nation. And how can this report be authentic while he (Umar) deemed him sufficient and appointed him over regions and said at his death: 'I advise the Caliph after me to appoint Sa'd; for I did not dismiss him due to betrayal or resentment'? Similarly, his saying regarding Ali, that he is much given to frivolity and jesting, even if this narration were authentic, its meaning is prohibition, warning, and a call to abandon jesting at some times. And all of this does not require wickedness, dropping of uprightness, or removing one who has these descriptions or some of them from deserving the imamate. As for his saying regarding Abd al-Rahman: 'What is Zuhra and this matter!' it is in the manner of warning against incapability, if it is authentic. And indeed the firmness of Abd al-Rahman, his severity, and the people gathering to consider this matter with him while armed has appeared, indicating the negation of incapability from him and his distance from it. And this, with the people's agreement to be satisfied with him and reliance on his opinion, and with what is known of his asceticism regarding it and his removing himself from it despite his suitability for it and his ability to undertake it. Whoever thinks that Umar intended other than what we have mentioned, if the report is authentic, has thought far off. If we leave the apparent known from Umar's veneration of them and his good praise of them for these reports, he would have thought incapability and great negligence and believed an extreme thing.
Source pages p. 516

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of accusations against Umar and other Companions. Baqillani begins by stating that such accusations must be rejected. He asks how it is possible to suppose that Umar, given his intelligence and knowledge, would contradict himself in his speech. He then argues that if Umar had truly intended to disparage the Companions, it would conflict with his own actions in leading them on the right path. Baqillani invokes the well-known praise that Umar expressed for them, which contradicts any negative reports. He then addresses specific charges against Talha, Zubair, Sa'd, Ali, and Abd al-Rahman individually. For Talha, he cites the Prophet's praise to establish his high status, implying that Umar's statements could not be negative. For Zubair, he explains that Umar's remark about finding him 'a doer' was a warning against severity, not a description of miserliness. He further interprets Umar's description of Zubair as 'a rough rock' and his statements about him being 'one day a devil, one day a human' as references to his character fluctuations, but still as warnings. For Sa'd, Baqillani notes that Umar's description of him as a hunter was a warning against neglecting duties, and points out that Umar himself appointed Sa'd and recommended him as caliph. For Ali, he argues that even if the report of his frivolity is authentic, it was a call to avoid jesting at times, not a negation of his uprightness. Finally, for Abd al-Rahman, Baqillani interprets Umar's question 'What is Zuhra and this matter?' as a warning against incapability, but notes that Abd al-Rahman's actual firmness and the people's agreement with him disprove any inability. The passage concludes by dismissing those who would interpret Umar's words as anything other than warnings, calling such interpretations far-fetched and negligent.

تحذير
عجز
صرامة
زهد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Umar considered Abd al-Rahman unfit for leadership due to his lineage.
Correction: Baqillani shows it was a warning against potential incapability, but Abd al-Rahman's actions proved his capability.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what does Umar's question 'What is Zuhra and this matter!' indicate?
A) Umar's rejection of Abd al-Rahman's lineage
B) A warning against incapability
C) Umar's doubt about Abd al-Rahman's ability
D) A literal criticism

Key Takeaway
Umar's remark about Abd al-Rahman is a warning, and ignoring the broader context of Umar's praise leads to a grave misunderstanding.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever judged someone’s character based on a single comment, without examining their full actions and the context? How does this lesson’s emphasis on gathering evidence challenge you to be more fair in your judgments?
?
What personal attachments or ambitions do you cling to that, like the desire for power, may cloud your interpretation of others’ intentions? Would you be willing to step back, as Abd al-Rahman did, if you were capable but saw a greater good?
?
When you read historical accounts of the Companions, do you tend to assume the worst or the best about them? How can you actively adopt Baqillani’s method of defending their honor by looking for context and evidence before concluding?

The Evidence for Abd al-Rahman's Appointment of Uthman
Baqillani presents evidence for the validity of Abd al-Rahman's appointment of Uthman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational and historical basis for the legitimacy of Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf's appointment of Uthman as caliph, as argued by Imam al-Baqillani.

Core Idea
The Companions' consultation and consensus prove Abd al-Rahman's appointment of Uthman was valid.

In this passage, Imam al-Baqillani addresses a key historical objection regarding the succession of Uthman. He does not rely on mere narration but constructs a rational proof based on the observable conduct of the Companions. The argument centers on their deliberate consultation, their acceptance of Abd al-Rahman as an arbiter, and the necessary knowledge that their agreement constitutes a valid contract. This lesson unpacks that proof step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Familiarize yourself with the Arabic text and its literal meaning. Notice the structure: heading, objection, response, supporting report.
The Arabic has 'وأن الباقين' which is incomplete but contextually understood as 'and that the rest agreed'.
2
Identify the objection and response
Find the hypothetical question and the direct answer. This frames the entire proof.
3
Examine the evidence: consultation and consensus
Understand why the Companions' nights of deliberation and their satisfaction with Abd al-Rahman as a trustee are considered strong evidence. Note the term 'darura' (necessary knowledge).
Necessary knowledge means the fact is so obvious it cannot be denied.
4
Consider the additional support from Umar's statement
See how Umar's words about Sa'd reinforce the legitimacy of the consultative process and underscore the trustworthiness of the participants.
Umar's statement shows that even though he did not appoint Sa'd as caliph, he held him in high esteem, validating the process.
5
Reflect on the concept of 'darura'
Grasp how Baqillani claims that the validity of the appointment is known necessarily through the consensus and observable actions of the Companions.
This is a key method in kalam: using necessary knowledge from historical consensus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ذكر الدلالة على صحة عقد عبد الرحمن لعثمان بن عفان رضي الله عنهما فإن قال قائل : ما الدليل على صحة عقد عبد الرحمن لعثمان؟ قيل له : الدليل على ذلك أنهم تشاوروا ليالي وأياماً ونظروا في أمرهم ورضوا بعبد الرحمن أميناً ومشيراً فى هذا الباب وعلمنا ضرورة أنه عقد لعثمان وأن الباقين وقد قال عمر يوم أمر بالشورى وأن تولوا سعداً فأهلها هو وإلا فليستعن به الوالي فإني لم أعزله عن خيانة ولا ضعف .
Section mentioning the evidence for the validity of the contract of Abd al-Rahman for Uthman ibn Affan, may Allah be pleased with them both. If someone says: What is the evidence for the validity of the contract of Abd al-Rahman for Uthman? It is said to him: The evidence for that is that they consulted for nights and days and considered their affair and were satisfied with Abd al-Rahman as a trustee and advisor in this matter, and we know necessarily that he contracted for Uthman and that the rest (agreed). And Umar said on the day he ordered the consultation: 'If you appoint Sa'd, then he is its people; otherwise, let the ruler seek help from him, for I did not dismiss him due to betrayal or weakness.'
Source pages p. 517

Commentary
This passage is a proof of the validity of Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf's appointment of Uthman ibn Affan as caliph. Baqillani presents it as a section (باب) dedicated to this evidence. He begins by posing an objection: 'What is the evidence for the validity of Abd al-Rahman's contract for Uthman?' This is a hypothetical question from a doubter. The answer is given: the Companions deliberated for several nights and days, examined their situation, and accepted Abd al-Rahman as a trustworthy advisor in this matter. We know with necessary knowledge (ضرورة) that he appointed Uthman and that the remaining Companions agreed. Baqillani then adds support from Umar's statement during the consultation: Umar advised that if they appoint Sa'd, then he is fit; otherwise, the ruler should seek his help, as Umar did not dismiss him due to betrayal or weakness. This indicates Umar's trust in Sa'd and underscores the legitimacy of the consultative process. The argument is that the consensus of the Companions and their reliance on Abd al-Rahman's judgment confirm the validity of the appointment.

Key Terms
عقد
شورى
ضرورة
أمين
مشير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Abd al-Rahman's appointment of Uthman was arbitrary or lacked consensus.
Correction: Baqillani shows it was based on extensive consultation and agreement of the Companions, known necessarily.

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence for the validity of Abd al-Rahman's appointment of Uthman according to Baqillani?
A) Uthman's own claim to the caliphate
B) The Companions' consultation and agreement with Abd al-Rahman
C) A direct revelation from Allah
D) Umar's appointment of Abd al-Rahman as caliph

Key Takeaway
The legitimacy of Uthman's caliphate rests on the Companions' deliberate consultation and consensus, which provides certain knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Companions spent nights and days in consultation before making their decision. When was the last time you gave that level of time and care to a major decision in your life? What would change if you did? Will you commit to slowing down and seeking counsel before your next important choice?
?
Umar trusted Sa'd despite having dismissed him, showing that disagreement does not destroy respect. Who in your life have you disagreed with deeply, yet still need to rely on? How can you rebuild trust with them starting today?
?
The passage says 'we know necessarily' that the contract was made—a certainty based on the Companions' consensus. Is your conviction in the legitimacy of the caliphs that certain? If not, what is the source of your doubt, and how will you seek the knowledge to remove it?

Defense of Umar's Statements about Companions
Author defends Umar's praise and criticism of Sa'd, Ali, and Abd al-Rahman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how apparent criticisms of the Companions by Umar can be reconciled with their integrity and qualification for leadership in Sunni theology.

Core Idea
Umar's statements about the Companions are not criticisms but contextual warnings or praise.

In this passage, Imam Baqillani addresses reports that might suggest Umar ibn al-Khattab criticized some of the leading Companions. Such reports could be used by sectarian groups to undermine their status. Baqillani shows that these statements, even if authentic, are either expressions of praise, warnings against specific behaviors, or misconstrued. His defense reinforces the Sunni doctrine of the Companions' collective integrity and suitability for leadership.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Context
Recognize that this passage defends Umar's statements about three major Companions against the charge that they imply fault.
The author is countering potential sectarian arguments that use these reports to question the Companions' integrity.
2
Examine Each Case
Go through the cases of Sa'd, Ali, and Abd al-Rahman individually. Notice how Baqillani interprets each statement by Umar.
For Sa'd, Umar praises him even after dismissing him. For Ali, jesting is a warning, not a moral flaw. For Abd al-Rahman, Umar's remark cautions against incapacity, but Abd al-Rahman's actions prove otherwise.
3
Identify the Underlying Principle
Understand that apparent criticisms do not negate a person's integrity or worthiness for the imamate.
The author argues that Umar's statements do not imply immorality or disqualification.
4
Assess the Conclusion
Baqillani concludes that those who believe Umar intended criticism rather than praise are making a grave error, ignoring the clear evidence of Umar's veneration.
This reinforces the Sunni position that the Companions are all upright and qualified for leadership.

بذلك أحياناً والانتصاب إلى النظر في مصالح الأمة وكيف يكون هذا الخبر صحيحاً وهو يستكفيه ويُؤَمِّرُه على الأقاليم ويقول عند موته: «أوصي الخليفة من بعدي أن يُوَلِّي سعداً ؛ فإني لم أصرفه عن خيانة ولا موجدةٍ» (١) . وكذلك قوله في عليّ وأنه لكثير البطالة والدعابة، لو صحت هذه الرواية أيضاً، إنما المراد به النهي والتحذير والدعاء إلى ترك المزح في بعض الأوقات وهذا كله لا يوجبُ الفجور وإسقاط العدالة وإخراج من له هذه الأوصاف أو شيء منها عن استحقاق الإمامة . وأما قوله في عبد الرحمن: وما زُهرةُ وهذا الأمر!» إنما هو على مذهب التحذير من العجز إن صح ولقد ظهر من صرامة عبد الرحمن وشدته وجمع القوم للنظر في هذا الأمر معه شاكاً سلاحه ما يدل على نفي العجز عنه وبُعدُهُ منه وهذا مع اجتماع القوم على الرضا به والاعتماد على رأيه ومع ما عُلم من زهده فيه وإخراجه نفسه عنه مع صلاحه له وتمكنه من القيام به. فمن ظن أن عمر أراد غير ما ذكرناه إن صح الحديث فقد ظن بعيداً قدر أنا نترك الظاهر المعلوم من إعظام عمر لهم وحُسنِ ثنائه عليهم إلى هذه الروايات فقد ظن عجزاً وتفريطاً عظيماً واعتقد شططاً .
by that sometimes and standing up to consider the interests of the community, and how can this report be true while he appoints him and makes him governor over provinces and says at his death: 'I advise the caliph after me to appoint Sa'd, for I did not remove him due to betrayal or anger.' (1) Likewise his statement about Ali, that he was given to much idleness and jesting; if this narration is also authentic, it is only meant as prohibition, warning, and a call to abandon jesting at certain times. All this does not necessitate immorality, nullification of integrity (adala), or exclusion of one possessing these descriptions or any of them from deserving the imamate. As for his statement about Abd al-Rahman: 'What flower and this matter!' it is only on the basis of warning against incapacity, if authentic. Indeed, the severity and firmness of Abd al-Rahman, and his gathering the people to deliberate on this matter with him, armed with his weapon, indicates the negation of incapacity from him and its distance from him. This, along with the people's consensus of approval for him and reliance on his opinion, and what is known of his asceticism (zuhd) regarding it and his exclusion of himself from it despite his suitability for it and capability of undertaking it. Whoever thinks that Umar intended other than what we have mentioned, if the hadith is authentic, has indeed thought a far-fetched thing; if we abandon the apparent known fact of Umar's veneration for them and his good praise of them in favor of these narrations, then he has thought of great incapacity and negligence and adopted an extreme view.
Source pages p. 517

Commentary
This passage is a defense of statements attributed to Umar ibn al-Khattab regarding certain companions (Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, Ali ibn Abi Talib, and Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf) which might be taken as criticisms affecting their suitability for leadership. The author begins by addressing a report where Umar praises Sa'd despite dismissing him earlier, explaining that Umar's statement confirms Sa'd's integrity. Then he addresses a report about Ali being 'given to idleness and jesting'; even if authentic, it is interpreted as a warning against excessive jesting, not as a charge of immorality that would disqualify him from the imamate. Regarding Abd al-Rahman, a report has Umar asking 'What flower and this matter?' — this is taken as a warning against weakness, but Abd al-Rahman's later actions (his firmness, the community's trust, his asceticism in declining the caliphate despite being qualified) prove he is far from incapacity. The author concludes that anyone who assumes Umar intended criticism instead of praise based on such reports is making a grave error, abandoning clear evidence of Umar's esteem for these companions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Umar's statements necessarily imply these companions were unfit for leadership.
Correction: Umar's words are either praise, warnings against specific behaviors, or misconstrued; they do not undermine the companions' integrity or worthiness for the imamate.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the correct interpretation of Umar's statement about Ali's idleness and jesting?
A) It proves Ali was unqualified for the imamate.
B) It is a warning against excessive jesting at certain times.
C) It shows Umar disliked Ali.
D) It is fabricated and should be rejected.

Key Takeaway
Umar's reported statements about Sa'd, Ali, and Abd al-Rahman do not undermine their integrity or qualification for the caliphate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The author argues that clear evidence of Umar's veneration must override ambiguous reports. In your own relationships, are there times when you have allowed a single negative comment to overshadow years of known goodness? How can you correct this pattern starting today?
?
If a companion's integrity could be questioned based on a few statements, how much more careful must we be with the honor of believers? What step can you take this week to defend the reputation of someone you know, even when it is easier to remain silent or assume the worst?

Proof of Validity of Abd al-Rahman's Appointment of Uthman
Author provides a proof based on consensus and compliance for Abd al-Rahman's contract for Uthman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Baqillani argues for the validity of Abd al-Rahman's contract for Uthman using consensus, necessity, and the qualifications of the parties involved.

Core Idea
The validity of a caliph's appointment is proven by community consensus and the integrity of the process, not by isolated reports.

Imam Baqillani presents a cumulative proof for the legitimacy of the historical process that led to Uthman's caliphate. He anticipates a hypothetical question and builds his case from observable facts: the shura committee's deliberation, its unanimous trust in Abd al-Rahman, and the community's subsequent compliance. This lesson unpacks that evidence and shows why later conflicting narrations are dismissed.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then the English translation. Let the structure of the argument emerge naturally.
2
Identify the main elements of the proof
Look for the hypothetical question and the answer. The answer contains several points: consultation, necessity, qualifications of Uthman, qualifications of Abd al-Rahman, and dismissal of opposing reports.
This is the logical skeleton of the passage.
3
Understand the concept of 'necessity' (darura)
Baqillani claims that we know 'necessarily' that Abd al-Rahman contracted for Uthman. Reflect on why he uses this strong term—because the community's compliance is undeniable.
This is a key epistemological claim.
4
Appreciate the role of ahl al-hall wa al-aqd
Abd al-Rahman is described as being among the 'people of loosening and binding', the elite qualified to choose a leader. This establishes his authority.
5
Understand why conflicting narrations are rejected
The author dismisses any narrations that contradict the clear evidence of consensus and conduct as null. Note how he prioritizes observable, mass-transmitted facts over isolated reports.
This is a methodological point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن باب ذكر الدلالة على صحة عقد عبد الرحمن لعثمان بن عفان رضي الله عنهما فإن قال قائل : ما الدليل على صحة عقد عبد الرحمن العثمان؟ قيل له : الدليل على ذلك أنهم تشاوروا ليالي وأياماً ونظروا في أمرهم ورضوا بعبد الرحمن أميناً ومشيراً فى هذا الباب وعلمنا ضرورة أنه عقد لعثمان وأن الباقين منهم ومن سائر الأمة انقادوا لعثمان وخاطبوه بأمير المؤمنين، وعثمان بصفة من يصلح العقد له والعهد إليه وعبد الرحمن في فضله ونبله وسابقته وعلمه وما لا حاجة لنا إلى الإطالة في ذكره من فضائله ممن يصلح لعقد هذا الأمر بل هو من جلَّةِ أهل الحل والعقد. وقد ظهر من تبرئه منها وزهده فيها مع كونه مرضيّاً عندهم وعند سائر الأمة ما يدل على قوة إيمانه وشدة خوفه وحذره وعظيم مناصحته للأمة فهو أبعد الناس من التهمة في هذا الباب وأشدهم إيثاراً وتوخياً لأداء الأمانة وحسن النظر للأمة هذا معلوم من حاله وفعله وما بعد ذلك من الروايات التي لا تليق بما وصفناه ملغاة مطرحة .
And from the chapter on mentioning the evidence for the validity of Abd al-Rahman's contract for Uthman ibn Affan (may Allah be pleased with them both): If someone says: What is the proof for the validity of Abd al-Rahman's contract for Uthman? It is said to him: The proof for that is that they consulted for nights and days and considered their affair, and they were pleased with Abd al-Rahman as a trustee and advisor in this matter, and we know necessarily that he contracted for Uthman, and that the rest of them and the rest of the community submitted to Uthman and addressed him as Commander of the Faithful (Amir al-Mu'minin). And Uthman has the description of one suitable for the contract and the covenant to him, and Abd al-Rahman, in his virtue, nobility, precedence, and knowledge—and we have no need to prolong mentioning his merits—is among those suitable for contracting this matter; indeed he is from the great ones of the people of loosening and binding (ahl al-hall wa al-'aqd). And it has appeared from his exoneration from it (the caliphate) and his asceticism in it, along with being approved by them and the rest of the community, what indicates the strength of his faith, intensity of his fear and caution, and greatness of his sincere counsel to the community. So he is the furthest of people from suspicion in this matter and the most preferring and cautious in fulfilling the trust and good consideration for the community. This is known from his state and action, and whatever narrations after that which do not befit what we have described are null and discarded.
Source pages p. 517

Commentary
This passage is a proof (dalil) for the validity of Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf's appointment of Uthman as caliph. The chapter heading explicitly states the topic. The author presents a hypothetical question: 'What is the proof?' The answer is based on multiple circumstantial evidences: (1) The shura committee (the six chosen by Umar) deliberated at length and unanimously agreed to make Abd al-Rahman the arbiter. (2) We know by necessity (darura) that Abd al-Rahman formally contracted allegiance to Uthman, because the other members and the wider community submitted to Uthman and addressed him as Commander of the Faithful. (3) Uthman was qualified for the office. (4) Abd al-Rahman himself was eminently qualified—by virtue, nobility, precedence, knowledge—as one of the 'people of loosening and binding' (ahl al-hall wa al-'aqd), i.e., the elite who decide leadership. Moreover, Abd al-Rahman's own conduct—his refusal of the caliphate despite being eligible, his asceticism, the community's trust in him—shows his integrity and sincerity. Therefore, any narrations that contradict this clear picture are rejected as null. The argument is cumulative: observable consensus, qualifications, and moral character all support the validity.

Key Terms
عقد
الشورى
أهل الحل والعقد
ضرورة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the proof for Uthman's caliphate depends on a single narration.
Correction: Baqillani shows it is based on observable consensus, necessity, and character, not on a single report.

Checkpoint
What is the main proof the author provides for the validity of Abd al-Rahman's contract?
A) A single hadith from Umar.
B) The fact that the shura committee chose Abd al-Rahman, and then the entire community accepted Uthman.
C) That Abd al-Rahman was forced by the committee.
D) That Uthman had a direct designation from the Prophet.

Key Takeaway
The appointment of Uthman by Abd al-Rahman is validated by the consensus of the shura committee, the community's compliance, and the qualifications and integrity of both men.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that the entire community submitted to Uthman and addressed him as Amir al-Mu'minin, what doubts arise in your heart about the justice of that process? Can you honestly trace those doubts back to a lack of trust in Allah's wisdom in guiding the sahaba? Commit to replacing speculation with acceptance of the clear consensus.
?
Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf proved his integrity by refusing the caliphate despite being qualified. Where in your life are you clinging to a position or authority out of desire, rather than stepping aside for the greater good of the community? What would it take for you to emulate his detachment?

Refuting the Claim that Ali Criticized Uthman's Appointment
Baqillani refutes a report of Ali's criticism by dismissing it and presenting authentic evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Baqillani refutes the objection that Ali ibn Abi Talib criticized Uthman's appointment by dismissing unreliable reports and citing consistent evidence from Ali's actions and reliable narrations.

Core Idea
What appears contradictory is often resolved by checking the reliability of reports and the weight of established facts.

Objectors sometimes cite isolated reports to challenge the legitimacy of the early caliphs. In this passage, Imam al-Baqillani addresses the claim that Ali disapproved of Uthman's appointment. He shows that such reports are baseless whispers and that the known facts and reliable traditions confirm Ali's acceptance.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the structure: the objection is raised, then immediately dismissed with strong language.
The objection is phrased as a rhetorical question: 'Was it not narrated...'
2
Understand the author's critique
Baqillani dismisses the report as 'wasawis and hadith al-nafs' (whispers and self-talk). Observe that he does not engage with its content but calls it baseless.
He also rejects Shia claims of ignorance or taqiyya as false and unknowable.
3
Examine the positive evidence
Baqillani presents an authentic narration where Ali advises to proceed with Uthman's pledge. Notice how this aligns with Ali's known allegiance and cooperation.
This narration is presented as more consistent with Ali's character.
4
Reflect on the methodology
Consider the principle: established facts (like Ali's public actions) cannot be set aside by weak reports. Reliable narrations outweigh isolated ones.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا : أفليس قد روي أن علياً قال لعبد الرحمن لما عقد لعثمان : «أغَدْرُ هذا يا عبد الرحمن؟» وأنكر ما كان منه؟ قيل لهم : هذا من الوساوس وحديث النفس لأن المعلوم الذي لا شك فيه مبايعة علي لعثمان وتصرفه معه وإقامته الحدود بين يديه حتى قال كثير من الشيعة : إنهم جهلُوا الحد فقام يعلمهم ؛ وقال آخرون : إنه كان في تقيةٍ منهم وهذا كله باطل لا سبيل إلى علمه ؛ فلا يجوز ترك هذا الظاهر بمثل هذه الروايات هذا لو لم يعارضها من رواية أهل الثبتِ والثقات ما يطابق الظاهر من فعل عليّ وانقياده فكيف وقد ورد ذلك بما لا قبل لأحد بدفعه وذلك أن الصحيح في هذا ما رُوي أن علياً عليه السلام قال لعبد الرحمن بن عوف بعد أن عرض عليه البيعة على شرط ما رُوي عنه أنه شرطه فأباه عليّ والتزمه عثمان، فقال له علي عليه السلام : أخاك، فقد أعطى الرضا من نفسه واستخر بالله واصفق على يده ؛ وهذا أشبه بقول علي وفعله .
For if they say: Was it not narrated that Ali said to Abd al-Rahman when he contracted for Uthman: 'Is this treachery, O Abd al-Rahman?' and he disapproved of what he did? It is said to them: This is from whisperings (wasawis) and self-talk (hadith al-nafs), because what is known without doubt is that Ali gave allegiance to Uthman, acted alongside him, and carried out the prescribed punishments (hudud) under his authority, to the extent that many of the Shia said: 'They were ignorant of the [ruling of the] hadd punishment, so he stood to teach them,' and others said: 'He was in taqiyya (dissimulation) towards them.' All this is false; there is no way to know it. So it is not permissible to abandon this apparent [evidence] with such narrations, even if there were no opposing narrations from reliable and trustworthy people that match the apparent [evidence] of Ali's action and submission. How then, when such [reliable] narrations have come that cannot be rejected by anyone? That is, what is authentic in this matter is what is narrated that Ali, peace be upon him, said to Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf after he offered him the pledge of allegiance on the condition that is narrated he stipulated, and Ali refused it and Uthman accepted it, then Ali said to him: 'Your brother, for he has given satisfaction from himself; so seek Allah's guidance and strike his hand.' And this is more similar to Ali's word and action.
Source pages p. 518

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer (qala qa'il) structure. The objectors claim that Ali ibn Abi Talib said to Abd al-Rahman after the latter appointed Uthman: 'Is this treachery?' and disapproved. The author responds by dismissing this report as 'wasawis and hadith al-nafs' (whispers and self-talk), i.e., baseless internal thoughts or rumors. The known fact (al-ma'lum) is that Ali did pledge allegiance to Uthman, cooperated with him, and even administered hudud punishments. Some Shia tried to explain this by claiming ignorance or taqiyya, but the author rejects those explanations as unknowable and false. Furthermore, there are authentic narrations from reliable sources that confirm Ali's acceptance. The author cites one such narration: when Abd al-Rahman offered Ali the caliphate on certain conditions, Ali refused, and Uthman accepted. Then Ali told Abd al-Rahman: 'Your brother (Uthman) has given satisfaction; so seek Allah's help and strike his hand' (i.e., conclude the pledge). This is more consistent with Ali's known character and actions.

Key Terms
وساوس
حديث النفس
تقية
أهل الثبت

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the report of Ali criticizing Uthman's appointment shows that Ali did not accept Uthman's caliphate, casting doubt on the legitimacy of the early caliphs.
Correction: The author argues that the report is unreliable (whispers and self-talk) and contradicts the well-known fact of Ali's allegiance and cooperation. Furthermore, authentic narrations confirm Ali's acceptance.

Checkpoint
How does the author refute the report that Ali said 'Is this treachery?' to Abd al-Rahman?
A) He accepts it but explains it away as a joke.
B) He dismisses it as baseless whispers and contrasts it with Ali's known allegiance and cooperation with Uthman.
C) He claims the report is fabricated by the Shia.
D) He says Ali later regretted it.

Key Takeaway
Authentic narrations and established facts take precedence over weak, contradictory reports.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a time when you entertained a rumor about someone you know, even though their consistent actions showed the opposite. How does Baqillani's dismissal of the weak report challenge you to base your judgments on established facts rather than whispers? Will you commit today to verifying any harmful report before acting on it?
?
Have you ever used a convenient excuse (like 'I had no choice' or 'I was just pretending') to justify a contradiction between your beliefs and your actions? This lesson rejects taqiyya as an explanation for Ali's cooperation. What does this teach you about the importance of integrity between your inner convictions and outward behavior?
?
The author says 'there is no way to know' the Shia claims about Ali's hidden disapproval. Is there a person you have assumed bad intentions for, without certain knowledge? How can you apply the principle of taking apparent good actions at face value, even when whispers suggest otherwise?
